Leaving Parts of Tawaf al-Sadr
Ruling on expiation for leaving circuits of Tawaf al-Sadr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the expiation for leaving three or fewer circuits of Tawaf al-Sadr and for leaving four or more circuits.

Core Idea
Leaving up to three circuits of Tawaf al-Sadr requires sadaqah; four or more requires a sheep.

This passage from al-Quduri provides a clear ruling on the expiation for omitting parts of Tawaf al-Sadr, the farewell Tawaf. Unlike Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the consequences are lighter, but still obligatory. Understanding this distinction is essential for any pilgrim or student of Hajj fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its status
Recognize that Tawaf al-Sadr is a wajib act in Hajj. Omitting parts of it requires expiation.
Tawaf al-Sadr is also known as Tawaf al-Wada'.
2
Note the thresholds
The passage distinguishes between leaving three or fewer circuits and leaving four or more circuits.
The total circuits of Tawaf are seven.
3
State the expiation for each threshold
For three or fewer: sadaqah (charity of half a sa' of wheat or equivalent). For four or more: a sheep.
Sadaqah here is a specific measure in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Compare with Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Note that this expiation is lighter than for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, reflecting the lesser importance of Tawaf al-Sadr.
This distinction helps in memorizing the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ تَرَكَ ثَلَاثَةَ أَشْوَاطِ مِنْ طَوَافِ الصَّدَرِ فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ مِنْهُ أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ فَعَلَيْهِ شَاةٌ
And whoever leaves three circuits of Tawaf al-Sadr, upon him is sadaqah (charity), and if he leaves from it four circuits, upon him is a sheep.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for Tawaf al-Sadr (the farewell Tawaf). The expiation is lighter than for Tawaf al-Ziyarah: for three or fewer circuits, only sadaqah (which is half a sa' of wheat or similar, according to the Hanafi school) is required; for four or more, a sheep is required. Unlike Tawaf al-Ziyarah, there is no perpetual ihram here because Tawaf al-Sadr is less essential. No proof is cited in this passage, but the ruling is standard in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell Tawaf performed before leaving Makkah, also known as Tawaf al-Wada'.
صدقة (sadaqah): A charitable donation specified as half a sa' of wheat or equivalent in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required if a pilgrim leaves two circuits of Tawaf al-Sadr?
A) A sheep
B) Sadaqah
C) Remaining in ihram
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Tawaf al-Sadr, the expiation for leaving up to three circuits is sadaqah; for four or more, a sheep.

Leaving Sa'yi Between Safa and Marwah
Ruling on omission of Sa'yi with proof from a tabi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for leaving Sa'yi in Hajj, identify that it requires a dam but does not invalidate the Hajj, and explain the proof from the saying of al-Hasan al-Basri.

Core Idea
Sa'yi is wajib, not rukn; leaving it requires a dam but Hajj remains valid.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a common question: what happens if a pilgrim omits the Sa'yi between Safa and Marwah? The ruling may surprise you—the Hajj is still complete, but a sacrificial animal (dam) is required. We will examine the text and the evidence used to support this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The act is leaving the Sa'yi entirely. According to the text, the ruling is that a sacrifice (dam) is required and the Hajj is complete (tam).
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The author cites the saying of al-Hasan al-Basri (a tabi'i) regarding a man who cut through al-Hijr during Tawaf. Al-Hasan said he should repeat the Tawaf, and if he had already become halal and had intercourse, he should 'spill blood' (i.e., offer a sacrifice).
This is a qawl tabi'i, which is considered a proof in Hanafi usul when not contradicted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove the ruling? The analogy is: missing an obligatory part of Tawaf (cutting through al-Hijr, which is part of the Kaaba) requires a dam. By extension, missing the Sa'yi, which is also a wajib ritual, similarly requires a dam but does not invalidate the Hajj because Sa'yi is not a rukn.
The legal link is that both are obligatory acts; omission necessitates compensation (dam) but not total invalidation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Yes, the Shafi'i school holds that Sa'yi is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj. Therefore, omitting it would invalidate the Hajj entirely, requiring repetition of the entire pilgrimage.
This disagreement stems from different classifications of Sa'yi based on interpretation of Quranic and hadith evidence.
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
What is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school? Sa'yi is wajib, not rukn. Omission requires a dam, but the Hajj is valid and complete. This is the mufta bihi position.
The ruling is supported by the authority of al-Quduri and the Zahir al-Riwayah texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ تَرَكَ السَّعْيَ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَحَجُّهُ تَامٌ ۲۲ وجه (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَمَنْ تَرَكَ السَّعْيَ بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ \ عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، فِي رَجُلٍ طَافَ الطَّوَافَ الْوَاجِبَ، فَجَعَلَ يَجْتَازُ فِي الْحِجْرِ قَالَ: «يُعِيدُ الطَّوَافَ، فَإِنْ كَانَ حَلَّ وَغَشِيَ النِّسَاءَ أَهْرَقَ لِذَلِكَ دَمًا» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة فِي الرَّجُلِ يَطُوفُ بِالْبَيْتِ فَيَكُونُ مِنْ طَوَافِهِ دُخُولا في الحِجْرِ، نمبر: 13942)
And whoever leaves the Sa'yi between Safa and Marwah, upon him is a sacrifice (dam), and his Hajj is complete. 22 Evidence (1): The saying of a follower (tabi'i) as proof for 'Whoever leaves the Sa'yi between Safa and Marwah': from al-Hasan, regarding a man who performed the obligatory Tawaf but cut through al-Hijr (the area of the Kaaba), he said: 'He should repeat the Tawaf, and if he had become halal and had intercourse with women, he should spill blood for that.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Chapter on a man who performs Tawaf and from his Tawaf he enters al-Hijr, no. 13942)
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage rules that omitting Sa'yi entirely requires a sacrifice (dam), but unlike Tawaf al-Ziyarah, the Hajj is still valid (tam). So Sa'yi is not a rukn that invalidates Hajj if missed; it is wajib. The proof cited is the saying of al-Hasan al-Basri (a tabi'i) about cutting through al-Hijr during Tawaf, which is analogous: one who misses part of Tawaf must repeat it and if already halal, offer a sacrifice. The reasoning is that leaving Sa'yi is like leaving an obligatory part, requiring compensation but not invalidating the entire Hajj.

Key Terms
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal, typically a sheep or goat, required for certain omissions in Hajj.
سعي (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah seven times.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A pilgrim forgets to perform Sa'yi but already left Makkah. What is required?
A) His Hajj is invalid
B) He must sacrifice a dam and his Hajj is complete
C) He must return and perform Sa'yi without expiation
D) He must perform Umrah

Key Takeaway
Sa'yi is wajib in Hajj; omitting it requires a sacrificial animal (dam), but the Hajj remains valid and complete.

Leaving Arafah Before the Imam
Ruling on departing Arafah before the Imam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that departing Arafah before the Imam requires a sacrifice (dam), identify the two proofs cited (hadith of Jabir and saying of Ibn Abbas), and explain why the dam is classified as wajib.

Core Idea
Leaving Arafah before the Imam triggers a wajib dam for violating the proper time of standing.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in Hajj: what happens if a pilgrim departs from Arafah before the Imam (the leader of the pilgrims). The Hanafi school holds that such a pilgrim must offer a sacrifice (dam), but his Hajj remains valid. The passage from Al-Quduri presents the ruling and supports it with two pieces of evidence: the practice of the Prophet ﷺ during his Hajj and a general principle from Ibn Abbas on omissions in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is departing Arafah before the Imam. The ruling is that a dam (sacrifice) is obligatory upon the pilgrim.
The ruling applies regardless of whether the pilgrim stood at Arafah for a short or long time, as long as he left before the Imam.
2
Examine the first dalil — hadith of Jabir
The hadith describes the Prophet ﷺ standing at Arafah until sunset. This indicates the proper time for departure is after sunset. Leaving earlier violates the sunnah and requires compensation.
The hadith is sahih (Muslim, Abu Dawood). Its transmission is qat'i but its dalalah is zanni because it is an action, not an explicit command.
3
Examine the second dalil — saying of Ibn Abbas
Ibn Abbas said: 'Whoever forgets something of his rites or leaves it, let him spill blood.' Departing before the Imam is a leaving of the proper sunnah, thus requiring dam.
This is a qawl sahabi (companion's saying), which is a hujjah in Hanafi usul.
4
Synthesize the proof and identify the hukm level
Both proofs together establish that departing before the Imam is an omission requiring compensation. The dam is wajib (not fard) because the evidence is zanni al-dalalah.
The hukm level is wajib. The authority weight is zahir riwayah from Quduri.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ أَفَاضَ مِنْ عَرَفَاتٍ قَبْلَ الْإِمَامِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ ۲۳. وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ أَفَاضَ مِنْ عَرَفَاتٍ قَبْلَ الْإِمَامِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ \ دَخَلْنَا عَلَى جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللهِ، . . . فَلَمْ يَزَلْ وَاقِفًا حَتَّى غَرَبَتِ الشَّمْسُ، وَذَهَبَتِ الصُّفْرَةُ قَلِيلًا، حَتَّى غَابَ الْقُرْصُ، (مسلم: بَابُ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1218/ أبو داؤد: بَابُ صِفَةِ حَجَّةِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، نمبر: 1905) وجه : (۲) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَمَنْ أَفَاضَ مِنْ عَرَفَاتٍ قَبْلَ الْإِمَامِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمَاعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ: «مَنْ نَسِيَ شَيْئًا مِنْ نُسُكِهِ أَوْ تَرَكَهُ فَلْيُهْرِقْ دَمًا». سنن الدارقطني: كِتَاب الحج،: 2534)
And whoever departs from Arafat before the Imam, upon him is a sacrifice. 23 Evidence (1): The hadith as proof for 'Whoever departs from Arafat before the Imam': We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... and he remained standing until the sun set, and the yellowness went away a little, until the disk disappeared. (Muslim, Chapter on the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1218; Abu Dawood, Chapter on the description of the Prophet's Hajj, no. 1905) Evidence (2): The saying of a companion as proof: from Ibn Abbas that he said: 'Whoever forgets something of his rites or leaves it, let him spill blood.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Book of Hajj, no. 2534)
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage deals with leaving Arafah prematurely, before the Imam (leader of the pilgrims) departs. The Hanafi ruling is that such a pilgrim must offer a sacrifice (dam), but his stay at Arafah is still valid. The first evidence is from the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's Hajj: he stood until sunset, indicating that the proper time for departure is after sunset. The second evidence is the general principle from Ibn Abbas that any omission requires sacrifice. Together, they support the ruling that departing before the Imam is an omission requiring compensation.

Key Terms
الإمام (al-imam): The leader of the pilgrim caravan, often the caliph or appointed leader, whose departure signals the permitted time.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) offered as expiation for an omission in Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a pilgrim who departs Arafah before the Imam?
A) His Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) He must offer a sacrifice (dam).
C) He must fast three days.
D) Nothing; his Hajj is complete.

Key Takeaway
Departing Arafah before the Imam is an omission that requires a wajib dam, but the standing at Arafah remains valid.

Majority in Tawaf is Treated as the Whole
Usul principle: majority in Tawaf is treated as the whole

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the majority in Tawaf is treated as the whole to determine when Tawaf al-Ziyarah must be completed fully.

Core Idea
Leaving most of Tawaf is like leaving all of it — the pilgrim remains in ihram until all circuits are done.

In Hanafi fiqh, certain acts are evaluated by a 'majority rule': when most of an obligation is missed, it is considered as if the entire act was missed. This principle is applied to Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a key rite of Hajj. Understanding this rule clarifies why a pilgrim who leaves four or more circuits must complete all seven before leaving ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Tawaf al-Ziyarah is wajib in the Hanafi school. Its completion requires seven full circuits around the Ka'bah.
The act is obligatory, not merely sunnah.
2
Understand the principle: al-aksar yu'ta lahu hukm al-kull
The Hanafi legal maxim holds that the majority (aksar) of an obligation, when omitted, is treated as the whole (kull). This means leaving more than half of the required circuits is legally equivalent to leaving all of them.
This principle is specific to Hanafi fiqh and does not apply universally to all acts.
3
Apply to the specific case of Tawaf al-Ziyarah
Since Tawaf al-Ziyarah consists of seven circuits, the majority is four or more circuits. If a pilgrim leaves four, five, six, or seven circuits, it is as if he left the entire Tawaf.
Leaving three circuits (less than half) is not treated as leaving the whole; the pilgrim only needs to complete the remaining four.
4
Note the consequence
If the majority is left, the Tawaf is considered incomplete. The pilgrim must complete all seven circuits. Until then, he remains in ihram and cannot perform acts that require exiting ihram.
This consequence emphasizes the importance of completing the full number of circuits.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول : طواف میں اکثر پر کل کا حکم لگایا جائے گا، لہذا اگر طواف زیارت میں اکثر چھوڑ دیا تو کل ترک ہوا.
Principle: In Tawaf, the majority is given the ruling of the whole; therefore, if in Tawaf al-Ziyarah the majority is left, it is as if the whole was left.
Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This is a usul (legal principle) note that explains the reasoning behind the ruling on Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Since leaving four or more circuits (majority) is treated as leaving the entire Tawaf, the pilgrim remains in ihram indefinitely until he completes all seven circuits. This principle is applied to other acts as well: when the majority of an obligatory act is missed, it is considered as if the entire act was missed.

Key Terms
اکثر (aksar): Majority, more than half.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this usul principle, if a pilgrim leaves four circuits of Tawaf al-Ziyarah, how is it treated?
A) As leaving all seven
B) As leaving only four
C) As leaving three
D) Requires only sadaqah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that the majority is treated as the whole in Tawaf ensures that a pilgrim who leaves most of the circuits must complete all seven before exiting ihram.

Leaving the Standing at Muzdalifah: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling with two proofs (Quran and Hadith).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a pilgrim who misses the standing at Muzdalifah and explain the Quranic and hadith proofs that establish this obligation.

Core Idea
Leaving the standing at Muzdalifah requires a sacrifice (dam) — it is wajib, not optional.

The standing at Muzdalifah is a key component of Hajj in the Hanafi school. While some schools consider it a sunnah, the Hanafi school holds it to be wajib, and missing it necessitates a sacrifice. This lesson examines the ruling as stated in Al-Quduri and the two proofs cited: a Quranic verse and a Prophetic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'leaving the standing at Muzdalifah'. The ruling is that a dam (sacrifice) is required.
The dam is a sheep or equivalent.
2
Locate the first dalil
The Quranic verse (2:198) commands remembrance at al-Mash'ar al-Haram (Muzdalifah).
The verse is quoted in the text.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The command implies presence at Muzdalifah; omission requires compensation.
Hanafi usul: amr indicates wujub.
4
Locate the second dalil
The hadith of Urwah ibn Mudarris states that one who stands with the Prophet at Muzdalifah after standing at Arafah has completed Hajj.
The hadith is from Tirmidhi.
5
Derive the ruling
The hadith indicates that standing at Muzdalifah is essential; if missed, compensation is needed.
Missing a wajib requires dam, not invalidation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ تَرَكَ الْوُقُوفَ بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ ۲۴ وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وَمَنْ تَرَكَ الْوُقُوفَ بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمَ ا ﴿فَإِذَا أَفَضْتُم مِّنْ عَرَفَاتٍ فَاذْكُرُوا اللَّهَ عِندَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ ﴾ (سورة البقرة، 2 آلاية نمبر : 198) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ تَرَكَ الْوُقُوفَ بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ \ عَنْ عُرْوَةَ بْنِ مُضَرِّسِ بْنِ أَوس بن حارثة بن لام الطَّائِي، قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ . . . فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ شَهِدَ صَلَاتَنَا هَذِهِ، وَوَقَفَ مَعَنَا حَتَّى نَدْفَعَ وَقَدْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ لَيْلًا، أَوْ نَهَارًا ، فَقَدْ أَتَم حَجَّهُ، وَقَضَى تَفَثَهُ الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ أَدْرَكَ الإِمَامَ بِجَمْعٍ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الحَجَّ، نمبر: 891)
And whoever leaves the standing at Muzdalifah, upon him is a sacrifice. 24 Evidence (1): The verse as proof for leaving standing at Muzdalifah: 'Then when you depart from Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument (al-Mash'ar al-Haram).' (Surah al-Baqarah, 2:198) Evidence (2): The hadith as proof: from Urwah ibn Mudarris... he said: I came to the Messenger of Allah at Muzdalifah... So the Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever attends our this prayer, and stands with us until we depart, and has stood at Arafah before that, night or day, then he has completed his Hajj and fulfilled his dirtiness.' (Tirmidhi, Chapter on what came regarding one who catches up with the Imam at Jam' (Muzdalifah) then he has caught up with Hajj, no. 891)
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage rules that failing to perform the standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah requires a sacrifice (dam). Two proofs are given: first, the Quranic verse (al-Baqarah 2:198) which commands remembrance at al-Mash'ar al-Haram (Muzdalifah), implying the obligation of being there. Second, the hadith of Urwah ibn Mudarris, which explains that one who stands with the Prophet at Muzdalifah after having stood at Arafah has completed Hajj, indicating that standing at Muzdalifah is essential; omitting it requires compensation.

Key Terms
المشعر الحرام (al-mash'ar al-haram): Another name for Muzdalifah, the sacred monument where pilgrims stand after Arafah.
وقوف (wuquf): The act of standing, specifically at Arafah and Muzdalifah during Hajj.
دم (dam): A sacrifice (sheep or equivalent) required as compensation for missing a wajib in Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for a pilgrim who misses the standing at Muzdalifah?
A) His Hajj is invalid
B) He must sacrifice a dam
C) He must fast three days
D) No expiation is required

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, standing at Muzdalifah is wajib; leaving it requires a sacrifice (dam).

Leaving Stoning of Jamarat: Expiation and Proof
Rulings on leaving the stoning of the jamarat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the expiation required for omitting the stoning of the jamarat, distinguishing between cases of omitting all stoning, one day, one jamrah, and jamrat al-Aqabah, and identify the evidence (qawl al-tabi'i) used.

Core Idea
Omitting any part of the stoning of the jamarat requires expiation — the amount depends on how much is missed.

This passage from Al-Quduri lays out the precise expiations for various omissions during the stoning of the jamarat, a wajib act of Hajj. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for fulfilling your religious duties correctly. The rulings are supported by the sayings of early scholars (qawl al-tabi'i), which the Hanafi school accepts as valid proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal status
The act is stoning the jamarat, which is wajib in the Hanafi school. This lesson deals with the expiations for leaving it.
Wajib means obligatory but with a lower level of certainty than fard.
2
List the four scenarios of omission
Read the first part of the passage and note the four scenarios: leaving all stoning, leaving one day, leaving one jamrah, and leaving jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice.
3
Match each scenario with its expiation
For each scenario, identify the required expiation: dam or sadaqah. Dam is a sacrifice, sadaqah is half a sa' of wheat.
Dam is heavier than sadaqah.
4
Examine the proofs (qawl al-tabi'i)
Two proofs are cited: the statement of Ata ibn Abi Rabah and the statement of al-Zuhri/Aban ibn Uthman. Understand how they support the rulings.
The Hanafi school accepts the saying of a tabi'i as proof when not contradicted.
5
Distinguish between the scenarios
Note that missing one jamrah requires sadaqah, while missing an entire day or all days requires a dam. This distinction is often confused.
The hadith from Ata covers forgetting all until after tashreeq, not individual omissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ الْحِمَارِ فِي الْأَيَّامِ كُلِّهَا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ يَوْمٍ وَاحِدٍ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ إِحْدَى الْحِمَارِ الثَّلَاثِ فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ مِنْ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَم ۲۵ وجه (۱) قول التابعي لثبوت وَمَنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ الْحِمَارِ فِي الْأَيَّامِ \ عَنْ عَطَاءِ بْنِ أَبِي رَبَاحٍ أَنَّهُ قَالَ : " مَنْ نَسِيَ جَمْرَةً وَاحِدَةً أَوِ الْحِمَارَ كُلَّهَا حَتَّى يَذْهَبَ أَيَّامُ التَّشْرِيقِ فَدَمٌ وَاحِدٌ يُجْزِيهِ " (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ مَنْ تَرَكَ شَيْئًا مِنَ الرَّمْي حَتَّى يَذْهَبَ أَيَّامُ مِي، نمبر: 9688) وجه (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ الْحِمَارِ فِي الْأَيَّامِ \ عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، عَنْ أَبَانَ بْنِ عُثْمَانَ قَالَ: «وَاللَّهِ إِنَّ الصَّلَاةَ لَتُقْضَى، فَكَيْفَ لَا تَقْضِي رَمْيَ الْحِمَارِ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في الرَّجُلِ يَنْسَى أَنْ يَرْمِيَ الْجُمَارَ، يَقْضِيهِ أَوْ يُهْرِقُ دَمًا، نمبر: 15307)
And whoever leaves the stoning of the jamarat (literally 'the small stones') in all the days, upon him is a sacrifice; and if he leaves the stoning of one day, upon him is a sacrifice; and if he leaves the stoning of one of the three jamarat, upon him is sadaqah; and if he leaves jamrat al-Aqabah from the day of sacrifice, upon him is a sacrifice. 25 Evidence (1): The saying of a follower (tabi'i) as proof for 'Whoever leaves the stoning of the jamarat': from Ata ibn Abi Rabah that he said: 'Whoever forgets one jamrah or all the jamarat until the days of tashreeq pass, one sacrifice suffices him.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Chapter on one who leaves something of the stoning until the days of Mina pass, no. 9688) Evidence (2): The saying of a follower as proof for 'Whoever leaves the stoning of the jamarat': from al-Zuhri, from Aban ibn Uthman, he said: 'By Allah, the prayer is made up, so why not make up the stoning of the jamarat?' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, on a man who forgets to stone the jamarat, should he make it up or spill blood?, no. 15307)
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive ruling on omissions in the stoning of the jamarat. The rulings are: (1) If one omits the stoning of all three jamarat on all days (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul-Hijjah), a dam is required. (2) If one omits the stoning of one entire day (e.g., the 12th), a dam is required. (3) If one leaves stoning of one of the three jamarat on a given day, sadaqah is required. (4) If one leaves jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice (10th), a dam is required. Two proofs are given: the statement of Ata ibn Abi Rabah that one sacrifice suffices for all omissions of stoning; and the statement of al-Zuhri/Aban illustrating that stoning should be made up like prayer. These are qawl al-tabi'i, which serves as proof in Hanafi usul when not contradicted.

Key Terms
الحمار (al-himar): Literally 'the small stones', but here a plural form referring to the jamarat (stoning pillars).
صدقة (sadaqah): A charitable offering, here half a sa' of wheat or equivalent.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Dam
B) Sadaqah
C) Nothing
D) Repeat the Hajj

Key Takeaway
The expiation for omitting stoning ranges from sadaqah (for one jamrah) to a dam (for a full day or all days), supported by the sayings of early scholars (qawl al-tabi'i).

Delaying Shaving Until After Days of Nahr Requires a Sacrifice
Ruling on delaying shaving until after the days of Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying shaving during Hajj and identify the two proofs cited by Abu Hanifah.

Core Idea
Delaying shaving the head until after the days of Nahr requires a sacrifice (dam).

This lesson examines the specific ruling of Imam Abu Hanifah regarding a pilgrim who delays shaving or cutting their hair beyond the prescribed days of Nahr. The source cites two proofs: a hadith from Ibn Abbas and a statement from the tabi'is. Understanding this illustrates how the Hanafi school handles timing obligations in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delaying shaving (khalq) until after the days of Nahr. Ruling: wajib to perform it within those days; if delayed, a dam (sacrifice) is required. Note: The passage specifies this is the view of Abu Hanifah.
2
Locate the first proof
The first proof is a hadith from Ibn Abbas (mawquf) that whoever advances or delays an act of Hajj must spill blood.
This is a qawl sahabi.
3
Locate the second proof
The second proof is a statement from the tabi'is Amir and Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Aswad regarding a woman who forgot to trim her hair until after leaving.
This is a qawl tabi'i.
4
Evaluate the authority
Both proofs are zanni al-thubut, but they are used by Abu Hanifah to establish the ruling.
The Hanafi school considers qawl sahabi as a valid source.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ أَخَرَ الْخَلْقَ حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَيَّامُ النَّحْرِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت إِنْ أَخَّرَ الْخَلْقَ حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَيَّامُ التَّحْرِ عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسِ قَالَ: «مَنْ قَدَّمَ شَيْئًا مِنْ حَجِهِ أَوْأَخَرَهُ ، فَلْيُهْرِقُ لِذَلِكَ دَمًا ( ابن شيبة : فِي الرَّجُلِ يَحْلِقُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَذْبَحَ: 14958) وجه : (۲) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ أَخَرَ الْخَلْقَ حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَيَّامُ النَّحْرِ \ عَنْ عَامِرٍ فِي امْرَأَةٍ نَسِيَتْ أَنْ تُقَصِرَ حَتَّى خَرَجَتْ، فَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ الْأَسْوَدِ، وَعَامِرٌ: «تُقَصِرُ وَتُهْرِقُ دَمًا» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة في الرَّجُلِ وَالْمَرْأَةِ نَسِيَا أَنْ يُقَصِّرَا، نمبر : 15540)
And if he delays shaving until the days of Nahr have passed, upon him is a sacrifice according to Abu Hanifah. Evidence (1): The hadith as proof for delaying shaving until the days of Nahr have passed: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'Whoever brings forward something of his Hajj or delays it, let him spill blood for that.' (Ibn Abi Shaybah: on a man who shaves before slaughtering, no. 14958) Evidence (2): The saying of a follower (tabi'i) as proof for delaying shaving: from Amir regarding a woman who forgot to shorten (her hair) until she left, so Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Aswad and Amir said: 'She shortens and spills blood.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, on a man and woman who forget to shorten, no. 15540)
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage, attributed specifically to Abu Hanifah, rules that delaying the act of shaving (halq) or trimming (taqsir) until after the days of Nahr (10th-12th Dhul-Hijjah) requires a dam. This is because the order of actions on the Day of Sacrifice is prescribed; delaying beyond its time is an omission requiring compensation. Two proofs are cited: (1) The hadith of Ibn Abbas (mawquf) that any advancement or delay requires blood; (2) The statement of the tabi'is Amir and Abd al-Rahman regarding a woman who forgot to trim her hair, indicating that after leaving, she must still trim and offer a sacrifice. This reinforces the Hanafi position that the timing of haircutting is significant.

Key Terms
الخلق (al-khalq): Shaving or cutting the hair, which is part of the tahallul (emergence from ihram).
أيام النحر (ayyam al-nahr): The days of sacrifice, i.e., the 10th, 11th, and 12th of Dhul-Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A sacrifice (dam)
C) Sadaqah

Key Takeaway
Delaying the shaving of the head during Hajj beyond the days of Nahr necessitates a dam according to Imam Abu Hanifah.

Consolidation of Same-Kind Offences in Hajj
Usul principle: multiple same-kind offences require one dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle regarding multiple offences of the same kind in Hajj and apply it to determine the number of dams required.

Core Idea
Multiple violations of the same type in Hajj require only one dam.

The Hanafi school offers a merciful consolidation for pilgrims who commit multiple errors of the same kind during Hajj. Instead of burdening them with separate expiations for each omission, a single dam suffices. This principle is rooted in the teaching of the early scholar Ata ibn Abi Rabah and is exemplified by the stoning of the jamarat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nature of the offences
Determine whether the missed acts are of the same kind (jins wahid). For example, all missing the stoning of different jamarat is one kind.
The principle applies only when the offences are of the same category, such as multiple missed stonings.
2
Determine the individual expiation
If the offence is a missing wajib, the normal expiation is one dam. Recognise that each such omission would ordinarily require its own dam.
Most wajibat in Hajj are expiated by dam.
3
Apply the consolidation principle
If the offences are of the same kind, combine them into a single dam. One sacrifice suffices for all.
This prevents excessive expiation for similar errors.
4
Verify with the example
The text gives the example of stoning the jamarat: if a pilgrim misses two or three stones (or even multiple days), only one dam is needed.
This is the concrete application of the principle.
5
Note the boundary
If the offences are of different kinds (e.g., missing stoning and missing shaving), each kind requires its own separate dam.
The consolidation only works within the same jins.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول: اگر ایک جنس کی متعدد جنایت ہو جائے تو ایک ہی دم کافی ہو گا، مثلار می جمار.
Principle: If multiple offences of the same kind occur, a single sacrifice suffices, for example, the stoning of the jamarat.
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This is another usul note. It explains that if a pilgrim commits several similar omissions (e.g., missing the stoning of multiple jamarat on multiple days), one dam compensates for all. This is based on the evidence from Ata ibn Abi Rabah cited earlier in the chapter. This principle prevents excessive expiation for multiple related errors, reflecting the leniency of the Hanafi school within the framework of wajibat.

Key Terms
جنایت (jinayat): Offences or violations committed during Hajj that require expiation.
دم (dam): Expiatory sacrifice (usually a sheep or goat) required for missing certain Hajj obligations.
جنس واحد (jins wahid): Same kind or category.
رمی جمار (ramy al-jamarat): Stoning of the pillars at Mina during Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim commits multiple offences of the same kind during Hajj, how many dams are required?
A) One
B) One for each offence
C) None
D) It depends on the number of days

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle consolidates multiple same-kind Hajj offences into a single expiatory dam, preventing excessive burden on the pilgrim.

Ruling on Leaving Wuquf at Muzdalifah
States ruling on omitting Muzdalifah standing with Quran and hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on omitting wuquf at Muzdalifah, explain the evidence, and apply the consequence.

Core Idea
Wuquf at Muzdalifah is wajib; omission requires dam, but Hajj remains valid.

This passage from al-Quduri establishes a key wajib act in Hajj: standing at Muzdalifah. The Hanafi school, drawing on Quran and hadith, rules that leaving this standing does not break the Hajj but obligates a sacrifice. We will examine the proofs and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the act being discussed (wuquf at Muzdalifah) and its hukm level (wajib). Note the consequence stated: dam.
The passage begins by stating the ruling directly.
2
Examine the first proof – Quranic verse
Locate the Quranic verse (2:198) and understand how it supports the obligation. The imperative 'fa-udhkuru' indicates wujub in Hanafi usul.
The verse commands dhikr at the Sacred Monument after departing 'Arafat.
3
Analyze the second proof – Hadith of 'Urwah ibn Mudarris
Read the hadith: the Prophet (peace be upon him) describes completion of Hajj for one who stands at Muzdalifah with him. This implies that missing it requires a penalty, as omission does not preclude complete Hajj.
The hadith shows that wuquf at Muzdalifah is not a rukn.
4
Understand the consequence and cross-madhhab difference
Recognize that the Hanafi school considers this omission punishable by dam, while other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) view it as sunnah without penalty.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether a dam is required.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْحِنَايَاتِ فِي الْحَجّ وَمَنْ تَرَكَ الْوُقُوفَ بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَجْه: (۱) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ ﴿فَإِذَا أَفَضْتُم مِّنْ عَرَفَاتٍ فَاذْكُرُوا اللَّهَ عِندَ الْمَشْعَرِ الْحَرَامِ﴾ (سورة البقرة ۲:۱۹۸) وَجْه (۲) الْحَدِيثُ: عَنْ عُرْوَةَ بْنِ مُضَرِّسٍ قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بِالْمُزْدَلِفَةِ ... فَقَالَ: «مَنْ شَهِدَ صَلَاتَنَا هَذِهِ وَوَقَفَ مَعَنَا حَتَّى نَدْفَعَ وَقَدْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ لَيْلًا أَوْ نَهَارًا فَقَدْ أَتَمَّ حَجَّهُ وَقَضَى تَفَثَهُ» (ترمذي ۸۹۱)
Chapter of Offenses in Hajj: Whoever leaves the standing at Muzdalifah, upon him is a dam. Proof (1): The verse for establishing that: {And when you depart from 'Arafat, remember Allah at the Sacred Monument} (Surah al-Baqarah 2:198). Proof (2): The hadith: From 'Urwah ibn Mudarris, he said: I came to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) at Muzdalifah... He said: 'Whoever attends this prayer of ours and stands with us until we depart, having stood at 'Arafah before that by night or day, then he has completed his Hajj and fulfilled his obligations.' (Tirmidhi 891)
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The Hanafi school holds that wuquf at Muzdalifah is a wajib act in Hajj, not a rukn. If a pilgrim omits it, a dam (a sacrificial offering) becomes obligatory as compensation. The author provides two proofs: the Quranic verse (2:198) which commands dhikr at al-Mash'ar al-Haram (Muzdalifah), indicating its significance; and the hadith of 'Urwah ibn Mudarris which shows that missing the congregational standing at Muzdalifah does not invalidate Hajj if 'Arafah was performed, but implies that its omission requires a penalty. The dam is of a sheep or equivalent, and the Hajj remains valid.

Key Terms
وُقُوف (wuquf): Standing at a specific place during Hajj rituals
مُزْدَلِفَة (Muzdalifah): A place between 'Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night after 'Arafah
دَم (dam): A sacrificial penalty of a sheep or goat for omitting a wajib act in Hajj or 'Umrah

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A dam (penalty sacrifice) is required
C) No consequence, it is optional
D) Fasting three days is required

Key Takeaway
Omission of wuquf at Muzdalifah requires a dam; the Hajj remains valid.

Penalties for Omitting Ramy al-Jimar
Specifies dam or sadaqah penalties for various omissions of stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the penalties for omitting ramy al-jimar according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence from the Tabi'un.

Core Idea
Missing a single jamrah requires sadaqah; missing an entire day's ramy requires a dam.

The stoning of the jamarat (ramy) is a wajib act of Hajj during the days of Tashriq. The Hanafi school specifies precise penalties for omission, distinguishing between missing one jamrah, one full day, all days, or the specific Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr. This lesson details these rulings and the evidence from the statements of the Tabi'un, which the school accepts as a source of law in such matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that ramy al-jimar is wajib (obligatory) for each day of Tashriq. Omission triggers compensatory penalties.
The Hanafi position contrasts with some schools that consider ramy as sunnah.
2
Classify the omission
Determine whether the pilgrim missed all days, one full day, one jamrah only, or specifically Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr.
The classification directly determines the penalty.
3
State the corresponding penalty
Apply the rule: missing all days or one full day requires a dam; missing one jamrah requires a sadaqah; missing Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr requires a dam.
A dam is a sacrificial animal; sadaqah is half a sa' of wheat or similar.
4
Analyze the evidence
The proofs are statements of the Tabi'un ('Ata' and al-Zuhri) indicating that ramy is compensable and that a single dam suffices for multiple omissions.
The Hanafi school accepts qawl al-tabi'i as evidence when no contradictory text exists.
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Other schools may view ramy as sunnah, thus no penalty for omission. The Hanafi position relies on the obligation established by practice and these statements.
This ikhtilaf affects whether a deficient Hajj requires a dam or no compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ الْجِمَارِ فِي الْأَيَّامِ كُلِّهَا فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ يَوْمٍ وَاحِدٍ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ رَمْيَ إِحْدَى الْجِمَارِ الثَّلَاثِ فَعَلَيْهِ صَدَقَةٌ وَإِنْ تَرَكَ جَمْرَةَ الْعَقَبَةِ مِنْ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ وَجْه (۱) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنْ عَطَاءِ بْنِ أَبِي رَبَاحٍ قَالَ: «مَنْ نَسِيَ جَمْرَةً وَاحِدَةً أَوِ الْجِمَارَ كُلَّهَا حَتَّى يَذْهَبَ أَيَّامُ التَّشْرِيقِ فَدَمٌ وَاحِدٌ يُجْزِيهِ» (البيهقي ۹۶۸۸) وَجْه (۲) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ عَنْ أَبَانَ بْنِ عُثْمَانَ قَالَ: «وَاللَّهِ إِنَّ الصَّلَاةَ لَتُقْضَى فَكَيْفَ لَا تُقْضِي رَمْيَ الْجِمَارِ» (ابن أبي شيبة ۱۵۳۰۷)
Whoever leaves the stoning of the jamarat in all the days, upon him is a dam. If he leaves the stoning of one day, upon him is a dam. If he leaves the stoning of one of the three jamarat, upon him is a sadaqah. If he leaves Jamrat al-Aqabah on the day of Nahr, upon him is a dam. Proof (1): The statement of the Tabi'i: From 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah: 'Whoever forgets one jamrah or all the jamarat until the days of Tashriq have passed, one dam suffices him.' (Bayhaqi 9688) Proof (2): The statement of the Tabi'i: From al-Zuhri from Aban ibn 'Uthman: 'By Allah, the prayer is made up, so why would the stoning of the jamarat not be made up?' (Ibn Abi Shaybah 15307)
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage provides detailed rulings on the penalty for omitting ramy (stoning) during the days of Tashriq. According to the matn, if a pilgrim misses all stonings on all days, a dam is required. If he misses the stoning of one entire day (i.e., all three jamarat on that day), also a dam. If he misses stoning one jamrah (out of three) on a given day, a sadaqah (charity) is required. However, if he misses Jamrat al-Aqabah specifically on the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), a dam is required. The proofs are from the statements of the Tabi'un: 'Ata' ibn Abi Rabah and al-Zuhri, indicating that the ramy is compensable, and different levels of omission incur different penalties. The Hanafi usul distinguishes between missing the majority vs minority of pebbles, as mentioned in the later usul notes: if missing seven pebbles per day, majority is 4; missing majority requires dam, minority requires sadaqah.

Key Terms
رَمْي (ramy): Stoning of the jamarat during Hajj
جَمْرَة (jamrah): One of the three stone pillars stoned in Mina
صَدَقَة (sadaqah): A charitable offering, here one-half sa' of wheat or similar

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pilgrim forgets to stone one jamrah on a day of Tashriq, what is the required penalty according to the Hanafi school?
A) Dam
B) Sadaqah
C) Nothing, it can be omitted
D) Fasting

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes a dam for missing an entire day's ramy and a sadaqah for missing a single jamrah, based on statements of the Tabi'un.

Delaying Halq Beyond the Days of Nahr Requires Dam
States ruling and proof for dam on delayed halq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying halq beyond the days of Nahr and explain the dalil that supports it.

Core Idea
Delaying halq beyond the days of Nahr incurs dam—a wajib delayed requires compensation.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Al-Quduri regarding the timing of halq (shaving) in Hajj. According to Abu Hanifa, if a pilgrim delays shaving until after the three days of Nahr (10th–12th Dhul Hijjah), a dam (sacrificial animal) becomes obligatory. We will explore the textual proof and the legal reasoning behind this requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is delaying halq (shaving the head) beyond the days of Nahr (10th–12th Dhul Hijjah). The ruling according to Abu Hanifa is that dam is wajib.
Halq is a ritual act in Hajj. The days of Nahr are the three days after Eid al-Adha.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Ibn Abbas (ra): 'Whoever advances or delays anything of his Hajj, let him spill blood.' This is a general proof that any premature or delayed Hajj act requires a sacrifice.
The hadith is narrated by Ibn Abi Shaybah and is considered ahad (solitary), but it is used as evidence in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'falyuhriq' (let him spill blood) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul. Delaying halq falls under 'anything of his Hajj', so the ruling applies.
The general nature of the hadith covers all Hajj acts, including halq.
4
Consider the secondary proof
The statement of the Tabi'i 'Amir and 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Aswad regarding a woman who forgot to trim her hair until after leaving the sanctuary: she must trim and offer dam. This confirms that delaying hair removal requires compensation.
This is a qawl al-sahabi (or Tabi'i) which is also used as evidence.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Other madhhabs may consider halq as sunnah and not require dam for delay. The Hanafi position is specific: halq is wajib, and delay incurs dam.
The practical difference: a Hanafi must offer dam if delayed; a Shafi'i might not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ أَخَّرَ الْحَلْقَ حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَيَّامُ النَّحْرِ فَعَلَيْهِ دَمٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَجْه (۱) الْحَدِيثُ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «مَنْ قَدَّمَ شَيْئًا مِنْ حَجِّهِ أَوْ أَخَّرَهُ فَلْيُهْرِقْ لِذَلِكَ دَمًا» (ابن أبي شيبة ۱۴۹۵۸) وَجْه (۲) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنْ عَامِرٍ فِي امْرَأَةٍ نَسِيَتْ أَنْ تُقَصِّرَ حَتَّى خَرَجَتْ فَقَالَ عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنُ الْأَسْوَدِ وَعَامِرٌ: «تُقَصِّرُ وَتُهْرِيقُ دَمًا» (ابن أبي شيبة ۱۵۵۴۰)
If he delays the shaving until the days of Nahr have passed, then upon him is a dam according to Abu Hanifah. Proof (1): The hadith: From Ibn 'Abbas that he said: 'Whoever advances or delays anything of his Hajj, let him spill blood for that (i.e., offer a sacrifice).' (Ibn Abi Shaybah 14958) Proof (2): The statement of the Tabi'i: From 'Amir regarding a woman who forgot to shorten her hair until she left (the sanctuary), 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Aswad and 'Amir said: 'She shortens and spills blood (offers a sacrifice).' (Ibn Abi Shaybah 15540)
Source pages p. 278

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling of Abu Hanifah on delaying halq (shaving or trimming hair) beyond the three days of Nahr (10th-12th Dhul Hijjah). According to Abu Hanifah, a dam is required. The proofs include a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas that any premature or delayed act in Hajj necessitates a sacrifice, and a statement from the Tabi'un 'Amir and 'Abd al-Rahman ibn al-Aswad regarding a woman who delayed taqsir (hair trimming) until after leaving the sanctuary. This indicates that hair removal is time-specific and delayed performance requires compensation. The Hanafi school generally holds that halq is wajib and must be performed within the Haram and within the days of Nahr; delaying it beyond those days incurs dam. The text does not mention the positions of Abu Yusuf or Muhammad here, but the ruling is attributed specifically to Abu Hanifah.

Key Terms
حَلْق (halq): Shaving the head completely, a ritual act in Hajj/Umrah
تَقْصِير (taqsir): Trimming the hair, an alternative to shaving for women or men
أَيَّام النَّحْر (ayyam al-nahr): The days of sacrifice: 10th, 11th, 12th of Dhul Hijjah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No penalty
B) Fasting three days
C) Dam
D) Sadaqah

Key Takeaway
Delaying halq beyond the days of Nahr requires a dam according to Abu Hanifah, supported by the general hadith on advancing/delaying Hajj acts.

Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah Requires a Dam
States ruling on delaying tawaf al-ziyarah with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying tawaf al-ziyarah and explain why the 'la haraj' hadith does not negate the obligation of a dam.

Core Idea
Delaying tawaf al-ziyarah requires a dam, even though the order of rites is flexible.

In the previous lesson, we saw that missing ramy or delaying it requires a dam. Here, al-Quduri extends the same ruling to delaying tawaf al-ziyarah, also known as tawaf al-ifadah. He provides two proofs: a statement from the Madinan jurists and the well-known hadith of Ibn Abbas about the Prophet's response 'la haraj'. The Hanafi school interprets 'la haraj' as confirming the validity of the Hajj, not as an exemption from compensation due to delay.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What is the act being discussed? Delaying tawaf al-ziyarah beyond its prescribed time. What is the ruling? It requires a dam (penalty of sacrificing an animal).
The ruling is an extension of the previous passage on ramy.
2
Examine the first proof: practice of Madinan jurists
Al-Quduri cites a report from the Madinan jurists: one who forgets tawaf until returning home remains in ihram and must return to perform tawaf; if he had intercourse, he must offer a camel. This shows that tawaf is obligatory and cannot be abandoned without penalty.
This is a qawl sahabi or practice of the people of Madina.
3
Examine the second proof: the 'la haraj' hadith
Ibn Abbas narrates that a man asked about performing rites out of order, and the Prophet replied 'la haraj' (no harm). At first glance, this might suggest no penalty for delay. But the Hanafi school distinguishes: the hadith addresses order, not the timing of the act itself.
The hadith is sahih, but its dalala (indication) is zanni regarding the ruling on delay.
4
Understand the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith
The Hanafis understand 'la haraj' to mean the Hajj is valid despite the changed order. However, delaying an obligatory act like tawaf beyond its time (the days of Nahr) is a separate violation that incurs a dam. The hadith does not explicitly excuse delay; it only permits advancing or postponing rites relative to each other.
This interpretation is based on usul: the hadith is general (amm) but the ruling on delay is derived from other proofs.
5
Conclude the ruling and its evidence strength
The Hanafi position is clear: delaying tawaf al-ziyarah requires a dam. The proofs reinforce that tawaf is a pillar (rukn) and must be performed within its time; if delayed, compensation is due.
This is the mufta bihi position in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَا إِذَا أَخَّرَ طَوَافَ الزِّيَارَةِ وَجْه (۱) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنْ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَنِ الْفُقَهَاءِ الَّذِينَ يُنْتَهَى إِلَى قَوْلِهِمْ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْمَدِينَةِ: «مَنْ نَسِيَ أَنْ يُفِيضَ حَتَّى رَجَعَ إِلَى بِلَادِهِ فَهُوَ حَرَامٌ حِينَ يَذْكُرُ حَتَّى يَرْجِعَ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ فَيَطُوفَ بِهِ فَإِنْ أَصَابَ النِّسَاءَ أَهْدَى بَدَنَةً» (البيهقي ۹۶۵۰) وَجْه (۲) الْحَدِيثُ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: قَالَ رَجُلٌ لِلنَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: زُرْتُ قَبْلَ أَنْ أَرْمِيَ قَالَ: لَا حَرَجَ قَالَ: حَلَقْتُ قَبْلَ أَنْ أَذْبَحَ قَالَ: لَا حَرَجَ قَالَ: ذَبَحْتُ قَبْلَ أَنْ أَرْمِيَ قَالَ: لَا حَرَجَ (بخاري ۱۷۲۲/ مسلم ۱۳۰6)
And likewise if he delays tawaf al-ziyarah. Proof (1): The statement of the Tabi'i: From Abu al-Zinad from the jurists of Madinah: 'Whoever forgets to perform ifadah (tawaf al-ziyarah) until he returns to his homeland, he remains in ihram until he returns to the House and performs tawaf; if he has had intercourse with women, he must offer a camel.' (Bayhaqi 9650) Proof (2): The hadith: From Ibn 'Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) that a man said to the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'I visited (i.e., performed tawaf) before stoning.' He said: 'No harm.' He said: 'I shaved before slaughtering.' He said: 'No harm.' He said: 'I slaughtered before stoning.' He said: 'No harm.' (Bukhari 1722/Muslim 1306)
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage extends the previous ruling: similarly, delaying tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf of Hajj, also called ifadah) beyond its time requires a dam. The first proof is from the practice of the Madinan jurists, indicating that one who forgets tawaf must return and perform it while remaining in ihram; if he had marital relations, he must give a camel as penalty. The second proof is the well-known hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) allowed advancing or delaying certain rites without harm (la haraj). The Hanafi school interprets this hadith to mean that such actions are valid but may still require a dam if done out of order or delay. The phrase 'la haraj' indicates that the Hajj is sound, but the required order is not a condition for validity; however, compensation may still be due. Thus, delaying tawaf al-ziyarah necessitates dam.

Key Terms
طَوَاف الزِّيَارَة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory tawaf performed after returning from Mina, also called tawaf al-ifadah
إِفَاضَة (ifadah): Alternate name for tawaf al-ziyarah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No penalty
B) Invalidates Hajj
C) Requires a dam
D) Requires a sadaqah

Key Takeaway
Delaying tawaf al-ziyarah requires a dam; the 'la haraj' hadith does not negate this obligation.

Principles of Penalties for Hajj Wajibat: Dam, Sadaqah, and Place
Explains three Hanafi usul principles on penalties for Hajj omissions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi penalty (dam or sadaqah) for omitting a wajib act in Hajj or 'Umrah, and apply the rules for ramy and halq/taqsir.

Core Idea
Missing a wajib in Hajj requires dam but does not invalidate; ramy omissions are graded; halq must be within the Haram.

This lesson presents three short but essential usul principles from the Hanafi school regarding penalties for omissions in Hajj and 'Umrah. These principles clarify that not every mistake invalidates the pilgrimage, but specific compensations (dam or sadaqah) are due depending on the nature and extent of the omission. Understanding these gradations is key to applying Hanafi fiqh correctly.

Guided Path
1
General rule for wajib omission
Identify the overarching principle: if any wajib act is omitted in Hajj or 'Umrah, a dam (sacrifice) becomes necessary. However, the Hajj or 'Umrah remains valid and is not repeated.
This applies even to essential wajibat like sa'i.
2
Apply to sa'i in 'Umrah
Recognise that sa'i between Safa and Marwah is wajib in 'Umrah. If omitted, dam is due but the 'Umrah is completed without invalidation.
This distinguishes Hanafi view from those who consider sa'i a rukn.
3
Graded penalty for ramy omissions
Note the distinction: for ramy al-jamarat, the full number is seven pebbles. If the pilgrim omits the majority (four or more), a dam is required. If the omission is less than half (three or fewer), only a sadaqah (charity) is needed.
The exact threshold is 'most' vs 'less than half'.
4
Place-bound requirement for halq/taqsir
According to Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad, the acts of shaving (halq) or trimming (taqsir) the hair must be performed inside the sacred precincts of the Haram. Doing so outside incurs a dam.
This is because the ritual is tied to the sanctity of the Haram.
5
Synthesise the three principles
Summarise: (1) wajib omission → dam, valid; (2) ramy omission: most → dam, less than half → sadaqah; (3) halq outside Haram → dam.
These rulings are mufta bihi in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول : واجبات کے چھوٹنے سے دم لازم ہو گا، عمرہ میں سعی بین الصفاء والمر وہ لازم ہے ، اگر ترک ہو جائے تو دم لازم ہو گا البتہ حج یا عمرہ تمام ہو جائے گا. اصول : رمی میں سات کنکری مارنا چاہئے اگر اکثر کم ہو جائے تو دم لازم ہے، اور آدھے سے کم پر صدقہ ہے. اصول: امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد: حج یا عمرہ میں حلق یا قصر حرم کے ساتھ خاص ہے، لہذا حرم سے باہر حلق پر دم لازم ہو گا.
Principles: From the omission of wajibat, dam becomes necessary. In 'Umrah, sa'i between Safa and Marwah is wajib; if omitted, dam becomes necessary, but the Hajj or 'Umrah is completed. Principle: In ramy, one should throw seven pebbles; if most are omitted, dam is required; if less than half, sadaqah is required. Principle: Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad: Halq or taqsir in Hajj or 'Umrah is specific to the Haram; therefore, halq outside the Haram incurs dam.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
These are usul notes (principles) that comment on the earlier penalties. They clarify three key points: (1) Any omission of a wajib act in Hajj or 'Umrah requires a dam, and the act is still valid. For example, sa'i in 'Umrah is wajib; if omitted, dam must be given but the 'Umrah is complete. (2) For ramy, the required number is seven pebbles per jamrah per day. If one misses most (i.e., four or more), a dam is due; if less than half (three or fewer), a sadaqah suffices. This fine distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh. (3) According to Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad, the acts of halq (shaving) or taqsir (trimming) must be performed within the boundaries of the Haram (sanctuary). If one performs them outside, a dam is required. This is because the ritual of removing hair is tied to the sanctity of the Haram.

Key Terms
سَعْي (sa'i): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah
حَرَم (Haram): The sacred precincts of Makkah
رَمْي (ramy): The ritual stoning of the jamarat
دَم (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep) required as penalty for certain omissions
صَدَقَة (sadaqah): Charity; here a specified amount (e.g., half a sa' of wheat) for minor omissions

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Dam
B) Sadaqah
C) No penalty
D) Fasting

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, omission of a wajib in Hajj/Umrah requires a dam but does not invalidate; ramy penalties depend on quantity omitted; halq/taqsir must be in the Haram.

Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Ruling and Proofs
Ruling with hadith proofs and usul notes on delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah and explain why a dam is required if it is omitted entirely.

Core Idea
Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah is permissible without penalty, but omitting it entirely requires a sacrificial animal (dam).

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi position on delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah (also called Tawaf al-Ifadah) during Hajj. The source passage presents the ruling that changing the order of Hajj rites does not incur sin, as supported by the famous hadith of Ibn Abbas. However, if the Tawaf is neglected entirely, the obligation remains and must be fulfilled with a compensatory sacrifice. We will trace the proofs and understand the underlying usul principle that distinguishes between permissible delay and total omission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The source opens with 'And similarly if he delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah' implying that delaying is treated like other delays: it does not invalidate but requires remedy if the act is omitted entirely.
The phrase 'wa kadha' (and similarly) links to previous rulings on delays.
2
Examine the first proof (Anas hadith)
The hadith of Anas shows the Prophet's order of actions on the day of Nahr: throwing, slaughtering, then shaving. This establishes that the sequence is sunnah but not mandatory.
Sequence is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib.
3
Analyze the second proof (Madinan fuqaha)
If one forgets Tawaf al-Ifadah and returns home, he remains in ihram until he returns and performs it; if he has marital relations, he owes a badanah (camel). This indicates the Tawaf is a wajib that must be fulfilled eventually.
Badanah is a camel; shows severity of omission.
4
Study the third proof (Ibn Abbas hadith)
The Prophet said 'la haraj' (no harm) for changing the order of rites (visiting before throwing, shaving before slaughtering, etc.). This proves that delay is permitted without penalty, but it does not excuse the obligation.
The hadith is in Bukhari and Muslim, indicating strong authenticity.
5
Apply the usul note
The commentary explicitly states: 'Omission of obligations requires a sacrificial animal.' Therefore, if Tawaf al-Ziyarah is completely omitted (not just delayed), a dam is wajib. If it is merely delayed and eventually performed, no penalty.
The usul notes also cover rami and halq, but the principle is consistent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْحِنَايَاتِ فِي الْحَجّ
وَكَذَا إِذَا أَخَرَ طَوَافَ الزِّيَارَةِ
وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَإِنْ أَخَرَ الْخَلْقَ حَتَّى مَضَتْ أَيَّامُ النَّحْرِ 
عَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكِ: «أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَتَى مِنًى، فَأَتَى الْجَمْرَةَ فَرَمَاهَا، ثُمَّ أَتَى مَنْزِلَهُ مِنًى وَنَحَرَ، ثُمَّ قَالَ لِلْحَلَّاقِ خُذْ وَأَشَارَ إِلَى جَانِبِهِ الْأَيْمَنِ، (مسلم: بَابُ بَيَانِ أَنَّ السُّنَّةَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ أَنْ يَرْمِيَ، ثُمَّ يَنْحَرَ، ثم يخلق نمبر: 1305)
۲۷ وجه (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَكَذَا إِذَا أَخَرَ طَوَافَ الزِيَارَةِ 
عَنْ أَبِي الزِّنَادِ عَنِ الْفُقَهَاءِ الَّذِينَ يُنْتَهَى إِلَى قَوْهِمْ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْمَدِينَةِ كَانُوا يَقُولُونَ: مَنْ نَسِيَ أَنْ يُفِيضَ حَتَّى رَجَعَ إِلَى بِلَادِهِ فَهُوَ حَرَامٌ حِينَ يَذْكُرُ حَتَّى يَرْجِعَ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ فَيَطُوفَ بِهِ فَإِنْ أَصَابَ النِّسَاءَ أَهْدَى بَدَنَةً (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ التَّحَلُّلِ بِالطَّوَافِ إِذَا كَانَ قَدْ سَعَى عَقِيبَ طَوَافِ الْقُدُومِ، نمبر: 9650)
وجه:(۲) الحديث لثبوت وَكَذَا إِذَا أَخَرَ طَوَافَ الزِّيَارَةِ 
عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رضي الله عنهما: «قَالَ رَجُلٌ لِلنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم: زُرْتُ قَبْلَ أَنْ أَرْمِي، قَالَ: لَا حَرَجَ، قَالَ: حَلَقْتُ قَبْلَ أَنْ أَذْبَحَ، قَالَ: لَا حَرَجَ، قَالَ: ذَبَحْتُ قَبْلَ أَنْ أَرْمِيَ، قَالَ: لَا حَرَجَ (بخاري بَابُ الذَّبْحِ قَبْلَ الْخَلْقِ، نمبر: 1722/ مسلم: بَاب مَنْ حَلَقَ قَبْلَ النَّحْرِ ، أَوْ نَخَرَ قَبْلَ الرَّمْي، نمبر: 1306
اصول : واجبات کے چھوٹنے سے دم لازم ہو گا، عمرہ میں سعی بین الصفاء والمر وہ لازم ہے ، اگر ترک ہو جائے تو دم لازم ہو گا البتہ حج یا عمرہ تمام ہو جائے گا.
اصول : رمی میں سات کنکری مارنا چاہئے اگر اکثر کم ہو جائے تو دم لازم ہے، اور آدھے سے کم پر صدقہ ہے. اصول: امام ابو حنیفہ اور امام محمد: حج یا عمرہ میں حلق یا قصر حرم کے ساتھ خاص ہے، لہذا حرم سے باہر حلق پر دم لازم ہو گا.
Chapter of Mistakes in Hajj. And similarly if he delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah. Proof (3): Hadith for establishing that if he delays the creation until the days of Nahr have passed. From Anas ibn Malik: The Messenger of Allah came to Mina, then came to the Jamrah and threw, then came to his lodging in Mina and slaughtered, then said to the barber: 'Take,' and pointed to his right side. (Muslim: Chapter on clarifying that the Sunnah on the day of Nahr is to throw, then slaughter, then shave, no. 1305). 27 Proof (1): Saying of the Tabi‘i to establish that if he delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah: From Abu al-Zinad from the fuqaha of Medina whose words are relied upon: they said: Whoever forgets to perform al-Ifadah until he returns to his country, he remains in ihram until he remembers and returns to the House and performs Tawaf; and if he has intercourse, he must offer a badanah (Baihaqi: Chapter on tahlil with Tawaf if he did Sa‘i after Tawaf al-Qudum, no. 9650). Proof (2): Hadith to establish that if he delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah: Ibn Abbas: A man said to the Prophet: I visited before throwing; he said: No harm. I shaved before slaughtering; he said: No harm. I slaughtered before throwing; he said: No harm (Bukhari: Chapter on slaughter before shaving, no. 1722; Muslim: Chapter on whoever shaved before slaughtering or slaughtered before throwing, no. 1306). Usul: Omission of obligations requires a sacrificial animal; in ‘Umrah, Sa‘i between Safa and Marwah is obligatory, and if omitted, a sacrificial animal is required, but the Hajj or ‘Umrah is completed. Usul: In rami, one must throw seven pebbles; if most are missed, a sacrificial animal is required; if less than half, sadaqah. Usul: Imam Abu Hanifah and Imam Muhammad: Shaving or trimming in Hajj or ‘Umrah is specific to the Haram, so if one shaves outside the Haram, a sacrificial animal is required.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on mistakes in Hajj addresses the ruling on delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah. The matn states 'And similarly if he delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah,' implying that like other delayed obligations, it requires a dam (sacrificial animal). The commentary then provides three proofs. The first proof (from Anas) shows the order of actions on the day of Nahr: throwing, then slaughtering, then shaving. The second proof from the Madinan fuqaha states that if someone forgets the Ifadah tawaf and returns home, he remains in ihram until returning and performing tawaf; if he has intercourse, he must sacrifice a badanah (camel). The third proof (from Ibn Abbas) establishes that changing the order or delaying actions does not incur sin or penalty (‘la haraj’). However, the usul notes clarify that this only applies if the obligation is eventually fulfilled; if a wajib is omitted entirely, a dam becomes necessary. The usul also explains rules for rami (throwing pebbles) and shaving (halq) – the latter must be done within the Haram according to Abu Hanifah and Muhammad.

Key Terms
طواف الزيارة (tawaf al-ziyarah): The obligatory Tawaf of Hajj performed after returning from Mina, also called Tawaf al-Ifadah.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal required for omitting a wajib act in Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muhrim delays Tawaf al-Ziyarah until after the days of Nahr, what is the ruling?
A) Hajj is invalid and must be repeated.
B) Hajj is valid but a dam is required.
C) No penalty, as the delay is permissible.
D) Hajj is valid but sadaqah is required.

Key Takeaway
Delaying Tawaf al-Ziyarah is permissible without penalty as long as it is eventually performed; only complete omission requires a dam.

The Prohibition of Hunting During Ihram and the Full Penalty for a Muhrim
Ruling with multiple proofs on the penalty for a muhrim who kills or directs to game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a muhrim who kills or points to game, identify the Quranic and Prophetic proofs, and apply the penalty options to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Killing or even pointing to land game in ihram triggers a wajib penalty, whether intentional or not.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on hunting during ihram. The matn delivers a strict prohibition: a muhrim who kills game or merely directs another to do so must pay the full penalty. This applies equally to the deliberate and the forgetful, the first-time and the repeat offender. We will then explore the proofs from the Quran and Sunnah that establish this rule, including the distinction between land and sea game and the exceptions for harmful animals.

Guided Path
1
State the core ruling
Read the matn: if a muhrim kills game or points to it such that another kills it, the full penalty (jaza') is wajib. Note that this applies equally to intentional and unintentional acts.
The penalty is not reduced for forgetfulness or ignorance.
2
Identify the primary Quranic proof
Quran 5:94 directly prohibits killing game in ihram and prescribes three options for the penalty: an equivalent livestock animal, feeding the poor, or fasting.
The verse mentions 'intentional' but the prohibition applies generally; the penalty clause is triggered by the act, not just the intent.
3
Understand the scope of prohibition
Quran 5:96 clarifies that only land game (sayd al-barr) is forbidden; sea game (sayd al-bahr) is halal for the muhrim.
This distinction is crucial: fish and other sea creatures are permissible even during ihram.
4
Note the exceptions
The hadith of the five harmful animals (crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, ferocious dog) allows killing them even by a muhrim, as they are not considered game.
These exceptions prove the general rule: all other land game is prohibited.
5
Apply the ruling to pointing
The hadith of Abu Qatadah and the saying of Hasan and Ata confirm that pointing to game (even without killing) incurs the penalty. The muhrim who directs a non-muhrim to kill is liable.
This prevents a loophole where a muhrim could indirectly cause the death of game.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الصيد
وَإِنْ قَتَلَ الْمُحْرِمُ صَيْدًا أَوْ دَلَّ عَلَيْهِ مَنْ قَتَلَهُ فَعَلَيْهِ الْجَزَاءُ كَامِلًا يَسْتَوِي فِي ذَلِكَ الْعَامِدُ وَالنَّاسِي وَالْمُبْتَدِئُ وَالْعَائِدُ
وجه : (۱) الآية لثبوت 
يَا أَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا لَا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنتُمْ حُرُمٌ وَمَن قَتَلَهُ مِنكُم مُّتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاءٌ مِّثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَمِ يَحْكُمُ بِهِ ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِّنكُمْ هَدْيًا بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ أَوْ كَفَّارَةٌ طَعَامُ مَسَاكِينَ أَوْ عَدْلُ ذَلِكَ صِيَامًا لِّيَذُوقَ وَبَالَ أَمْرِهِ (القرآن سورة المائدة، 5:94)
وجه: (٢) الآية لثبوت 
أُحِلَّ لَكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَحْرِ وَطَعَامُهُ مَتَاعًا لَّكُمْ وَلِلسَّيَّارَةِ وَحُرِّمَ عَلَيْكُمْ صَيْدُ الْبَرِّ مَا دُمْتُمْ حُرُمًا وَاتَّقُوا اللَّهَ الَّذِي إِلَيْهِ تُحْشَرُونَ (القرآن سورة المائدة، 5:96)
وجه : (۳) الحديث لثبوت 
عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: خَمْسٌ مِنَ الدَّوَاتِ، كُلُهُنَّ فَاسِقٌ، يُقْتَلْنَ فِي الحِلِّ وَالحَرَمِ: الغُرَابُ، وَالحِدَأَةُ، وَالعَقْرَبُ، وَالفَأْرَةُ، وَالكَلْبُ العَقُورُ (بخاري: بَابُ مَا يَقْتُلُ الْمُحْرِمُ مِنَ الدَّوَاتِ، نمبر 1829؛ مسلم: بَابُ مَا يَنْدُبُ لِلْمُحْرِمِ وَغَيْرِهِ قَتْلَهُ مِنَ الدَّوَاتِ فِي الْحِلِّ وَالحَرَمِ، نمبر 1198)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت 
أَخْبَرَنِي عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ، ثُمَّ قُلْنَا: أَنَأْكُلُ لَحْمَ صَيْدٍ وَنَحْنُ مُحْرِمُونَ؟ فَحَمَلْنَا مَا بَقِيَ مِن لَّحْمِهَا، قَالَ: «أَمِنْكُمْ أَحَدٌ أَمَرَهُ أَنْ يَحْمِلَ عَلَيْهَا، أَوْ أَشَارَ إِلَيْهَا» . قَالُوا : لا ، قَالَ: «فَكُلُوا مَا بَقِيَ مِن لَّحْمِهَا» (بخاري بَابٌ: لَا يُشِيرُ الْمُحْرِمُ إِلَى الصَّيْدِ لِكَيْ يَصْطَادَهُ الحَلَالُ، 1824؛ مسلم: بَابُ تَحْرِيمِ الصَّيْدِ لِلْمُحْرِمِ، 1196)
وجه:(۲) قول التابعى لثبوت 
عَنِ الْحَسَنِ، وَعَطَاءٍ، فِي الْمُحْرِمِ أَشَارَ إِلَى صَيْدٍ فَأَصَابَهُ مُحْرِمٌ، قَالَا: «عَلَيْهِ الْجَزَاءُ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: فِي الْمُشِيرِ إِلَى الصَّيْدِ مَنْ قَالَ عَلَيْهِ الْجَزَاءُ، نمبر: 15518)
اصول : احرام کی حالت میں خشکی کے شکار کرنا حرام ہے البتہ سمندری شکار جائز ہے۔
Chapter on Hunting. If a muhrim kills game, or points to it and someone else kills it, then upon him is the full penalty; in that are equal the intentional and the forgetful, the beginner and the repeat offender. Proof (1): The verse [O you who believe! Do not kill game while you are in ihram. Whoever among you kills it intentionally, the penalty is an equivalent of what he killed from livestock, as judged by two just men among you, an offering to the Ka‘bah, or a kaffarah of feeding the poor, or the equivalent of that in fasting, that he may taste the consequence of his matter] (Quran 5:94). Proof (2): The verse [Permitted to you is the game of the sea and its food, as enjoyment for you and for the travelers, but forbidden to you is the game of the land as long as you are in ihram. And fear Allah to whom you will be gathered] (Quran 5:96). Proof (3): The hadith from ‘Aishah that the Messenger of Allah said: ‘Five harmful animals, each of which is wicked, may be killed in the state of halal and haram: the crow, the kite, the scorpion, the mouse, and the ferocious dog.’ (Bukhari no. 1829; Muslim no. 1198). Proof (1) of hadith: ‘Abdullah ibn Abi Qatadah narrated: Then we said: 'May we eat the meat of game while we are in ihram?' So we carried what remained of its meat. He said: 'Is there anyone among you who commanded to carry it, or pointed to it?' They said: 'No.' He said: 'Then eat what remains of its meat.' (Bukhari no. 1824; Muslim no. 1196). Proof (2): Saying of the Tabi‘i: From al-Hasan and ‘Ata’ concerning a muhrim who pointed to game, and a muhrim killed it; they both said: 'Upon him is the penalty.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah no. 15518). Usul: In the state of ihram, hunting on land is haram, but sea hunting is permissible.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on hunting (sawd) in the context of Hajj. The matn delivers the core ruling: if a person in ihram kills game (sawd) or merely points to it so that another kills it, he must pay the full penalty (jaza). This applies equally to intentional and unintentional acts, and to first-time and repeat offenders. The commentary then provides five proofs: (1) Quran 5:94, which explicitly forbids killing game in ihram and prescribes a sliding scale of penalty – an equivalent animal from livestock, or feeding the poor, or fasting. (2) Quran 5:96, which distinguishes sea game (halal) from land game (haram) during ihram. (3) The hadith of the five harmful animals that are exempted from this prohibition and can be killed even by a muhrim. (4) The hadith of Abu Qatadah, which shows that a muhrim may eat game killed by a non-muhrim if the muhrim did not help, point, or command. (5) The opinion of the Tabi‘un Hasan and ‘Ata’ that even pointing to game invites the penalty. The concluding usul note reaffirms: land game is absolutely haram, sea game is halal.

Key Terms
مُحْرِم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or ‘Umrah and is bound by its prohibitions.
صَيْد (sayd): Game animals and birds that are permissible to eat when not in ihram; includes land game exclusively.
جَزَاء (jaza'): The penalty or compensation required for killing game in ihram; it is either an equivalent sacrificial animal, feeding the poor, or fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muhrim points to a game animal and a non-muhrim kills it, what is the ruling?
A) Only the non-muhrim is responsible.
B) The muhrim has no penalty because he did not kill it himself.
C) The muhrim must pay the full penalty (jaza').
D) The muhrim must pay a small sadaqah.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim incurs the full penalty (jaza') for killing land game or even directing another to do so, regardless of intent, based on clear Quranic and Prophetic evidence.
