Penalty for Hunting by a Muhrim: Valuation and Options
Establishes penalty valuation method and three options for a muhrim who kills game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the penalty (jaza') for a muhrim who kills game, including the valuation method and the three options (sacrifice, charity, fasting), and identify the evidence from Quran and Sunnah.

Core Idea
A muhrim's penalty for killing game is based on value, with choice among sacrifice, charity, or fasting.

When a person in ihram kills game, a penalty becomes wajib. Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf teach that the game is evaluated by two just persons at the location of the killing. The muhrim then has three options: sacrifice, charity, or fasting. This lesson explains the valuation method and the options, with evidence from the Quran and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? Who is the subject? What is the legal consequence?
The act is killing game by a muhrim. The ruling is that a penalty (jaza') is wajib.
2
Understand the valuation method
How is the penalty determined? The game is evaluated in the place of killing by two just persons. The valuation serves as the basis for all options.
The location: place of killing or nearest place. Two just persons determine the value.
3
List the three options
The muhrim may choose among: (1) buying a sacrificial animal with the value, (2) buying food and giving charity (half sa' wheat per poor person or sa' of dates/barley), (3) fasting one day per half sa' of wheat equivalency.
If leftover less than half sa', can still give charity or fast one full day.
4
Identify the dalil
The scholar cites Quran 5:95 and a hadith about ostrich eggs, plus Ibn Abbas' interpretation.
The verse commands an equivalent judged by two just persons; the Hanafis interpret 'equivalent' to include value.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani differs: he requires the specific animal equivalent, not monetary valuation and options. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the one given here.
This is a legitimate scholarly difference within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الصيد
وَالْجُزَاءُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ أَنْ يُقَوَّمَ الصَّيْدُ فِي الْمَكَانِ الَّذِي قَتَلَهُ فِيهِ أَوْ فِي أَقْرَبِ الْمَوَاضِعِ إِلَيْهِ إِنْ كَانَ فِي بَرِّيَّةٍ يُقَوَمُهُ ذَوَا عَدْلٍ ثُم هُوَ مُخَيَّرٌ فِي الْقِيمَةِ إِنْ شَاءَ ابْتَاعَ بِمَا هَدْيًا وَإِنْ شَاءَ اشْتَرَى بِهِ طَعَامًا فَتَصَدَّقَ بِهِ عَلَى كُلِّ مِسْكِينٍ بِنِصْفِ صَاعِ مِنْ بُرٍ أَوْ صَاعِ مِنْ تَمرٍ أَوْ شَعِيرٍ وَإِنْ شَاءَ صَامَ عَنْ كُلِّ نِصْفِ صَاعِ مِنْ بُرٍ يَوْمًا وَعَنْ كُلِّ صَاعَ مِنْ تَرِ أَوْ شَعِيرٍ يَوْمًا
فَإِنْ فَضَلَ مِنْ الطَّعَامِ أَقَلُّ مِنْ نِصْفِ صَاعٍ فَهُوَ مُخَيَّرٌ إِنْ شَاءَ تَصَدَّقَ بِهِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ صَامَ عَنْهُ يَوْمًا كَامِلا
وجه : (۳) قول التابعى لثبوت وَإِنْ قَتَلَ الْمُحْرِمُ صَيْدًا قال مالك . . . أَوْ يَحْلِقُ عَنْ شَجَّةٍ فِي رَأْسِهِ لِضَرُورَةِ، أَوْ يَحْلِقُ قَفَاهُ لِمَوْضِعِ الْمَحَاجِمِ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ، نَاسِيًا أَوْ جَاهِلًا: إِنَّ مَنْ فَعَلَ شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْفِدْيَةُ فِي ذَلِكَ كُلِهِ. (المؤطا لإمام مالك: بَابُ فِدْيَةِ مَنْ حَلَقَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَنْحَرَ: 239) وجه: (ا) الأية لثبوت وَالجَزَاء عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ ، يَأَيُّهَا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا لَا تَقْتُلُوا الصَّيْدَ وَأَنتُمْ حُرُم وَمَن قَتَلَهُ مِنكُم مُّتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاءُ مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَمِ يَحْكُمُ بِهِ، ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِّنكُمْ ﴾ (القرآن سورة المائدة، 5 نمبر: 95)
و
وجه: (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَالْجَزَاء عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ \ عَنْ كَعْبِ بْنِ عُجْرَةَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَضَى فِي بَيْضِ نَعَامِ أَصَابَهُ مُحْرِمٌ بِقَدْرِ ثَمَنِهِ». (سنن الدار قطني: كِتَابُ الحج، نمبر: 2550/ سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ بِيضِ النَّعَامَةِ يُصِيبُهَا الْمُحْرِمُ، نمبر: 10021)
وجه : (۱)تفسير عباس لثبوت ثُمَّ هُوَ مُخَيَّرٌ فِي الْقِيمَةِ إِنْ شَاءَ ابْتَاعَ بِمَا هَدْيَا عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ فِي قَوْلِهِ: فَجَزَاءً مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَمِ} [المائدة: 95] قَالَ: "إِذَا أَصَابَ الْمُحْرِمُ الصَّيْدَ يُحْكَمُ عَلَيْهِ جَزَاؤُهُ فَإِنْ كَانَ عِنْدَهُ جَزَاؤُهُ ذَبَحَهُ وَتَصَدَّقَ بِلَحْمِهِ فَإِنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ عِندَهُ جَزَاؤُهُ قُوْمَ جَزَاؤُهُ دَرَاهِمَ. ثُمَّ قُوَّمَتِ الدَّرَاهِمُ طَعَامًا فَصَامَ مَكَانَ كُلَّ نِصْفِ صَاعٍ يَوْمًا وَإِنَّمَا أُرِيدَ بِالطَّعَامِ الصِّيَامُ أَنَّهُ إِذَا وَجَدَ الطَّعَامَ وَجَدَ جَزَاءَهُ (سنن للبيهقي: بَابُ مَنْ عَدَلَ صِيَامَ يَوْمٍ بِمُدَّيْن مِنْ طَعَامِ: 9898) اصول: شکار کی محافظت برباد کر ناخواہ کسی بھی حال میں ہو اس سے دم لازم ہوتا ہے ، خواہ از خود شکار کرے یا شکاری کی رہبری کر کے یہ کام کرے۔
Chapter on hunting. The penalty according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf is that the game is evaluated in the place where he killed it or in the nearest place to it; if it is in a wilderness, two just persons evaluate it. Then he has a choice regarding the value: if he wishes, he may purchase with it a sacrificial animal; if he wishes, he may purchase food with it and give it in charity, giving to each poor person half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or barley; and if he wishes, he may fast for each half sa' of wheat one day, and for each sa' of dates or barley one day. If there remains of the food less than half a sa', he has a choice: if he wishes, he may give it in charity, and if he wishes, he may fast for it one complete day. Proof (3): Statement of the Tabi'i to establish... (Malik’s Muwatta, Bab Fidyah). Proof (1): The verse to establish the penalty according to Abu Hanifa: 'O you who believe, do not kill game while you are in a state of ihram, and whoever of you kills it intentionally, then the penalty is an equivalent of what he killed from livestock, judged by two just persons among you...' (Quran 5:95). Proof (2): The hadith to establish the penalty according to Abu Hanifa: From Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged regarding ostrich eggs which a muhrim struck by its price. Proof (1): The interpretation of Ibn Abbas to establish that he has a choice regarding the value: if he wishes, he may purchase with it a sacrificial animal... (Sunan al-Bayhaqi). Principle: Destroying the protection of game, even unintentionally, necessitates a blood penalty, whether he himself hunts or guides a hunter.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school on the penalty (jaza') for a muhrim who kills game. It presents the position of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf. The key point is that the penalty is determined by evaluating the game at the location of the killing by two just persons. The muhrim then has three options: (1) use the value to buy a sacrificial animal (hady) and sacrifice it in the Haram, (2) purchase food grains and give half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates/barley to each poor person, or (3) fast one day for each half sa' of wheat equivalency. If the value is less than half a sa', he can either give it as charity or fast one full day. The proofs include the Quranic command (5:95), a hadith about ostrich eggs, and the interpretation of Ibn Abbas. The Urdu note adds the principle that destroying game requires a blood penalty in all circumstances. Note: The text also includes a stray Maliki reference (proof 3) which is likely a footnote. The position of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani differs, as he requires specific equivalent animals (see next lesson). The relied-upon position for fatwa is the one given here.

Key Terms
الجزاء (al-jazā'): The penalty required from a muhrim who kills game, which can be sacrificial animal, charity, or fasting.
المحرم (al-muḥrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
القيمة (al-qīmah): Monetary value of the game as determined by two just persons at the place of killing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is the first option for a muhrim who kills game?
A) Pay the equivalent animal
B) Purchase a sacrificial animal with the value
C) Fast for ten days
D) No penalty

Key Takeaway
The penalty for a muhrim who kills game is wajib and is determined by valuation, with three options: sacrifice, charity, or fasting.

Game Penalties, Injuries, and Exemptions in Ihram
Rulings on game penalties, injuries, egg breaking, and exemptions with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on specific animal equivalents for game penalties, apply the rule for injuries to game, and identify which animals are exempt from penalty.

Core Idea
For game with an equivalent, Muhammad requires the exact animal; the relied-upon position is valuation.

In this passage, we encounter Imam Muhammad's detailed list of animal equivalents for penalties when a muhrim kills game. This position contrasts with the majority Hanafi view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The passage also covers compensation for partial injuries to game, full value for incapacitation, egg breaking, and the important exemption for harmful animals. We will work through each ruling and the proofs adduced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on animal penalties
Note that Muhammad's position requires a specific animal for each game species, while Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow valuation and options (sacrifice, charity, fasting). Determine which is mufta bihi.
The mufta bihi is the valuation position.
2
Distinguish partial injury from total incapacitation
For wounds, hair plucking, or limb cutting, only the decrease in value is owed. If the injury renders the game unable to escape (e.g., plucking feathers, cutting legs), the full value must be paid.
The key is whether the game leaves 'حيز الامتناع' (state of being able to escape).
3
Apply the egg-breaking rule
Breaking an egg requires paying its value. If a dead chick emerges, the value of a live chick must be paid.
The proof is a hadith from Aisha and a judgment of the Prophet.
4
List the exempted harmful animals
The passage lists crow, kite, dog, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse – all may be killed without penalty. The basis is the hadith of five fasiq animals.
The hadith is cited from Bukhari and Muslim.
5
Evaluate the proofs for each ruling
Check the type of proof: hadith (ahad), qawl sahabi. Note the thubut (zanni) and dalala (qati) where appropriate.
The hadith of Jabir is ahad; the hadith of five animals is mutawatir in meaning.

Source Text

ه وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَجِبُ فِي الصَّيْدِ النَّظِيرُ فِيمَا لَهُ نَظِيرُ فَفِي الشَّي شَاةٌ وَفِي الصَّبْعِ شَاةٌ وَفِي الْأَرْتَبِ عَنَاقٌ وَفِي النَّعَامَةِ بَدَنَةٌ وَفِي الْيَرْبُوع جَفْرَةٌ وَفِي حِمَارِ الْوَحْشِ بَقَرَةٌ
ل وَمَنْ جَرَحَ صَيْدًا أَوْ نَتَفَ شَعْرَهُ أَوْ قَطَعَ عُضْوًا مِنْهُ ضَمِنَ مَا نَقَصَ مِنْ قِيمَتِهِ ك وَإِنْ نَتَفَ رِيشَ طَائِرٍ أَوْ قَطَعَ قَوَائِمَ صَيْدٍ فَخَرَجَ مِنْ حَيْزِ الِامْتِنَاعِ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ كَامِلَةً وَمَنْ كَسَرَ بَيْضَ صَيْدٍ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ فَإِنْ خَرَجَ مِنْ الْبَيْضَةِ فَرْخٌ مَيِّتٌ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ حَيًّا
و وَلَيْسَ فِي قَتْلِ الْغُرَابِ وَالْحِدَأَةِ وَالْكَلْبِ وَالذِنْبِ وَالخَيَّةِ وَالْعَقْرَبِ وَالْفَأْرَةِ جَزَاءً د. وجه : (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَجِبُ فِي الصَّيْدِ اعَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَضَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ «فِي الظَّيْ شَاةً, وَفِي الصَّبْع كَبْشًا, وَفِي الْأَرْتَبِ عَنَافًا وَفِي الْيَرْبُوعِ جَفْرَةً» . فَقُلْتُ لِابْنِ الزُّبَيْرِ: وَمَا الْخَفْرَةُ؟ قَالَ: الَّتِي قَدْ قُطِمَتْ وَرَعَتْ (سنن الدار قطني : كِتَابُ الحَجّ،: 2549/) د. وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ جَرَحَ صَيْدًا أَوْ نَتَفَ شَعْرَهُ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «فِي بَيْضَةِ نَعَامِ كَسَرَهُ رَجُلٌ مُحرِم صِيَامُ يَوْمٍ فِي كُلِّ بَيْضَةِ» (سنن الدار قطني : كِتَابُ الحَجَ : 2560)
ى وجه (۱) قول الصحابى لثبوت وَإِنْ نَتَفَ رِيشَ طَائِرِ \ عَنْ طَارِقٍ أَنَّ أَرْبَدَ أَوْطَأَ ضَبًّا فَفَزَرَ ظَهْرَهُ, فَأَتَى عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ فَسَأَلَهُ فَقَالَ عُمَرُ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ: "مَا تَرَى؟" فَقَالَ: جَدْيَا قَدْ جَمَعَ الْمَاءَ وَالشَّجَرَ, فَقَالَ عُمَرُ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ: "فَذَلِكَ فِيهِ" (سنن للبيهقي : بَابُ فِدْيَةِ الصّبِ،: 9890) دوجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ كَسَرَبَيْضَ صَيْدٍ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ عَنْ كَعْبِ بْنِ عُجْرَةَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى
اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَضَى فِي بَيْضِ نَعَامِ أَصَابَهُ مُحْرِمٌ بِقَدْرِثْنِهِ» (الدارقطني: كِتَابُ الحَجَ: 2550) و. وجه: (ا) الحديث لثبوت وَلَيْسَ فِي قَتْلِ الْغُرَابِ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: " خَمْسٌ مِنَ الدَّوَاتِ، كُلُّهُنَّ فَاسِقٌ، يَقْتُلُهُنَّ فِي الْحَرَمِ الغُرَابُ، وَالحِدَأَةُ، وَالعَقْرَبُ، وَالفَأْرَةُ، وَالكَلْبُ العَقُورُ " (بخاري): بَابُ مَا يَقْتُلُ المُحْرِمُ مِنَ الدَّوَابِ، غير : 1829/ مسلم : بَابُ مَا يَنْدُبُ لِلْمُحْرِمِ وَغَيْرِهِ قَتْلَهُ مِنَ الدَّوَاتِ فِي الْحِلِ وَالْحَرَمِ، نمبر: 1198) لغات: فرخ مرده بچه، طبية : گابھن ہرن، الْغُرَابِ کوا، الْحَدَأَةِ: چیل، الذنْبِ: بھیڑیا، الحيَّة: سانپ، الْعَقْرَبِ : بچھو، الْفَارَةِ : چوہا، الْكَلْبِ الْعَقُورِ: باولا كتا،
And Muhammad said: For game, the equivalent is obligatory for that which has an equivalent: for the gazelle, a sheep; for the hyena, a sheep; for the rabbit, a ewe lamb; for the ostrich, a camel; for the jerboa, a young goat; for the wild ass, a cow. And whoever wounds game, or plucks its hair, or cuts a limb from it, must guarantee the decrease in its value. And if he plucks the feathers of a bird, or cuts the legs of game so that it leaves the state of being able to escape, then he must pay its full value. And whoever breaks the egg of game must pay its value; if a dead chick comes out of the egg, he must pay its value when alive. And there is no penalty in killing the crow, the kite, the dog, the wolf, the snake, the scorpion, and the mouse. Proof (1): The hadith to establish what Muhammad said: from Jabir who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) judged: 'For the gazelle, a sheep; for the hyena, a ram; for the rabbit, a ewe lamb; for the jerboa, a young goat.' I asked Ibn al-Zubayr: 'What is al-jafrah?' He said: 'That which has weaned and grazed.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, no. 2549) Proof (1): The hadith to establish 'whoever wounds game or plucks its hair': from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'For an ostrich egg broken by a muhrim, fasting one day for each egg.' (Sunan al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, no. 2560) Proof (1): The statement of the Companion to establish 'if he plucks the feathers of a bird': from Tariq that Arbad trod on a dabb lizard and split its back, so he came to Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) and asked him. Umar said: 'What do you think?' He said: 'A young goat that has gathered water and trees.' So Umar said: 'That is for it.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab Fidyah al-Dabb, no. 9890) Proof (1): The hadith to establish 'whoever breaks the egg of game must pay its value': from Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah that the Prophet (peace be upon him) judged regarding ostrich eggs which a muhrim struck by its price. (Al-Daraqutni, Kitab al-Hajj, no. 2550) Proof (1): The hadith to establish 'there is no penalty in killing the crow': from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Five are harmful animals, all of them are sinful, they are killed in the Haram: the crow, the kite, the scorpion, the mouse, and the vicious dog.' (Bukhari, Bab ma yaqtul al-muhrim min al-dawab, no. 1829; Muslim, Bab ma yundabu lil-muhrim wa ghayrihi qatlahu min al-dawab, no. 1198) Vocabulary: dead chick, pregnant gazelle, crow, kite, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse, mad dog.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage contains multiple rulings. First, it presents Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's opinion that for game with an equivalent animal, the penalty is that specific animal (e.g., a sheep for a gazelle, a camel for an ostrich). This contrasts with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's valuation system. Second, it covers injuries to game: if one wounds, plucks hair, or cuts a limb, he pays the decrease in value. If the injury makes the game incapable of escape (e.g., plucking feathers or cutting legs), he pays full value. Breaking an egg requires its value; if a dead chick emerges, he pays the value of a live chick. Third, it lists harmful animals (crow, kite, dog, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse) for which there is no penalty, citing the hadith of the five fasiq animals. The proofs include hadith from Jabir (specific animals), Aisha (egg breaking), Umar's judgment (lizard case), and the well-known hadith on the five harmful animals. The Urdu gloss provides translations of animal names.

Key Terms
النظير (al-naẓīr): The equivalent animal that must be given as penalty for killing game in ihram.
جفرة (jafrah): A young goat that has weaned and begun grazing, used as penalty for jerboa.
الغراب (al-ghurāb): Crow, one of the harmful animals that may be killed without penalty in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Crow
C) Rabbit
D) Hyena

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school offers flexibility in game penalties through valuation, while the harmful animals exemption is based on clear prophetic guidance.

Compensation for Game Animals: Imam Muhammad's Ruling
Ruling on compensation for specific game animals with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle of compensation by mithl (equivalent animal) and list the specific compensations for six game animals as per Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
Compensation for game is by like (nazir) when available; specific animals have fixed equivalents.

When a muhrim (pilgrim in ihram) kills game animals, the Qur'an and Sunnah require compensation (jaza'). This lesson presents the Hanafi view as recorded by Imam Muhammad in the zahir al-riwayah sources. The general rule is that compensation should be an equivalent animal (al-nazir) when one exists. For the specific animals listed, the school has fixed the exact type of animal to be offered as expiation, based on the Prophet's judgment and analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
Imam Muhammad declares: 'Compensation for game is an equivalent (nazir) when a like exists.' This means the exact same species or a similar domesticated animal is wajib.
The principle is derived from the general obligation of jaza' (Quran 5:95) and the Prophet's specific judgments.
2
Memorize the six animals and their compensations
Learn the following pairs: deer → sheep, hyena → sheep, hare → young she-goat (anaq), ostrich → camel (badanah), jerboa → jafrah (weaned sheep/goat), wild donkey → cow.
Use mnemonics or flashcards. Note that deer and hyena both require a sheep, but other animals have distinct compensations.
3
Identify the hadith proof
The hadith from Jabir records the Prophet's judgment for four of these animals. It is a hadith ahad, making both thubut and dalala zanni, but it is accepted as proof in the Hanafi school.
Imam Muhammad's list is slightly broader than the hadith; he adds ostrich and wild donkey through other evidence or qiyas.
4
Understand the cross-madhhab perspective
The Shafi'i school generally allows compensation either by mithl (like) or value (qeemah), giving the offender a choice. The Hanafi school insists on mithl when it exists, as per the principle of nazir.
This difference illustrates the Hanafi commitment to textual analogy over flexibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الصيد وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَجِبُ فِي الصَّيْدِ النَّظِيرُ فِيمَا لَهُ نَظِيرُ فَفِي الشَّي شَاةٌ وَفِي الصَّبْعِ شَاةٌ وَفِي الْأَرْتَبِ عَنَاقٌ وَفِي النَّعَامَةِ بَدَنَةٌ وَفِي الْيَرْبُوع جَفْرَةٌ وَفِي حِمَارِ الْوَحْشِ بَقَرَةٌ. عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَضَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ «فِي الظَّيْ شَاةً, وَفِي الصَّبْع كَبْشًا, وَفِي الْأَرْتَبِ عَنَافًا وَفِي الْيَرْبُوعِ جَفْرَةً».
Chapter on hunting. Muhammad said: The compensation for game is a like (equivalent) in what has a like. For the deer: a sheep, for the hyena: a sheep, for the hare: a young she-goat, for the ostrich: a camel, for the jerboa: a jafrah (weaned sheep), for the wild donkey: a cow. From Jabir, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) judged regarding the deer: a sheep, for the hyena: a ram, for the hare: a young she-goat, and for the jerboa: a jafrah.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Imam Muhammad on the compensation (jaza') for different types of game animals when a muhrim kills them while in ihram. The general principle is that compensation should be an equivalent animal (al-nazir) when one exists. The specific animals listed are: deer (zabi), hyena (dhab'), rabbit (arnab), ostrich (na'amah), jerboa (yarbu'), and wild donkey (himar al-wahsh). For each, Imam Muhammad specifies the required compensation: a sheep for deer and hyena, a young she-goat (anaq) for rabbit, a camel (badanah) for ostrich, a jafrah (a weaned sheep or goat) for jerboa, and a cow for wild donkey. The supporting hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah mentions the Prophet's judgement for deer (sheep), hyena (ram), hare (anaq), and jerboa (jafrah). Note that the hadith does not mention ostrich or wild donkey; Imam Muhammad's compensation for those is based on other evidence or qiyas. The compensation is wajib (obligatory) for the muhrim who kills these game animals.

Key Terms
النَّظِير (al-nazir): The equivalent animal in form and value for compensation (jaza') of game.
جَفْرَة (jafrah): A young sheep or goat that has been weaned and has started grazing.
بَدَنَة (badanah): A camel; used as a sacrificial animal.
عَنَاق (anaq): A young she-goat that has not yet given birth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the compensation for killing an ostrich while in ihram?
A) A sheep
B) A cow
C) A camel
D) A young she-goat

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires compensation for game by a like animal when available, as specified by Imam Muhammad for six types of game.

Compensation for Injuring Game Animals in Ihram
Rulings on compensation for various injuries to game while in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the compensation rules for partial and total injury to game by a muhrim, apply the threshold of hayz al-imtina', and explain the proof-based difference on egg compensation.

Core Idea
Compensation for injuring game in ihram is based on decrease in value; full value is due if the animal loses its ability to escape.

A pilgrim in ihram may accidentally injure game. Islamic law prescribes specific compensations (jaza') to restore the value lost. This lesson unpacks three scenarios: partial damage, full loss (when the animal can no longer escape), and egg breaking. We also examine the proofs, including a difference on whether to pay value or fast for broken eggs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage covers three types of injury: wounding/plucking/cutting a limb, plucking feathers/cutting legs making escape impossible, and breaking eggs. For each, identify the hukm level: wajib compensation.
The compensation is not a penalty but a replacement of lost value.
2
Determine compensation type for partial injury
For wounds, plucked hair, or cut limb where the animal remains able to escape, the compensation is the decrease in value (ma naqasa min qeematihi). This is estimated by comparing the animal's value before and after injury.
The companion Umar used the example of a kid (jadhy) as an estimate.
3
Apply the threshold of hayz al-imtina'
If the injury (e.g., plucking feathers of a bird, cutting legs of a quadruped) renders the animal incapable of escape, full value is due. This is because the animal is now effectively dead or lost; its value is fully compensated.
Hayz al-imtina' means the state from which escape is possible.
4
Analyze egg compensation
Breaking an egg of game requires payment of its value. If a dead chick emerges, pay the value the chick would have if alive (i.e., its market value as living). This is distinct from the injury to a hatched animal.
The hadith of Aisha mentions fasting for each egg, but the Hanafi school prefers value based on other evidence.
5
Examine the supporting proofs
The text cites three proofs: (1) Hadith of Aisha on fasting for ostrich egg, (2) Incident of Umar and a crushed lizard (dabb) where a kid was assigned as compensation, (3) Hadith of Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah that the Prophet judged value for ostrich eggs. The Hanafi position relies on the latter and qiyas.
The difference on egg compensation is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ جَرَحَ صَيْدًا أَوْ نَتَفَ شَعْرَهُ أَوْ قَطَعَ عُضْوًا مِنْهُ ضَمِنَ مَا نَقَصَ مِنْ قِيمَتِهِ. وَإِنْ نَتَفَ رِيشَ طَائِرٍ أَوْ قَطَعَ قَوَائِمَ صَيْدٍ فَخَرَجَ مِنْ حَيْزِ الِامْتِنَاعِ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ كَامِلَةً. وَمَنْ كَسَرَ بَيْضَ صَيْدٍ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ فَإِنْ خَرَجَ مِنْ الْبَيْضَةِ فَرْخٌ مَيِّتٌ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ حَيًّا. عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «فِي بَيْضَةِ نَعَامِ كَسَرَهُ رَجُلٌ مُحرِم صِيَامُ يَوْمٍ فِي كُلِّ بَيْضَةِ» . عَنْ طَارِقٍ أَنَّ أَرْبَدَ أَوْطَأَ ضَبًّا فَفَزَرَ ظَهْرَهُ, فَأَتَى عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ فَسَأَلَهُ فَقَالَ عُمَرُ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ: "مَا تَرَى؟" فَقَالَ: جَدْيَا قَدْ جَمَعَ الْمَاءَ وَالشَّجَرَ, فَقَالَ عُمَرُ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ: "فَذَلِكَ فِيهِ". عَنْ كَعْبِ بْنِ عُجْرَةَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَضَى فِي بَيْضِ نَعَامِ أَصَابَهُ مُحْرِمٌ بِقَدْرِ ثَمَنِهِ.
Whoever wounds a game animal, or plucks its hair, or cuts off a limb from it, he is liable for the decrease in its value. If he plucks the feathers of a bird or cuts the legs of a game animal so that it leaves its habitat of escape, then he must pay its full value. Whoever breaks an egg of game must pay its value. If a dead chick comes out of the egg, he must pay its value alive. Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, reported that the Messenger of Allah said: 'For an ostrich egg broken by a muhrim, fasting one day for each egg.' From Tariq that Arbad stepped on a lizard and crushed its back, so he came to Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, and asked him. Umar said: 'What do you think?' He said: 'A young goat that has gathered water and trees.' Umar said: 'Then that is due for it.' From Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah that the Prophet judged regarding ostrich eggs which a muhrim damaged: payment of their value.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage details the compensation (jaza') for non-lethal injuries to game while in ihram. There are three scenarios. First: if a person wounds a game animal, plucks its hair, or cuts a limb, the animal remains alive but its value has decreased. The compensation is the amount of that decrease (ma naqasa min qeematihi). Second: if the action (plucking feathers of a bird or cutting the legs of quadruped game) renders the animal unable to escape (kharaja min hayz al-imtina'), it is considered as if the animal is no longer capable of self-defense; therefore, the full value of the animal is due. Third: breaking an egg of game requires payment of the egg's value. If a dead chick emerges, the payer must pay the value the chick would have had if alive (i.e., its market value as a living chick). The supporting narrations: from Aisha regarding an ostrich egg: the Prophet said fasting one day for each egg - this shows an alternative compensation (fasting) for egg breaking, though the matn says value (qeemah); this is a difference in proofs. The Hanafi ruling of value is based on other evidence and qiyas. The narration from Umar regarding a lizard (dabb): Umar determined a young goat as compensation, showing the principle of estimating the decrease. From Ka'b ibn 'Ujrah: the Prophet judged value for ostrich eggs, which directly supports the matn.

Key Terms
حَيْزِ الِامْتِنَاعِ (hayz al-imtina'): The state or domain from which the animal is capable of escaping or defending itself.
جَدْي (jadhy): A young goat (kid) that has started grazing but is not yet fully grown.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim cuts the legs of a deer so that it cannot stand, how much compensation is due?
A) The decrease in value
B) The full value of the deer
C) A sheep
D) Fasting one day

Key Takeaway
In ihram, compensation for non-lethal injury to game is wajib; it equals the decrease in value for partial injury and full value when escape ability is lost; egg breakage requires value, but a valid difference exists with fasting.

The Five Harmful Animals (Fawasiq) and No Compensation
Ruling on exempt harmful animals with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five fawasiq and explain why killing them in ihram incurs no compensation, including the Hanafi extension by analogy.

Core Idea
The five fawasiq are exempt from compensation; Hanafi extends to other harmful animals by qiyas.

This lesson examines the hadith of Aisha listing five harmful animals (fawasiq) that may be killed in ihram without penalty. The Hanafi school extends this exemption by analogy to include other harmful creatures like the wolf and snake, while other schools restrict to the five mentioned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is killing certain harmful animals while in ihram. The ruling is that no compensation (jaza') is due.
This is a permission (ibaha) with no penalty.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Aisha: 'Five harmful creatures... are killed in the sanctuary.' This hadith is mutawatir in meaning.
Hadith reference: Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's explicit permission to kill these animals in the haram indicates that killing them does not incur sin or compensation. The absence of any mention of fidyah implies no obligation.
The imperative 'yuqtalna' (they are killed) is interpreted as permission.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school restricts the exemption to the five animals mentioned. The Hanafi school extends it by qiyas to other harmful animals like the wolf and snake because they share the illa of harm.
The Hanafi inclusion of 'dog' in the list includes all harmful dogs, not just the 'aqur'.
5
Apply the ruling
The exempt animals include crow, kite, scorpion, mouse, ferocious dog, and by analogy wolf, snake, and other harmful creatures. Also, mosquitoes, ants, etc. are included as they are not game.
The text also lists mosquito, ant, flea, tick with no compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ فِي قَتْلِ الْغُرَابِ وَالْحِدَأَةِ وَالْكَلْبِ وَالذِنْبِ وَالخَيَّةِ وَالْعَقْرَبِ وَالْفَأْرَةِ جَزَاءً. عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: "خَمْسٌ مِنَ الدَّوَاتِ، كُلُّهُنَّ فَاسِقٌ، يَقْتُلُهُنَّ فِي الْحَرَمِ الغُرَابُ، وَالحِدَأَةُ، وَالعَقْرَبُ، وَالفَأْرَةُ، وَالكَلْبُ العَقُورُ". وَلَيْسَ فِي قَتْلِ الْبَعُوضِ وَالنَّمْلِ وَالْبَرَاغِيثِ وَالْقُرَادِ شَيْءٌ. قَالَ مَالِكٌ... أَوْ يَحْلِقُ عَنْ شَجَّةٍ فِي رَأْسِهِ لِضَرُورَةِ، أَوْ يَحْلِقُ قَفَاهُ لِمَوْضِعِ الْمَحَاجِمِ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ، نَاسِيًا أَوْ جَاهِلًا: إِنَّ مَنْ فَعَلَ شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْفِدْيَةُ فِي ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ. وَمَنْ قَتَلَ قَمْلَةً تَصَدَّقَ بِمَا شَاءَ. عَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ، أَنَّ رَجُلًا جَاءَ إِلَى عُمَرَ بْن الْخَطَّابِ، فَقَالَ: يَا أَمِيرَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ. إِنِّي أَصَبْتُ جَرَادَاتٍ بِسَوْطِي وَأَنَا مُحْرِمٌ. فَقَالَ لَهُ عُمَرُ : «أَطْعِمْ قَبْضَةً مِنْ طَعَامٍ» . . . . فَقَالَ عُمَرُ لِكَعْبِ: «إِنَّكَ لَتَجِدُ الدَّرَاهِمَ، لَتَمْرَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جَرَادَةٍ». وَمَنْ قَتَلَ جَرَادَةً تَصَدَّقَ بِمَا شَاءَ وَتَمَرَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جَرَادَةٍ. عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَضَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي الطَّيِ شَاةَ, وَفِي الصَّبُعِ كَبْشًا, وَفِي الْأَرْتَبِ عَنَاقًا, وَفِي الْيَرْبُوعِ جَفْرَةً. وَمَنْ قَتَلَ مَا لَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ مِنْ الصَّيْدِ كَالسَّبَاعِ وَتَرَكَهَا فَعَلَيْهِ الْجُزَاءُ لَا يَتَجَاوَزُ بِقِيمَتِهَا شَاةً. وَإِنْ صَالَ السَّبْعُ عَلَى مُحْرِمٍ فَقَتَلَهُ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ. عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: "خَمْسٌ مِنَ الدَّوَاتِ، كُلُّهُنَّ فَاسِقٌ يَقْتُلُهُنَّ فِي الحَرَمِ الغُرَابُ، وَالحِدَأَةُ وَالعَقْرَبُ، وَالفَأْرَةُ، وَالكَلْبُ العَقُورُ". عَنْ عَطَاءٍ قَالَ: «كُلُّ عَدُوٍّ عَدَا عَلَيْكَ، فَاقْتُلْهُ وَأَنْتَ مُحْرِمٌ».
And there is no compensation for killing the crow, kite, dog, wolf, snake, scorpion, and mouse. Aisha reported that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Five harmful creatures, all of them are corrupt, they are killed in the sacred precinct: the crow, the kite, the scorpion, the mouse, and the ferocious dog.' And there is nothing for killing the mosquito, ant, flea, and tick. Malik said: '... or shave from a wound on his head due to necessity, or shave the back of his neck for the place of cupping while he is in ihram, forgetful or ignorant: whoever does any of that owes a fidyah in all of that.' And whoever kills a louse gives charity as he wishes. From Zayd ibn Aslam that a man came to Umar ibn al-Khattab and said: 'O Commander of the Faithful, I struck locusts with my whip while I was in ihram.' Umar said: 'Feed a handful of food...' Then Umar said to Ka'b: 'You find dirhams? A date is better than a locust.' And whoever kills a locust gives charity as he wishes, and a date is better than a locust. From Jabir: the Prophet judged for a deer a sheep, for a hyena a ram, for a hare a young she-goat, for a jerboa a jafrah. And whoever kills inedible game like predators and leaves them, then upon him is the compensation, not exceeding its value of a sheep. And if a predator attacks a muhrim and he kills it, then nothing is upon him. From Aisha: the Prophet said: 'Five harmful creatures...'. From 'Ata: 'Every enemy that attacks you, kill it while you are in ihram.'
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage covers a range of rulings regarding the permissibility of killing certain creatures in ihram without incurring compensation (jaza'). The first list (crow, kite, dog, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse) are exempt from compensation based on the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet allowed killing five harmful animals (fawasiq) in the sanctuary. The Hanafi school includes additional animals like the wolf and snake by analogy (qiyas) because they are harmful. The second list (mosquito, ant, flea, tick) also require no compensation, likely because they are not considered game and cause nuisance. The hadith from Malik (though not a Hanafi source) is cited to show that even for other matters, ignorance or forgetfulness does not remove the fidyah for shaving; this may be a proof that for these small creatures, no fidyah is due. For lice and locusts, the ruling is not a fixed compensation but a recommended charity (sadaqa bil ma shaa) – whatever one wishes. The narration from Umar shows that for locusts, he ordered feeding a handful of food, and the phrase 'a date is better than a locust' indicates that even a small charity suffices. For inedible game (ma la yu'kalu lahmuhu), like predators (siba'), if killed, compensation is due, but it cannot exceed the value of a sheep. This means that for a lion, the maximum compensation is a sheep. Finally, if a predator attacks the muhrim, he may kill it without any compensation, as per the hadith of Aisha and the statement of 'Ata: every enemy that attacks you, kill it. This is self-defense.

Key Terms
الْفَوَاسِق (al-fawasiq): Harmful animals that are permitted to be killed in ihram and in the haram without compensation.
لَا يَتَجَاوَزُ بِقِيمَتِهَا شَاةً (la yatajawazu bi qeematiha shatan): The compensation for inedible game is value but not exceeding the value of a sheep.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Crow
B) Wolf
C) Scorpion
D) Mouse

Key Takeaway
The five fawasiq are exempt from compensation; Hanafi extends the exemption to other harmful animals by qiyas.

Charity for Killing Lice and Locusts in Ihram
Ruling on voluntary charity for lice and locusts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended charity for killing a louse or locust in ihram and differentiate it from wajib compensation.

Core Idea
Killing a louse or locust in ihram requires voluntary charity, not fixed compensation.

This lesson covers the ruling for killing lice and locusts while in ihram. Unlike larger game, there is no fixed penalty; rather, the pilgrim is encouraged to give charity as he wishes. The narration from Umar ibn al-Khattab illustrates that even a date suffices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is killing a louse or locust while in ihram. The ruling is that one should give charity (sadaqa) voluntarily, not a fixed compensation.
This is a recommended act (mustahabb), not wajib.
2
Locate the evidence
The text states: 'And whoever kills a louse gives charity as he wishes.' The narration of Umar with a man who killed locusts shows Umar ordered 'feed a handful of food' and later said 'a date is better than a locust.'
There is no explicit hadith, but the practice of the Companions.
3
Understand the discretionary nature
The amount is not fixed; one gives what he wishes. The example of a date shows minimal charity suffices.
This contrasts with wajib fidyah for other violations.
4
Distinguish from other rulings
Killing lice/locusts is not comparable to killing game; it is a minor nuisance. Hence, only charity, not compensation.
The Hanafi school sees this as a recommended charity, not an obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَيْسَ فِي قَتْلِ الْغُرَابِ وَالْحِدَأَةِ وَالْكَلْبِ وَالذِنْبِ وَالخَيَّةِ وَالْعَقْرَبِ وَالْفَأْرَةِ جَزَاءً. عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: "خَمْسٌ مِنَ الدَّوَاتِ، كُلُّهُنَّ فَاسِقٌ، يَقْتُلُهُنَّ فِي الْحَرَمِ الغُرَابُ، وَالحِدَأَةُ، وَالعَقْرَبُ، وَالفَأْرَةُ، وَالكَلْبُ العَقُورُ". وَلَيْسَ فِي قَتْلِ الْبَعُوضِ وَالنَّمْلِ وَالْبَرَاغِيثِ وَالْقُرَادِ شَيْءٌ. قَالَ مَالِكٌ... أَوْ يَحْلِقُ عَنْ شَجَّةٍ فِي رَأْسِهِ لِضَرُورَةِ، أَوْ يَحْلِقُ قَفَاهُ لِمَوْضِعِ الْمَحَاجِمِ وَهُوَ مُحْرِمٌ، نَاسِيًا أَوْ جَاهِلًا: إِنَّ مَنْ فَعَلَ شَيْئًا مِنْ ذَلِكَ فَعَلَيْهِ الْفِدْيَةُ فِي ذَلِكَ كُلِّهِ. وَمَنْ قَتَلَ قَمْلَةً تَصَدَّقَ بِمَا شَاءَ. عَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ أَسْلَمَ، أَنَّ رَجُلًا جَاءَ إِلَى عُمَرَ بْن الْخَطَّابِ، فَقَالَ: يَا أَمِيرَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ. إِنِّي أَصَبْتُ جَرَادَاتٍ بِسَوْطِي وَأَنَا مُحْرِمٌ. فَقَالَ لَهُ عُمَرُ : «أَطْعِمْ قَبْضَةً مِنْ طَعَامٍ» . . . . فَقَالَ عُمَرُ لِكَعْبِ: «إِنَّكَ لَتَجِدُ الدَّرَاهِمَ، لَتَمْرَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جَرَادَةٍ». وَمَنْ قَتَلَ جَرَادَةً تَصَدَّقَ بِمَا شَاءَ وَتَمَرَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جَرَادَةٍ. عَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَضَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي الطَّيِ شَاةَ, وَفِي الصَّبُعِ كَبْشًا, وَفِي الْأَرْتَبِ عَنَاقًا, وَفِي الْيَرْبُوعِ جَفْرَةً. وَمَنْ قَتَلَ مَا لَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ مِنْ الصَّيْدِ كَالسَّبَاعِ وَتَرَكَهَا فَعَلَيْهِ الْجُزَاءُ لَا يَتَجَاوَزُ بِقِيمَتِهَا شَاةً. وَإِنْ صَالَ السَّبْعُ عَلَى مُحْرِمٍ فَقَتَلَهُ فَلَا شَيْءَ عَلَيْهِ. عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: "خَمْسٌ مِنَ الدَّوَاتِ، كُلُّهُنَّ فَاسِقٌ يَقْتُلُهُنَّ فِي الحَرَمِ الغُرَابُ، وَالحِدَأَةُ وَالعَقْرَبُ، وَالفَأْرَةُ، وَالكَلْبُ العَقُورُ". عَنْ عَطَاءٍ قَالَ: «كُلُّ عَدُوٍّ عَدَا عَلَيْكَ، فَاقْتُلْهُ وَأَنْتَ مُحْرِمٌ».
And there is no compensation for killing the crow, kite, dog, wolf, snake, scorpion, and mouse. Aisha reported that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Five harmful creatures, all of them are corrupt, they are killed in the sacred precinct: the crow, the kite, the scorpion, the mouse, and the ferocious dog.' And there is nothing for killing the mosquito, ant, flea, and tick. Malik said: '... or shave from a wound on his head due to necessity, or shave the back of his neck for the place of cupping while he is in ihram, forgetful or ignorant: whoever does any of that owes a fidyah in all of that.' And whoever kills a louse gives charity as he wishes. From Zayd ibn Aslam that a man came to Umar ibn al-Khattab and said: 'O Commander of the Faithful, I struck locusts with my whip while I was in ihram.' Umar said: 'Feed a handful of food...' Then Umar said to Ka'b: 'You find dirhams? A date is better than a locust.' And whoever kills a locust gives charity as he wishes, and a date is better than a locust. From Jabir: the Prophet judged for a deer a sheep, for a hyena a ram, for a hare a young she-goat, for a jerboa a jafrah. And whoever kills inedible game like predators and leaves them, then upon him is the compensation, not exceeding its value of a sheep. And if a predator attacks a muhrim and he kills it, then nothing is upon him. From Aisha: the Prophet said: 'Five harmful creatures...'. From 'Ata: 'Every enemy that attacks you, kill it while you are in ihram.'
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage covers a range of rulings regarding the permissibility of killing certain creatures in ihram without incurring compensation (jaza'). The first list (crow, kite, dog, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse) are exempt from compensation based on the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet allowed killing five harmful animals (fawasiq) in the sanctuary. The Hanafi school includes additional animals like the wolf and snake by analogy (qiyas) because they are harmful. The second list (mosquito, ant, flea, tick) also require no compensation, likely because they are not considered game and cause nuisance. The hadith from Malik (though not a Hanafi source) is cited to show that even for other matters, ignorance or forgetfulness does not remove the fidyah for shaving; this may be a proof that for these small creatures, no fidyah is due. For lice and locusts, the ruling is not a fixed compensation but a recommended charity (sadaqa bil ma shaa) – whatever one wishes. The narration from Umar shows that for locusts, he ordered feeding a handful of food, and the phrase 'a date is better than a locust' indicates that even a small charity suffices. For inedible game (ma la yu'kalu lahmuhu), like predators (siba'), if killed, compensation is due, but it cannot exceed the value of a sheep. This means that for a lion, the maximum compensation is a sheep. Finally, if a predator attacks the muhrim, he may kill it without any compensation, as per the hadith of Aisha and the statement of 'Ata: every enemy that attacks you, kill it. This is self-defense.

Key Terms
قَمْلَة (qamla): Louse; a small parasite that may be killed in ihram with recommended charity.
جَرَادَة (jarada): Locust; killing it in ihram requires charity as one wishes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for killing a locust in ihram according to the Hanafi school?
A) Compensation of a sheep
B) Feed a handful of food exactly
C) Give charity as one wishes
D) No action required

Key Takeaway
Killing lice or locusts in ihram only requires voluntary charity, not fixed compensation.

Compensation for Inedible Predators and Self-Defense Exemption
Ruling on compensation for inedible predators and self-defense exemption

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the compensation for killing inedible game (predators) and explain the exemption when the predator attacks.

Core Idea
Killing inedible predators in ihram requires compensation capped at a sheep, but no compensation if in self-defense.

This lesson covers the ruling for killing predators (siba') that are not edible. The general rule is that compensation is wajib, but its value cannot exceed that of a sheep. However, if the predator attacks the muhrim, he may kill it without any penalty. The hadith of Aisha and the statement of 'Ata support this exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is killing an inedible predator (e.g., lion, wolf, hyena) while not in self-defense. The ruling is that compensation is wajib, but its value does not exceed a sheep.
This applies when the predator is not attacking.
2
Locate the dalil
The text states: 'Whoever kills what is not eaten of game like predators, then upon him is the compensation, not exceeding its value of a sheep.' There is also a hadith from Jabir listing compensations for other animals (deer, hyena, etc.) which set precedents.
The cap of a sheep is a Hanafi specific ruling.
3
Understand the cap
The compensation is based on the value of the animal, but it is capped at the value of a sheep. Even if the predator is very large, the maximum is a sheep.
This is a concession to avoid excessive penalties.
4
Note the self-defense exemption
If the predator attacks the muhrim, he may kill it without any compensation. This is from the hadith of Aisha (the five fawasiq) and the statement of 'Ata: 'Every enemy that attacks you, kill it.'
Self-defense takes precedence over prohibition of hunting.

Source Text

And there is no compensation for killing the crow, kite, dog, wolf, snake, scorpion, and mouse. Aisha reported that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Five harmful creatures, all of them are corrupt, they are killed in the sacred precinct: the crow, the kite, the scorpion, the mouse, and the ferocious dog.' And there is nothing for killing the mosquito, ant, flea, and tick. Malik said: '... or shave from a wound on his head due to necessity, or shave the back of his neck for the place of cupping while he is in ihram, forgetful or ignorant: whoever does any of that owes a fidyah in all of that.' And whoever kills a louse gives charity as he wishes. And if a predator attacks a muhrim and he kills it, then nothing is upon him. From Aisha: the Prophet said: 'Five harmful creatures...'. From 'Ata: 'Every enemy that attacks you, kill it while you are in ihram.'

Commentary
This passage covers a range of rulings regarding the permissibility of killing certain creatures in ihram without incurring compensation (jaza'). The first list (crow, kite, dog, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse) are exempt from compensation based on the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet allowed killing five harmful animals (fawasiq) in the sanctuary. The second list (mosquito, ant, flea, tick) also require no compensation, likely because they are not considered game and cause nuisance. The hadith from Malik (though not a Hanafi source) is cited to show that even for other matters, ignorance or forgetfulness does not remove the fidyah for shaving; this may be a proof that for these small creatures, no fidyah is due. Key Terms
سَبُع / سِبَاع (sabu' / siba'): Predator; inedible wild animals like lion, wolf, hyena.
الْجُزَاء (al-jaza'): Compensation for hunting violations in ihram.

Cutting Vegetation of the Haram
Ruling on cutting grass or trees in the Haram with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on cutting unowned vegetation in the Haram and explain the textual proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
Cutting unowned vegetation in the Haram requires paying its value; the Haram's sanctity demands compensation.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling for cutting grass or trees in the Haram (the sacred precinct of Makkah) that are not owned or cultivated by people. The text presents the ruling and supports it with hadith evidence, while also noting the differing view of Imam al-Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is cutting unowned grass or trees in the Haram. The ruling is that the cutter must pay the value (qimah).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is from two hadith: the hadith of Ibn Abbas and the hadith of Abu Shurayh, both prohibiting cutting trees and grass in the Haram.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition in the hadith indicates the unlawfulness of cutting, and the sanctity of the Haram necessitates a compensatory payment (qimah) as a form of dam.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that specific animal compensations apply: a sheep for a small tree, a cow for a large tree.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school relies on the general prohibition and the principle of compensation for violating the sanctity of the Haram, opting for monetary value rather than specific animals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ قَطَعَ حَشِيشَ الْحَرَمِ أَوْ شَجَرَهُ الَّذِي لَيْسَ بِمَمْلُوكٍ وَلا هُوَ مِمَّا يُنْبِتُهُ النَّاسُ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ. وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَا يُعْضَدُ عِضَاهُهَا، وَلَا يُنَفَّرُ صَيْدُهَا، وَلاَ تَحِلُّ لُقَطَتُهَا، إِلَّا لِمُنْشِدٍ، وَلَا يُخْتَلَى خَلاَهَا» فَقَالَ عَبَّاسٌ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، إِلَّا الإِذْخِرَ، فَقَالَ: «إِلَّا الإِذْخِرَ». وَوَجْهُ قَوْلِ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنْ أَبِي شُرَيْحٍ الْعَدَوِيِّ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «...فَلَا يَحِلُّ لِامْرِئٍ يُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ أَنْ يَسْفِكَ بِمَا دَمًا، وَلَا يَعْضُدَ بِمَا شَجَرَةً». وَوَجْهُ قَوْلِ الشَّافِعِيِّ: قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ: مَنْ قَطَعَ مِنْ شَجَرِ الْحَرَمِ شَيْئًا جَزَاهُ، حَلَالًا كَانَ أَوْ مُحْرِمًا، فِي الشَّجَرَةِ الصَّغِيرَةِ شَاةٌ وَفِي الْكَبِيرَةِ بَقَرَةٌ.
And if he cuts the grass of the Haram or its tree that is not owned and not from what people cultivate, then upon him is its value. The aspect of the hadith: from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Its thorny trees shall not be cut, its game shall not be disturbed, its lost item is not permissible except for one who announces it, and its fresh grass shall not be cut.' So Abbas said: O Messenger of Allah, except idhkhir, so he said: 'Except idhkhir.' And the aspect of the saying of the Tabi'i: from Abu Shurayh al-Adawi from the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: '...so it is not permissible for anyone who believes in Allah and the Last Day to spill blood therein nor to cut a tree therein.' And the aspect of the saying of al-Shafi'i: al-Shafi'i said: Whoever cuts anything from the trees of the Haram must compensate, whether halal or muhrim: for a small tree a sheep, for a large tree a cow.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on cutting vegetation in the Haram, specifically grass or trees that are not owned and not cultivated by people. The ruling is that one must pay the value (qimah) of what was cut. The text then provides three proofs: (1) The hadith of Ibn Abbas about the Haram of Makkah where cutting trees and grass is prohibited except al-idhkhir (a type of fragrant grass). (2) The hadith of Abu Shurayh al-Adawi emphasizing not cutting trees in the Haram. (3) The position of Imam al-Shafi'i, who prescribes specific compensations: a sheep for a small tree and a cow for a large tree. The Hanafi position (from the matn) is to pay the value, not specific animals. The commentary highlights the textual basis for the ruling.

Key Terms
حشيش الحرم (hashīsh al-ḥaram): The grass or herbage growing in the Haram (sacred precinct) that is not owned or cultivated by people.
قيمة (qīmah): The monetary value of the cut vegetation as compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a person who cuts unowned grass in the Haram?
A) He must sacrifice a sheep.
B) He must pay the value (qimah) of the grass.
C) No compensation is required.
D) He must fast three days.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires payment of the monetary value for cutting unowned vegetation in the Haram, based on the prophetic prohibition.

Obligations of the Qarin in Hajj and Umrah
Ruling on the atonement sacrifices required from a Qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule for dams required from a Qarin and identify the exception when only one dam is owed.

Core Idea
A Qarin owes two dams for each violation that costs a Mufrid one dam, except if he passed the miqat without ihram.

This lesson examines the specific obligation of the Qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah) regarding atonement sacrifices. The Hanafi school establishes a doubling rule: any violation requiring one dam for a Mufrid requires two for a Qarin—one for each worship. However, a clear exception exists when the person passes the miqat without ihram and then enters both.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (violation by a Qarin) and the hukm level (wajib).
The ruling is about atonement sacrifices (dam).
2
Apply the general rule
State the doubling rule: two dams for the Qarin for every violation that would require one dam from a Mufrid.
Each dam is attributed separately to Hajj and Umrah.
3
Note the exception
Identify the case where only one dam is required: when the Qarin passes the miqat without ihram and then subsequently enters ihram for both Hajj and Umrah.
This is the exclusive exception mentioned in the text.
4
Examine the proof
Look at the dalil: the saying of Ibrahim al-Nakha'i ('هديان'). Understand that this is a qawl sahabi (Tabi'i) with zanni thubut and dalala.
The proof directly supports the two-dam ruling.
5
Understand the weight of evidence
Recognize that although the dalil is zanni, it is relied upon in the Hanafi school for this ruling.
There is cross-madhhab ikhtilaf on this issue.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكُلُّ شَيْءٍ فَعَلَهُ الْقَارِنُ مِمَّا ذَكَرْنَا أَنَّ فِيهِ عَلَى الْمُفْرِدِ دَمًا فَعَلَى الْقَارِنِ فِيهِ دَمَانٍ دَمٌ حَجَّتِهِ وَدَمٌ لِعُمْرَتِهِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَتَجَاوَزَ الْمِيقَاتَ غَيْرَ مُحْرِمٍ ثُمَّ يُحْرِمُ بِالْعُمْرَةِ وَالْحَجَ فَيَلْزَمُهُ دَمٌ وَاحِدٌ. وَجْهُ قَوْلِ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ قَالَ: «هَدْيَانِ».
And every action that the Qarin does for which we mentioned that upon the Mufrid there is a dam, then upon the Qarin there are two dams: a dam for his Hajj and a dam for his Umrah, except if he passes the miqat without being in ihram, then he assumes ihram for Umrah and Hajj, then only one dam is required. The aspect of the saying of the Tabi'i: from Ibrahim who said: 'Two sacrifices.'
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage outlines the obligation of a Qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah with one ihram) regarding atonement sacrifices (dam). The rule: for any violation that would require one dam from a Mufrid (one performing only Hajj), the Qarin owes two dams—one for his Hajj and one for his Umrah. However, an exception is made if the person passes the miqat without ihram and then enters ihram for both Hajj and Umrah thereafter; in that case, only one dam is required. The proof cited is the saying of Ibrahim (al-Nakha'i), a Tabi'i, who stated 'two sacrifices' for the Qarin.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): A person performing Hajj and Umrah together in one state of ihram.
مفرد (mufrid): A person performing only Hajj (or only Umrah) individually.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep or goat) offered as atonement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When he commits a violation unintentionally.
B) When he passes the miqat without ihram and then enters ihram for both.
C) When he is a woman.
D) When he is performing Hajj Tamattu'.

Key Takeaway
A Qarin generally owes two dams per violation, but if he first crossed the miqat without ihram, only one dam is required.

Joint Killing of Game by Muhrims and Halals in the Haram
Rulings on joint responsibility for killing game in ihram and Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jaza' for two muhrims and two halals jointly killing game, and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
Two muhrims each pay full jaza' for jointly killed game; two halals in Haram pay only one jaza' between them.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a nuanced scenario: when two persons together kill game, does liability split or remain full? The answer depends on their state (muhrim or halal) and location (Haram). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying the rules of hunting restrictions in ihram and in the sacred precincts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Two muhrims jointly kill game vs. two halals jointly kill game inside the Haram. Note the difference in the status of the persons and the location.
The ruling is distinct for each combination.
2
State the ruling precisely
For two muhrims: each pays full compensation (jaza' kamil). For two halals in the Haram: they pay one compensation between them.
Full compensation means the value of the game or its equivalent animal.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet (صلى الله عليه وسلم) refused a gift of a wild donkey because he was in ihram. This shows that a muhrim cannot benefit from game at all, implying full liability for any involvement.
The hadith is from al-Sa'b ibn Jaththamah and is classified as ahad.
4
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The prohibition of benefit extends to participation in killing. Each muhrim violates the sanctity of ihram independently, so full compensation is due from each.
This is why joint action does not reduce liability for muhrims.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools hold that muhrims share compensation proportionally, but the Hanafi view (full jaza' each) is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
This ikhtilaf stems from different interpretations of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اشْتَرَكَ مُحْرِمَانِ فِي قَتْل صَيْدِ فَعَلَى كُلّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا الْجَزَاءُ كَامِلا وَإِذَا اشْتَرَكَ حَلَالَانِ فِي قَتْلِ صَيْدِ الْحَرَمِ فَعَلَيْهِمَا جَزَاء وَاحِدٌ. وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنِ الصَّعْبِ بْنِ جَثَّامَةَ اللَّيْثِيِّ أَنَّهُ أَهْدَى لِرَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ حِمَارًا وَحْشِيًّا، وَهُوَ بِالأَبْوَاءِ، أَوْ بِوَدَّانَ، فَرَدَّهُ عَلَيْهِ، فَلَمَّا رَأَى مَا فِي وَجْهِهِ قَالَ: «إِنَّا لَمْ نَرُدَّهُ عَلَيْكَ إِلَّا أَنَّا حُرُمٌ».
And when two muhrims participate in killing game, then upon each of them is the full compensation. And when two halals participate in killing game of the Haram, then upon both is one compensation. The aspect of the hadith: from al-Sa'b ibn Jaththamah al-Laythi that he gifted a wild donkey to the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, while he was at al-Abwa' or Waddan, and he returned it to him. When he saw the expression on his face, he said: 'Verily, we only returned it to you because we are in ihram.'
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage addresses shared responsibility for killing game. Two scenarios: (1) Two muhrims (people in the state of ihram) jointly kill game: each must pay the full compensation (jaza'), not half. (2) Two halal (non-muhrim) persons jointly kill game within the Haram: they share one compensation (half each, or one compensation between them). The proof provided is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) refused a gift of a wild donkey because he was in ihram, indicating that the muhrim cannot accept or benefit from game. The rule for halals in the Haram is derived from the principle that the sin is joint but the compensation is single because they were not in ihram. The margin also mentions the principle that for two muhrims, each is fully liable because each violated the sanctity of ihram.

Key Terms
جزاء (jazā'): Compensation for killing game, equal to the value or a similar animal.
محرم (muḥrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
حلال (ḥalāl): A person not in the state of ihram; in this context, a non-muhrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two muhrims together kill a deer, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) They pay one compensation shared equally.
B) Each pays half a compensation.
C) Each pays a full compensation.
D) No compensation is due because they acted jointly.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that each muhrim is fully liable for jaza' even in joint killing, reflecting the stringent sanctity of ihram.

Joint Killing of Game and Muhrim's Transactions
Rulings on joint killing and muhrim's transaction invalidity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi rulings on joint killing of game by muhrims and halal persons in the Haram, and explain why a muhrim's sale of game is void, citing the supporting evidence.

Core Idea
Each muhrim owes a full penalty for joint killing; halal persons in Haram share one penalty; muhrim's sale of game is void.

This lesson examines three key rulings from the Hanafi school concerning hunting restrictions during Ihram and within the Haram. Understanding the distinction between multiple parties jointly killing game and the absolute prohibition of commercial transactions in game by a muhrim is essential for proper application of Islamic law. We will explore the textual proofs that establish these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Read the Arabic passage and list the three cases: (1) two muhrims jointly kill game, (2) two halal persons jointly kill game in the Haram, (3) a muhrim sells or buys game. Note the different outcomes.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
For the first ruling, the text cites a statement of Malik (a tabi'i). For the second, it cites the hadith of as-Sa'b ibn Jaththamah and the hadith of Ali. Identify these proofs in the source.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how each proof indicates the ruling. For example, the Prophet's refusal to accept the wild donkey shows that a muhrim cannot benefit from game, which supports both the penalty and the invalidity of sale.
4
Distinguish between the two joint killing scenarios
Note that for muhrims, each is individually liable (full penalty each), while for halal persons in the Haram, they share one penalty. Consider the underlying principle: the prohibition is personal for muhrims, collective for the sanctity of the Haram.
5
Apply the ruling on muhrim's sale
Understand that the sale is void (batil) because the muhrim cannot legally own or transfer game. This is derived from the same prohibition as hunting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في الصيد. وإذا اشترك محرمان في قتل صيد فعلى كل واحد منهما الجزاء كاملا. وإذا اشترك حلالان في قتل صيد الحرم فعليهما جزاء واحد. وإذا باع المحرم صيدا أو ابتاعه فالبيع باطل. وجه: (1) قول التابعي لثبوت وإذا اشترك محرمان في قتل صيد قال مالك في القوم يصيبون الصيد جميعا وهم محرمون. أو في الحرم. قال: أرى أن على كل إنسان منهم جزاءه إن حكم عليهم بالهدي، فعلى كل إنسان منهم هدي. (2) الحديث لثبوت وإذا اشترك حلالان في قتل صيد الحرم فعليهما جزاء واحد عن الصعب بن جثامة الليثي، أنه أهدى لرسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حمارا وحشيا، وهو بالأبواء، أو بودان، فرده عليه، فلما رأى ما في وجهه قال: إنا لم نرده عليك إلا أنا حرم. (3) الحديث لثبوت وإذا اشترك حلالان في قتل صيد الحرم فعليهما جزاء واحد عن علي رضي الله عنه، قال: أمرني النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أن أقوم على البدن، ولا أعطي عليها شيئا في جزارتها. أصول مشترک جنایت کا تاوان ایک نہیں ہے یعنی دو محرم آدمیوں نے ملکر شکار کیا تو دونوں پر الگ الگ بدلہ لازم ہے۔ اصول: لہذا اگر کسی نے ہرن کو حرم سے نکالا پھر اس ہرن نے بچہ دیا اور دونوں فوت ہو گیا تو دونوں کا بدلہ لازم ہو گا، کیونکہ حرم رہنے کی وجہ سے امن کا مستحق تھا، اور حرم سے نکالنا امن کو ضائع کرنا ہوا۔
Chapter on Hunting. If two muhrims jointly kill game, then upon each one of them is the full penalty. If two halal persons jointly kill game in the Haram, then upon both is one penalty. If a muhrim sells game or buys it, the sale is void. Aspect: (1) Statement of the Successor for the proof of: And if two muhrims jointly kill game... Malik said concerning a people who hit game together while they are muhrim or in the Haram: I think that upon each person among them is his penalty, if it is judged upon them by the gift of a sacrificial animal, then upon each person among them is a sacrificial animal. (2) The hadith for the proof of: And if two halal persons jointly kill game in the Haram, then upon both is one penalty: from as-Sa'b ibn Jaththamah al-Laythi that he gifted to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) a wild donkey while he was at al-Abwa' or Waddan, and he returned it to him, and when he saw what was on his face, he said: 'We have not returned it to you except that we are muhrim.' (3) The hadith for the proof of: And if two halal persons jointly kill game in the Haram, then upon both is one penalty: from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him), he said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded me to stand over the sacrificial animals and not give anything upon them from their slaughter. Principles: The penalty for a shared crime is not one, meaning two muhrim men who jointly hunt, then upon both is a separate penalty necessarily. Principle: Therefore if someone removes a deer from the Haram, then that deer gives birth and both die, then the penalty for both is necessary, because due to staying in the Haram it was deserving of security, and removing from the Haram is nullifying security.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn on the chapter of hunting presents three rulings. First, if two persons in the state of ihram jointly kill game, each must pay a full penalty (jaza'). This is because each is independently liable for the act of killing; joint action does not reduce the obligation. Second, if two non-muhrim (halal) persons jointly kill game within the Haram sanctuary, they owe only one penalty between them. The third ruling states that any sale or purchase of game by a muhrim is null and void, as the muhrim cannot legally deal in game. The text then provides evidence: a statement of Malik (a tabi'i view) for the first ruling, and hadiths for the second. Specifically, the hadith of as-Sa'b ibn Jaththamah shows the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) returning a gifted wild donkey because he was muhrim, indicating the prohibition of accepting game while in ihram. The hadith of Ali (radiAllahu anhu) about supervising the sacrificial animals supports the ruling that no payment is given to the butcher from the sacrificial meat, implying that game in the Haram is inviolable. The principle at the end clarifies that shared liability does not merge penalties; each muhrim is individually liable. The secondary example about removing a deer from the Haram illustrates that the penalty applies to both the original removal and the offspring, as the security of the Haram is lost by the act.

Key Terms
مُحْرِم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, subject to prohibitions including hunting.
جَزَاء (jaza'): The penalty or compensation for killing game while in ihram or in the Haram, typically an animal sacrifice or equivalent.
صَيْد الْحَرَم (sayd al-haram): Game within the boundaries of the Haram of Makkah, which is inviolable and killing it incurs penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If two muhrims jointly kill a deer, how many penalties are due?
A) One penalty, shared between them.
B) Two full penalties, one from each.
C) One penalty from the person who struck first.
D) No penalty if they did not intend to hunt.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, joint hunting by muhrims imposes full penalty on each individual, while joint hunting by halal persons in the Haram incurs only one penalty; moreover, any sale or purchase of game by a muhrim is void.

Ihsaar: Exiting Ihram When Prevented by Enemy or Illness
Ruling on ihsaar with proofs from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ihsaar, identify the proofs (Quran and Sunnah), and apply the conditions for exiting ihram lawfully.

Core Idea
A muhrim prevented by enemy or severe illness may exit ihram only after sending a sacrifice to the Haram.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on ihsaar (prevention from completing Hajj or Umrah). Al-Quduri's matn presents the case and the evidence. You will learn the exact conditions that permit tahallul and the required procedure, distinguishing between legitimate obstacles and mere inconvenience.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is ihsaar? What is the hukm on sending a sacrifice when prevented? The matn states that if a muhrim is prevented by enemy or illness, it becomes permissible to exit ihram after sending a sacrifice. That sending is wajib.
The ruling is permissive (halal) but sending the sacrifice is obligatory (wajib).
2
Locate the primary dalil (Quran)
Surah Al-Baqarah 2:196 commands: 'If you are prevented, then [sacrifice] what is easy of the sacrificial animal.' This indicates obligation.
The imperative form (fama istaysara) implies wujub in Hanafi usul.
3
Examine the secondary dalil (Sunnah)
Two hadiths are cited: Ibn Umar's practice and the explicit statement of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) that one who breaks a bone or becomes lame has exited ihram and owes a future Hajj.
These hadiths confirm the ruling and add details about the procedure.
4
Trace the Hanafi interpretation
The Hanafis include severe illness as a valid cause for ihsaar, unlike some other schools. They also require the sacrifice to be sent to the Haram and the muhrim to not shave until the animal reaches its destination.
This interpretation is based on the general wording of the verse and the practice of the Companions.
5
Determine the conditions and wajibat
Conditions for ihsaar: being prevented by an enemy or severe illness. Wajibat: send a sacrificial animal to the Haram, appoint a carrier for a specific day, then shave the head.
The muhrim may not simply shave; the sacrifice must precede tahallul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإحصار. قال - رحمه الله -: إذا أحصر المحرم بعدو أو أصابه مرض يمنعه من المضي حل له التحلل، وقيل له ابعث بشاة تذبح بالحرم، وواعد بها من يحملها ليوم بعينه ثم يتحلل. وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت إذا أحصر المحرم بعدو أو أصابه مرض: {وأتموا الحج والعمرة لله فإن أحصرتم فما استيسر من الهدي ولا تحلقوا رءوسكم حتى يبلغ الهدي محله} (سورة البقرة، 195). وجه: (2) الحديث لثبوت إذا أحصر المحرم بعدو أو أصابه مرض: كان ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما يقول: أليس حسبكم سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم؟ إن حبس أحدكم عن الحج، طاف بالبيت وبالصفا والمروة، ثم حل من كل شيء حتى يحج عاما قابلا، فيهدي أو يصوم إن لم يجد هديا. وجه: (3) الحديث لثبوت إذا أحصر المحرم بعدو أو أصابه مرض: سمعت الحجاج بن عمرو الأنصاري قال: قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «من كسر أو عرج فقد حل وعليه الحج من قابل». وجه: (1) الآية لثبوت وواعد بها من يحملها ليوم بعينه: {وأتموا الحج والعمرة لله فإن أحصرتم فما استيسر من الهدي ولا تحلقوا رءوسكم حتى يبلغ الهدي محله}. وجه: (2) الحديث لثبوت وواعد بها من يحملها ليوم بعينه: عن المسور بن مخرمة ومروان... أصول: احناف کے نزدیک دشمن کا سخت خوف ہو یا شدید مرض میں مبتلاء ہو جائے تو حج یا عمرہ سے احصار ہو سکتا ہے، البتہ ہدی کسی کے ذریعے بھیجدے اور حلق کرالے۔
Chapter on Ihsaar. He (rahimahullah) said: When the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or a sickness that prevents him from proceeding, it becomes permissible for him to exit ihram, and it is said to him: Send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram, and make an appointment with the one who carries it for a specific day, then exit ihram. Aspect: (1) The verse for proof of when the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or sickness: {And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah, but if you are prevented, then [sacrifice] what is easy of the sacrificial animal, and do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place of sacrifice} (Surah al-Baqarah, 195). Aspect: (2) The hadith for proof of when the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or sickness: Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) used to say: Is not the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah sufficient for you? If one of you is detained from the Hajj, he should circumambulate the House and [run] between Safa and Marwah, then exit ihram from everything, until he performs Hajj the following year, and he should sacrifice or fast if he does not find a sacrificial animal. Aspect: (3) The hadith for proof of when the muhrim is prevented by an enemy or sickness: I heard al-Hajjaj ibn Amr al-Ansari say: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever breaks a bone or becomes lame has exited ihram, and upon him is Hajj the following year.' Aspect: (1) The verse for proof of making an appointment with the one carrying it for a specific day: {And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah, but if you are prevented, then [sacrifice] what is easy of the sacrificial animal, and do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place of sacrifice}. Aspect: (2) The hadith for proof of making an appointment with the one carrying it for a specific day: from al-Miswar ibn Makhramah and Marwan... Principles: According to the Hanafis, if there is severe fear of the enemy or one is afflicted with intense illness, then ihsaar from Hajj or Umrah can occur, but one should send the sacrificial animal via someone and shave one's hair.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri's matn on the chapter of Ihsaar (prevention) outlines the ruling for a muhrim who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to an enemy (enemy blockade) or illness that prevents him from proceeding. In such a case, it becomes permissible for him to exit ihram (tahallul) by sending a sacrificial animal (shah) to be slaughtered in the Haram. He must make an appointment with the person carrying the animal for a specific day, then he may shave his head and exit ihram. The evidence cited includes the Quranic verse (2:196), which commands to send a sacrificial animal if prevented, and hadiths: one from Ibn Umar explaining the practice of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) for those detained; another from al-Hajjaj ibn Amr stating that one who breaks a bone or becomes lame has exited ihram and owes a future Hajj. The Hanafi principle at the end clarifies that ihsaar applies only in cases of severe fear (enemy) or illness; one must send the sacrifice and then shave. This distinguishes ihsaar from merely changing one's mind. The ruling emphasizes that the sacrifice must be sent to the Haram, and the muhrim cannot shave until the animal arrives at its destination.

Key Terms
إِحْصَار (ihsaar): Being prevented from continuing Hajj or Umrah due to an enemy or severe illness, which permits exiting ihram with a sacrifice.
تَحَلَّل (tahallul): The act of exiting ihram by shaving or trimming hair after sending a sacrifice.
هَدْي (hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram for slaughter during Hajj or Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a muhrim do when prevented by a severe illness?
A) Send a sacrifice to the Haram and then shave his head.
B) Simply shave his head and exit ihram.
C) Wait until he recovers and continue.
D) Perform Umrah instead.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a muhrim prevented by enemy or severe illness may exit ihram only after sending a sacrificial animal to the Haram and shaving upon its arrival.
