Ihsar: Ruling for a Prevented Pilgrim
Quduri's matn on ihsar with proofs from Quran and Sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for ihsar, identify the proofs from Quran and Sunnah, and explain the obligations for valid tahlil.

Core Idea
A prevented pilgrim must send a sacrifice to the Haram before exiting ihram.

The Hajj or Umrah may be interrupted by circumstances beyond one's control. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance: when a person in ihram is blocked by an enemy or severe illness, he may exit ihram but must first arrange a sacrificial animal to be slaughtered in the Haram on a specific day. This lesson examines the ruling, its conditions, and the supporting evidence from the Quran and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is being prevented (ihsar) from continuing Hajj or Umrah. The ruling: tahlil (exiting ihram) becomes permissible, but sending a sacrificial animal (hady) is wajib.
The hukm level is wajib due to the command in the verse (amr implies wujub in Hanafi usul).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof is Quran 2:196: 'But if you are prevented, then [offer] what can be obtained with ease of sacrificial animals.' This indicates the obligation of a sacrifice.
The verse is qat'i in transmission (thubut) but zanni in meaning (dalala) regarding the exact details.
3
Understand the hadith proofs
The hadith of Ibn Umar shows the practical application: if prevented, one performs tawaf and sa'y, then exits ihram, and owes a sacrifice or fasting. The hadith of al-Hajjaj shows that injury also permits tahlil.
These hadith support the ruling and provide alternatives when a sacrifice is unavailable.
4
Note the condition of appointing a day
The matn requires making a promise with the carrier for a specific day of slaughter. This ensures the sacrifice reaches the Haram at a known time.
This condition is derived from the practice of the Prophet at Hudaybiyyah.
5
Apply: alternative if no sacrifice available
If a person cannot find a sacrificial animal, fasting is an acceptable substitute, as stated in the hadith of Ibn Umar.
This is a textual concession; it does not replace the obligation to send a sacrifice when possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْإِحْصَارِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - إِذَا أُحْصِرَ الْمُحْرِمُ بِعَدَةٍ أَوْ أَصَابَهُ مَرَضٌ يَمْنَعُهُ مِنَ الْمُضِيِّ حَلَّ لَهُ التَّحَلُّلُ وَقِيلَ لَهُ ابْعَثْ بِشَاةٍ تُذْبَحُ بِالْحَرَمِ وَوَاعِدْ بِهَا مَنْ يَحْمِلُهَا لِيَوْمٍ بِعَيْنِهِ ثُمَّ يَتَحَلَّلْ.
ادلته:
وجه (۱) الآية: ﴿وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ فَإِنْ أُحْصِرْتُمْ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيِ وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُءُوسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدْيُ مَحِلَّهُ﴾ (البقرة: ۱۹۶)
وجه (۲) الحديث عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: «أَلَيْسَ حَسْبُكُمْ سُنَّةَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ؟ إِنْ حُبِسَ أَحَدُكُمْ عَنِ الْحَجِّ طَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ وَبِالصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ ثُمَّ حَلَّ مِنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ حَتَّى يَحُجَّ عَامًا قَابِلًا فَيُهْدِي أَوْ يَصُومُ إِنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ هَدْيًا» (رواه البخاري)
وجه (۳) الحديث عَنِ الْحَجَّاجِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو الْأَنْصَارِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ كُسِرَ أَوْ عَرَجَ فَقَدْ حَلَّ وَعَلَيْهِ الْحَجُّ مِنْ قَابِلٍ» (رواه أبو داود والترمذي)
وجه (۱) الآية لثبوت الوعد: ﴿وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ فَإِنْ أُحْصِرْتُمْ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيِ﴾ (البقرة: ۱۹۶)
وجه (۲) الحديث عَنِ الْمِسْوَرِ بْنِ مَخْرَمَةَ وَمَرْوَانَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ لِأَصْحَابِهِ عَامَ الْحُدَيْبِيَةِ: «قُومُوا فَانْحَرُوا ثُمَّ احْلِقُوا» (رواه البخاري)
اصول: احناف کے نزدیک دشمن کا سخت خوف ہو یا شدید مرض میں مبتلا ہو جائے تو حج یا عمرہ سے احصار ہو سکتا ہے، البتہ ہدی کسی کے ذریعے بھیج دے اور حلق کرالے۔
Chapter of Ihsar: He said - may Allah have mercy on him - When a muhrim is prevented by an enemy or afflicted by an illness that prevents him from proceeding, tahlil becomes permissible for him, and he is told: Send a sheep to be slaughtered in the Haram, and make a promise with it to the one carrying it for a specific day, then he makes tahlil. Its proofs: Face (1) the verse: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah, but if you are prevented, then [offer] what can be obtained with ease of sacrificial animals, and do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place of sacrifice' (Al-Baqarah 2:196). Face (2) the hadith from Ibn Umar: 'Is not the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah enough for you? If one of you is prevented from Hajj, he performs tawaf of the House and Sa'y between Safa and Marwah, then he becomes free from all restrictions, until he performs Hajj the following year and offers a sacrifice or fasts if he cannot find a sacrifice' (Bukhari). Face (3) the hadith from al-Hajjaj ibn Amr al-Ansari: 'Whoever breaks a bone or becomes lame has made tahlil and owes the Hajj next year' (Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi). Face (1) the verse for establishing the promise: 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah, but if you are prevented, then [offer] what can be obtained with ease of sacrificial animals' (Al-Baqarah 2:196). Face (2) the hadith from al-Miswar ibn Makhramah and Marwan that the Messenger of Allah said to his companions in the year of Hudaybiyyah: 'Stand and sacrifice, then shave' (Bukhari). Principle: According to the Hanafis, being severely fearful of the enemy or afflicted with a serious illness can constitute ihsar from Hajj or Umrah; however, he should send the sacrificial animal through someone and have his head shaved.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on ihsar (prevention from completing Hajj or Umrah). The ruling: if a person in ihram is prevented by an enemy or falls so ill that he cannot proceed, he is permitted to exit ihram (tahlul). However, he must send a sheep (or equivalent sacrificial animal) to be slaughtered within the Haram (the sacred precincts of Makkah). He appoints a specific day for the slaughter by promising the carrier that the animal will be slaughtered on that day. After sending it, he may shave his head and remove ihram. The proofs include: (1) Quran 2:196, which commands that if prevented, one offers a sacrificial animal and does not shave until it reaches its destination; (2) the hadith of Ibn Umar, showing the practice of exiting ihram after tawaf and sa'y and then making up the Hajj the next year with a sacrifice or fasting; (3) the hadith of al-Hajjaj ibn Amr that breaking a bone or lameness permits tahlil but requires performing Hajj again. The additional proofs show the command to send the animal and appoint a day, from the same verse and the incident of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet ordered sacrifice and shaving after being prevented. The Urdu note clarifies that according to the Hanafi school, both enemy fear and illness justify ihsar, and one must send the sacrificial animal through a proxy for slaughter.

Key Terms
الْإِحْصَار (al-ihsar): Prevention from completing the rites of Hajj or Umrah due to enemy or illness.
الْمُحْرِم (al-muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
التَّحَلُّل (al-tahlul): Exiting the state of ihram by shaving the head or cutting hair after performing the required rites.
الْهَدْي (al-hady): A sacrificial animal, typically a sheep, goat, cow, or camel sent to the Haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Remain in ihram until the next year without any action.
B) Send a sacrificial animal to the Haram and appoint a day for its slaughter, then make tahlil.
C) Simply shave his head and exit ihram immediately.
D) Fast for ten days in lieu of sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
A prevented pilgrim must send a sacrificial animal to the Haram and appoint a day before exiting ihram.

Ruling for Qarin and Timing of Slaughter for Muhsar
Additional rulings: qarin sends two sacrifices; intra-Hanafi dispute on slaughter timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a qarin who is muhsar and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of slaughter for a muhsar bil-Hajj.

Core Idea
A muhsar qarin sends two sacrifices; Abu Hanifa permits early slaughter, Sahibayn require Yawm al-Nahr.

This passage from al-Quduri adds two important rules for those prevented from completing Hajj (muhsar). First, if the prevented person had combined Hajj and Umrah (qarin), he must send two sacrificial animals. Second, there is a notable intra-Hanafi dispute about when a muhsar bil-Hajj may slaughter his sacrifice. Imam Abu Hanifa allows it before the Day of Sacrifice, while his two companions restrict it to that day. Understanding this dispute reveals the flexibility within the Hanafi school regarding the constraints of ihsar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for a qarin muhsar
State that a qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) who is prevented from completing the rites must send two blood sacrifices (dam): one for the qiran and one for the ihsar.
The proof is from Malik's Muwatta regarding a qarin who misses Hajj.
2
Locate the disputed issue
The dispute is about the timing of slaughter for a muhsar bil-Hajj: can it be done before Yawm al-Nahr (10th Dhu al-Hijjah) or only on that day?
Both sides agree on the place: the Haram.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and evidence
Abu Hanifa permits slaughter before Yawm al-Nahr, as soon as the animal reaches the Haram. His evidence includes the verse (2:196) which does not specify a date, and the hadith of Anas that the Prophet slaughtered his hady for Umrah al-Hudaybiyah in Dhu al-Qa'dah (before Hajj).
4
State the Sahibayn's position and evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that sacrifice for a muhsar bil-Hajj is permissible only on Yawm al-Nahr. They interpret 'mahill' (place of sacrifice) in the verse as specifically Mina on that day for Hajj.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Abu Hanifa's view allows early exit from ihram, while the Sahibayn require remaining in ihram until Yawm al-Nahr. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's.
Later Hanafi works like al-Hidayah favor Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ كَانَ قَارِنًا بَعَثَ بِدَمَيْنِ وَلَا يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ دَمِ الْإِحْصَارِ إِلَّا فِي الْحَرَمِ وَيَجُوزُ قَبْلَ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا يَجُوزُ الذَّبْحُ لِمُحْصَرٍ بِالْحَجِّ إِلَّا فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُحْصَرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ الذَّبْحُ مَتَى شَاءَ.
ادلته:
وجه (۱) قول التابعي: قَالَ مَالِكٌ: وَمَنْ قَرَنَ الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ ثُمَّ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ فَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَحُجَّ قَابِلًا وَيَقْرِنَ بَيْنَ الْحَجِّ وَالْعُمْرَةِ وَيُهْدِي هَدْيَيْنِ: هَدْيًا لِقِرَانِهِ وَهَدْيًا لِمَا فَاتَهُ مِنَ الْحَجِّ (الموطأ)
وجه (۱) الآية: ﴿وَلَا تَحْلِقُوا رُءُوسَكُمْ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدْيُ مَحِلَّهُ﴾ (البقرة: ۱۹۶)
وجه (۲) الحديث عَنْ أَنَسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: اعْتَمَرَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَرْبَعَ عُمَرٍ كُلُّهُنَّ فِي ذِي الْقَعْدَةِ إِلَّا الَّتِي مَعَ حَجَّتِهِ: عُمْرَةَ الْحُدَيْبِيَةِ فِي ذِي الْقَعْدَةِ حَيْثُ صَدَّهُ الْمُشْرِكُونَ (رواه البخاري)
If he is a qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together), he sends two blood sacrifices. It is not permissible to slaughter the blood sacrifice of ihsar except in the Haram, and it is permissible before the Day of Sacrifice according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The slaughter for one prevented from Hajj is not permissible except on the Day of Sacrifice. It is permissible for one prevented from Umrah to slaughter whenever he wishes. Its proofs: Face (1) the saying of the Tabi'i: Malik said: Whoever combines Hajj and Umrah and then misses Hajj must perform Hajj the following year, combine Hajj and Umrah, and offer two sacrificial animals: one for his qiran and one for missing Hajj (al-Muwatta). Face (1) the verse: 'Do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place of sacrifice' (Al-Baqarah 2:196). Face (2) the hadith from Anas: The Prophet performed four Umrahs, all in Dhu al-Qa'dah except the one with his Hajj: Umrah al-Hudaybiyah in Dhu al-Qa'dah when the polytheists prevented him (Bukhari).
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage presents two additional rulings on ihsar. First, if the prevented person is a qarin (had combined Hajj and Umrah in one ihram), he must send two sacrificial animals: one for the qiran and one for the ihsar. The proof is a statement of Imam Malik regarding a missed Hajj for a qarin. Second, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the timing of slaughter for a muhsar who was performing Hajj. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is permissible to slaughter the sacrifice for a muhsar bil-Hajj before the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhu al-Hijjah). Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) hold that it is not permissible except on the Day of Sacrifice. For a muhsar bil-Umrah, all agree that he may slaughter whenever he wishes. The proofs for the permissibility before yawm al-nahr include the verse that merely connects the slaughter with shaving, and the hadith of Anas that the Prophet's Umrah al-Hudaybiyah was in Dhu al-Qa'dah (which is before Hajj season), and the animals were slaughtered then. The Sahibayn argue that the verse 'until the hady reaches its place' implies the Day of Sacrifice for Hajj.

Key Terms
الْقَارِن (al-qarin): A person who enters ihram for both Hajj and Umrah together.
دَم (dam): Blood sacrifice; in this context, a sacrificial animal required for ihsar or qiran.
يَوْمُ النَّحْر (yawm al-nahr): The Day of Sacrifice, 10th Dhu al-Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Before Yawm al-Nahr, as soon as the animal reaches the Haram.
C) Only after completing Hajj the following year.
D) Only after the 12th of Dhu al-Hijjah.

Key Takeaway
A muhsar qarin sends two sacrifices; Abu Hanifa's position allows early slaughter before Yawm al-Nahr, which is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.

Obligations of the Muhsar bil-Hajj After Tahlil
Ruling with proof for the muhsar bil-Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a muhsar bil-Hajj after tahlil and identify the proofs from the practice of Umar and the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
A muhsar bil-Hajj owes both a makeup Hajj and a separate Umrah after tahlil.

When a person enters ihram for Hajj but is prevented from completing it (muhsar bil-Hajj), the Hanafi school holds that ihsar does not cancel the obligation entirely. After making tahlil (exiting ihram), he must make up the missed Hajj and also perform an additional Umrah. This lesson explores the ruling and its evidence from the practice of Caliph Umar and the hadith of Aisha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category and initial situation
Recognize that the ruling applies to a person who has entered ihram for Hajj and is then prevented (muhsar bil-Hajj). The situation assumes he has made tahlil to exit ihram.
The source text does not detail the method of tahlil, but it is typically done by performing a 'Umrah or sacrificing an animal.
2
State the ruling after tahlil
The text explicitly says: 'Upon him is a Hajj and an Umrah.' This means he owes both a complete makeup Hajj and a separate Umrah as qada.
This is the mufta bihi position for the Hanafi school.
3
Follow the proofs: first evidence
The first proof is the practice of Caliph Umar, who ordered Abu Ayyub and Habbab, when they missed Hajj, to exit ihram with Umrah, then later perform Hajj the following year.
This is a Qawl Sahabi (saying of a companion), which is a valid proof in Hanafi usul.
4
Follow the proofs: second evidence
The second proof is the hadith of Aisha, where the Prophet sent her to Tan'im to perform an Umrah in place of the one she missed, establishing the principle that a missed Umrah must be made up.
This hadith from Bukhari supports the requirement of a separate Umrah for the muhsar bil-Hajj.
5
Understand the sequence
The Urdu note clarifies: first, the muhsar bil-Hajj performs an Umrah to become halal (tahlil), then later at the next Hajj season, he performs the makeup Hajj.
Thus, the Umrah serves both as the means of tahlil and as a required qada.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُحْصَرُ بِالْحَجِّ إِذَا تَحَلَّلَ فَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَةٌ.
ادلته:
وجه (۱) قول التابعي: قَالَ مَالِكٌ: وَقَدْ أَمَرَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ أَبَا أَيُّوبَ الْأَنْصَارِيَّ وَهَبَّارَ بْنَ الْأَسْوَدِ حِينَ فَاتَهُمَا الْحَجُّ وَأَتَيَا يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ أَنْ يَحِلَّا بِعُمْرَةٍ ثُمَّ يَرْجِعَا حَلَالًا ثُمَّ يَحُجَّانِ عَامًا قَابِلًا وَيُهْدِيَانِ فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعَ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ (الموطأ)
وجه (۲) الحديث عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ ... أَرْسَلَنِي النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مَعَ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ إِلَى التَّنْعِيمِ فَاعْتَمَرْتُ فَقَالَ: «هَذِهِ مَكَانَ عُمْرَتِكِ» (رواه البخاري)
اصول: حج کا محصر حج اور عمرہ دونوں کرے گا، بایں طور کہ حج سے محصر ہوا تو عمرہ کر کے حلال ہو جائے، لہذا اولاً عمرہ کرے بعد ازاں حج کے موقع سے حج کی قضاء کرے۔
The one prevented from Hajj, when he makes tahlil, owes a Hajj and an Umrah. Its proofs: Face (1) the saying of the Tabi'i: Malik said: And Umar ibn al-Khattab ordered Abu Ayyub al-Ansari and Habbab ibn al-Aswad when both missed Hajj and came on the Day of Sacrifice, to exit ihram with an Umrah, then return as non-muhrims, then perform Hajj the following year and offer sacrifices, and whoever cannot find [a sacrifice] should fast three days in Hajj and seven when he returns to his family (al-Muwatta). Face (2) the hadith from Aisha: She said: We went out with the Prophet in the Farewell Pilgrimage... the Prophet sent me with Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr to Tan'im and I performed Umrah, and he said: 'This in place of your Umrah' (Bukhari). Principle: The muhsar bil-Hajj will perform both Hajj and Umrah: that is, since he was prevented from Hajj, he becomes halal by performing Umrah; therefore he first performs Umrah, then at the time of Hajj he makes qada of the Hajj.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage states that a person prevented from completing Hajj (muhsar bil-Hajj) after making tahlil (exiting ihram) owes two acts of worship: a full Hajj and a separate Umrah. The proof is a precedent from Caliph Umar who ordered Abu Ayyub and Habbab when they missed Hajj to make tahlil by performing an Umrah immediately, then later perform a makeup Hajj the following year. The hadith of Aisha shows that when she missed the Umrah due to menstruation, the Prophet sent her to Tan'im to perform an Umrah in lieu of the missed one, establishing the principle that a missed Umrah must be made up. For the muhsar bil-Hajj, the Hanafi position is that he owes both: he first performs an Umrah to exit ihram (since he cannot complete Hajj), then later performs the makeup Hajj. The Urdu note explains the sequence: he first does Umrah to become halal, then at the next Hajj season, he does the qada of the missed Hajj.

Key Terms
الْمُحْصَرُ بِالْحَجِّ (al-muhsar bi al-hajj): A person who has entered ihram for Hajj but is prevented from completing it.
الْقَضَاء (al-qada): Making up a missed obligatory act of worship, in this case Hajj and Umrah missed due to ihsar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a muhsar bil-Hajj do after making tahlil?
A) Nothing; his obligation is discharged.
B) Only perform a makeup Hajj the following year.
C) Perform a complete Hajj and a separate Umrah as makeup.
D) Only perform an Umrah.

Key Takeaway
A muhsar bil-Hajj must perform both a makeup Hajj and a separate Umrah after tahlil, as established by the practice of Umar and the hadith of Aisha.

The Qarin Muhsar Must Send Two Sacrificial Animals
A ruling from al-Quduri's matn on the qarin muhsar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a qarin muhsar regarding sacrificial animals and identify the two reasons for the requirement.

Core Idea
A qarin muhsar must send two sacrificial animals: one for the qiran and one for the ihsar.

This lesson clarifies a specific Hajj ruling from al-Quduri's matn: what must a person who combines Hajj and Umrah (qarin) do if he is prevented (muhsar) from completing the Hajj? The answer is not one animal but two, each with its own cause. Understanding this distinction is crucial for fulfilling the obligations correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What is the act? A qarin (one who performs qiran) who becomes muhsar (prevented from completing Hajj). Ruling: He must send (ba'atha) two sacrificial animals (dam).
2
Determine the two reasons
Why two animals? The first is for the qiran itself: every qarin must offer a hadi (sacrifice) due to combining Hajj and Umrah. The second is for the ihsar: being prevented from completing the Hajj triggers a separate dam.
One dam for qiran, one for ihsar.
3
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The author cites Malik's statement from the Muwatta. Malik explicitly says that one who combines Hajj and Umrah and misses the Hajj must offer two sacrificial animals: one for the qiran and one for missing the Hajj. This corroborates the Hanafi ruling.
Malik's statement is used as evidence, though Maliki fiqh may have nuances.
4
Note the cross-madhhab consideration
The Hanafi position is that both dums are wajib. The Maliki school agrees on two animals. Other schools may differ on the number or obligation. This is an area of legitimate ikhtilaf.
The passage does not elaborate on disagreements, but shows Hanafi reliance on Malik's narration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ كَانَ قَارِنًا بَعَثَ بِدَمَيْنِ. قَالَ مَالِكٌ: وَمَنْ قَرَنَ الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ. ثُمَّ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُ فَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَحُجَّ قَابِلًا وَيَقْرُنُ بَيْنَ الْحَجِّ وَالْعُمْرَةِ. وَيُهْدِي هَدْيَيْنِ: هَدْيًا لِقِرَانِهِ الْحَجَّ مَعَ الْعُمْرَةِ، وَهَدْيًا لِمَا فَاتَهُ مِنَ الْحَجِّ.
If he is a qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah), he sends two sacrificial animals. Malik said: Whoever combines Hajj and Umrah, then misses the Hajj, must perform Hajj the following year and combine between Hajj and Umrah, and offer two sacrificial animals: one for his combining Hajj and Umrah, and one for missing the Hajj.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from al-Quduri's matn with a supporting narration from Imam Malik. The ruling states that a person who enters ihram for both Hajj and Umrah (qiran) and is then prevented (muhsar) from completing the Hajj must send two sacrificial animals (dam). The reason is that he owes one dam for the qiran (since the qarin is required to offer a hadi) and another dam for being muhsar. The evidence quoted from Malik reinforces this obligation, detailing that such a person must perform Hajj the next year combining again and offer two animals. Note that this is the Hanafi position, though Malik's wording is used as corroboration. The Urdu usul note (not part of this lesson) later clarifies that the qarin also owes one hajj and two umrahs in qada.

Key Terms
قارن (qarin): A person who performs Hajj and Umrah together in one ihram (qiran).
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as compensation for certain acts in Hajj/Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One animal
B) Two animals
C) Three animals
D) None

Key Takeaway
A qarin who is prevented from completing Hajj must send two sacrificial animals: one for the qiran and one for the ihsar.

Timing of Slaughter for a Muhsar: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of muhsar's slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when a muhsar bi'l-Hajj may slaughter his dam al-ihsar, explain the Sahibayn's view, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
A muhsar's dam is compensation, not a hadi — so timing is flexible before Yawm al-Nahr.

This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on the timing of slaughter for a person prevented from completing Hajj (muhsar). While all agree the dam must be slaughtered within the Haram, they differ on when: Abu Hanifa allows any time before Yawm al-Nahr, while the Sahibayn restrict it to Yawm al-Nahr itself. The practical consequence affects whether the sacrifice suffices if done early.

Guided Path
1
State the agreed rule on place
All Hanafis agree that the dam al-ihsar must be slaughtered in the Haram. Identify this from the text and note the Quranic basis (2:196).
Place is uncontested; the dispute is about timing.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's position on timing
Abu Hanifa permits slaughter before Yawm al-Nahr. Understand his reasoning: the dam is compensation for prevention, not a hadi tied to a specific day.
He relies on the general permission and the Prophet's practice at Hudaybiyyah.
3
Identify the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict it to Yawm al-Nahr by analogy to hadi al-tamattu'. Recognize their qiyas-based argument.
They treat it as a sacrificial animal linked to the day of sacrifice.
4
Note the exception for umrah
The text adds that for a muhsar bi'l-umrah, no time restriction exists. Understand why: Umrah has no fixed sacrificial day.
This shows the specificity of the Hajj ruling.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon for fatwa due to its ease and stronger textual support. Confirm this from the commentary.
Later Hanafi scholars prefer the more flexible ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ دَمِ الْإِحْصَارِ إِلَّا فِي الْحَرَمِ وَيَجُوزُ قَبْلَ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ لَا يَجُوزُ الذَّبْحُ لِمُحْصَرٍ بِالْحَجِّ إِلَّا فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ. وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُحْصَرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ الذَّبْحُ مَتَى شَاءَ.
It is not permissible to slaughter the dam of ihsar except in the Haram, and it is permissible before the Day of Sacrifice according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is not permissible for one prevented from Hajj to slaughter except on the Day of Sacrifice. And it is permissible for one prevented from Umrah to slaughter whenever he wishes.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of slaughter for a muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj). All agree that the dam al-ihsar must be slaughtered within the Haram (sanctuary), based on the Quranic verse 'until the offering reaches its place of sacrifice' (2:196). However, Abu Hanifa holds that the slaughter can take place any time before Yawm al-Nahr (the 10th of Dhul Hijjah), once the animal is conveyed to the Haram. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) restrict it to Yawm al-Nahr itself, analogizing it to the hadi of Hajj. For a muhsar bi'l-umrah, there is no time restriction – he may slaughter whenever he wants, as Umrah is not tied to specific days. The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa, as it is more facilitating and based on the general proof of compliance with the qurban. The evidence cited after this passage includes the Quranic verse and a hadith from Anas about the Prophet's Umrah at Hudaybiyyah.

Key Terms
محصر (muhsar): A person prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to enemy, illness, or any excuse beyond control.
دم الإحصار (dam al-ihsar): A sacrificial animal required from a muhsar to compensate for being unable to complete the pilgrimage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, when may a person prevented from Hajj slaughter the dam al-ihsar?
A) Only on Yawm al-Nahr
B) At any time before Yawm al-Nahr
C) Only after returning home
D) Only at the Haram on the Day of Sacrifice

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view is that a muhsar bi'l-Hajj may slaughter his dam any time before Yawm al-Nahr, as it is compensation, not a fixed hadi.

Muhsar bi'l-Umrah: Slaughter Anytime
A ruling statement on the timing of slaughter for muhsar bi'l-umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a muhsar bi'l-umrah regarding the timing of the slaughter and explain why it differs from the muhsar bi'l-hajj.

Core Idea
The muhsar bi'l-umrah may slaughter his dam any time; no fixed day like the muhsar bi'l-hajj.

This short matn from al-Quduri gives a clear and concise ruling for a person prevented from completing Umrah (muhsar bi'l-umrah). Unlike the muhsar bi'l-hajj who must slaughter on a specific day (Yawm al-Nahr), the muhsar bi'l-umrah has full flexibility in timing. This lesson explores the ruling, its legal basis, and its practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slaughtering the dam al-ihsar (the sacrificial animal due to prevention). The ruling is that it is wajib to do so, and it is permissible (ja'iz) to do it at any time the muhsar wishes.
The word 'yajuz' indicates permissibility of timing, not permissibility of the slaughter itself (which is wajib).
2
Contrast with the muhsar bi'l-hajj
The muhsar bi'l-hajj is restricted to slaughter on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). The muhsar bi'l-umrah has no such restriction because Umrah is not tied to a specific time period.
This contrast highlights that Umrah can be performed any time of the year.
3
Understand the legal cause (sabab)
The cause of this ruling is that the purpose of the dam is to exit ihram (tahlal), not to mark a festival. Since Umrah is not time-bound, there is no need to wait for a specific day.
The sabab is the need to lift the ihram, which is immediate.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
All Hanafi imams agree: the muhsar bi'l-umrah may slaughter at any time. There is no intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
This is the mufta bihi position and is considered muttfaq alayh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ لِلْمُحْصَرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ الذَّبْحُ مَتَى شَاءَ.
And it is permissible for the one prevented from Umrah to slaughter whenever he wishes.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This is a concise ruling from the matn of al-Quduri. It states that a person who is prevented (muhsar) from completing Umrah may slaughter the dam al-ihsar at any time he wishes, without being restricted to a specific day like the Hajj muhsar. The reason is that Umrah is not time-bound to specific dates (it can be performed any time of the year), and the duty of slaughter is merely to exit ihram. Therefore, the muhsar bi'l-umrah may send the animal and slaughter as soon as possible. This is the Hanafi position and is agreed upon by the school.

Key Terms
عمرة (umrah): The lesser pilgrimage, consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq or taqsir.
مُحْصَر (muhsar): One who enters ihram for Hajj or Umrah but is prevented from completing it due to an obstacle like enemy blockade, illness, or detention.
ذَبْح (dhabh): The Islamic method of slaughtering an animal by cutting the throat while reciting Bismillah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah
B) Within three days of being prevented
C) Whenever he wishes
D) Only at the end of the year

Key Takeaway
The muhsar bi'l-umrah has complete flexibility in the timing of slaughter; the only requirement is to slaughter before performing tahlal.

Qada of Hajj and Umrah for the Muhsar bi'l-Hajj
Ruling that a muhsar bi'l-Hajj must perform both Hajj and Umrah as qada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a muhsar bi'l-hajj must perform both Hajj and Umrah as qada after tahlal, and identify the supporting textual evidence.

Core Idea
Tahlal after prevention does not discharge the obligation; both Hajj and Umrah must be made up.

When a person is prevented from completing Hajj after entering ihram, he may exit the state of ihram by sending a sacrifice. This lesson examines the ruling that such a person (muhsar bi'l-hajj) is not free from the obligation; rather, he must later perform both a complete Hajj and a complete Umrah as qada. The Hanafi school derives this from the actions of the Prophet ﷺ at Hudaybiyyah and the command of Umar ibn al-Khattab to Abu Ayyub al-Ansari.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is tahlal (exiting ihram) after being prevented from Hajj. The ruling: upon the person is wajib to perform qada of both a Hajj and an Umrah.
The obligation is separate for each act.
2
Analyze the first proof: Prophet's Umrah at Hudaybiyyah
The Prophet was prevented (muhsar bi'l-umrah) and later performed an Umrah. This shows that prevention does not cancel the obligation; qada is required.
Although this was for Umrah, it establishes the principle for ihsar.
3
Analyze the second proof: Umar's command
Umar commanded two companions who missed Hajj to make tahlal with Umrah and then perform Hajj the next year. This explicitly shows the requirement of both Hajj and Umrah as qada.
The companions were muhsar bi'l-hajj.
4
Analyze the third proof: Aisha's incident
The Prophet told Aisha that her Umrah from Tan'im was 'in place of your Umrah' – indicating that qada substitutes for the missed act.
This supports the principle of making up missed acts.
5
Note cross-madhhab agreement
The Maliki school (via Malik) also holds this view. Some schools may require only Hajj, but the Hanafi position is consistent with the strongest evidence.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْمُحْصَرُ بِالْحَجِّ إِذَا تَحَلَّلَ فَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَةٌ. عَنْ قَتَادَةَ: سَأَلْتُ أَنَسًا: كَمِ اعْتَمَرَ النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم؟ قَالَ: أَرْبَعَ عُمْرَةُ الْحُدَيْبِيَةِ فِي ذِي الْقَعْدَةِ حَيْثُ صَدَّهُ الْمُشْرِكُونَ. (بخاري، باب كم اعتمر النبي، نمبر: 1778) أَقَالَ مَالِكٌ: وَقَدْ أَمَرَ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ، أَبَا أَيُّوبَ الأَنْصَارِيَّ، وَهَبَّارَ بْنَ الْأَسْوَدِ حِينَ فَاتَهُمَا الْحَجُّ، وَأَتَيَا يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ، أَنْ يَحِلَّا بِعُمْرَةٍ، ثُمَّ يَرْجِعَا حَلَالًا ثُمَّ يَحُجَّانِ عَامًا قَابِلًا وَيُهْدِيَانِ. (المؤطا، باب ما جاء فيمن أحصر بغير عدو: 103) عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ... أَرْسَلَنِي النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مَعَ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ إِلَى التَّنْعِيمِ فَاعْتَمَرْتُ، فَقَالَ: «هَذِهِ مَكَانَ عُمْرَتِكِ». (بخاري، باب كيف تحل الحائض، نمبر: 1556)
And the one prevented from Hajj, when he becomes free (tahlal), upon him is (obligation of) a Hajj and an Umrah. From Qatada: I asked Anas: How many Umrahs did the Prophet perform? He said: Four, the Umrah of Hudaybiyyah in Dhul Qa'dah when the polytheists prevented him. (Bukhari) Malik said: Indeed Umar ibn al-Khattab commanded Abu Ayyub al-Ansari and Habbar ibn al-Aswad, when they missed the Hajj and came on the Day of Sacrifice, to make tahlal with an Umrah, then return in a state of tahlal, then perform Hajj the following year and offer sacrifices. (Muwatta) From Aisha: She said: We went out with the Prophet in the Farewell Hajj... the Prophet sent me with Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr to Tan'im and I performed Umrah, and he said: 'This is in place of your Umrah.' (Bukhari)
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with multiple proofs. The matn states that a person prevented from Hajj (muhsar bi'l-hajj) who exits ihram (tahlal) must later make up (qada) both a Hajj and an Umrah. The Hanafi position is that the qada requires both because the original ihram was for Hajj, but by exiting early the person has failed to complete either an independent Hajj or Umrah; hence both are owed. The evidence includes: (1) the Prophet's example at Hudaybiyyah where he was prevented and later performed Umrah, (2) the practice of Umar with Abu Ayyub and Habbar, and (3) the incident of Aisha where an Umrah was substituted. The Urdu usul note (from the text) adds: 'The principle: Hajj muhsar will perform both Hajj and Umrah, such that he becomes muhsar from Hajj, he does Umrah and becomes halal, then later perform qada of Hajj at the proper time.'

Key Terms
تحلل (tahlal): Exiting the state of ihram after being prevented, usually by sending a sacrifice and shaving/trimming hair.
قضاء (qada): Making up an incomplete or missed obligatory act of worship at a later time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a person who was prevented from completing Hajj (muhsar bi'l-hajj) do after tahlal?
A) Only perform Hajj the next year
B) Only perform Umrah
C) Perform both Hajj and Umrah
D) Nothing, because it was excused

Key Takeaway
A muhsar bi'l-hajj must perform qada of both Hajj and Umrah after tahlal, as supported by the Sunnah and the practice of the Companions.

Qada for Muhsar bi'l-Umrah and Qarin
Ruling with proof from hadith and tabi'i statement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the qada obligations for a muhsar bi'l-umrah and a qarin, and explain the evidence from hadith and tabi'i statements.

Core Idea
A prevented qarin must make up one Hajj and two Umrahs: one for the qiran and one for the missed Umrah.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario in Hajj: when a pilgrim is prevented (ihsar) after entering ihram. The source text from al-Quduri gives two rulings: one for a person prevented from Umrah alone, and another for a qarin. The evidence includes a hadith of Aisha and a statement of the tabi'i Hammad, with a minor disagreement from al-Hakam. Understanding these rulings clarifies the compensatory obligations in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
First, a muhsar bi'l-umrah must perform qada (make up) the Umrah. Second, a qarin who is prevented must make up one Hajj and two Umrahs.
The qada is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
2
Locate the first proof
For the muhsar bi'l-umrah, the evidence is the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet sent her to Tan'im to perform an Umrah in place of the one she missed.
This hadith is from Bukhari (1556).
3
Locate the second proof
For the qarin, the evidence is the statement of Hammad (a tabi'i) in the Musannaf of Ibn Abi Shaybah: 'upon him is one Hajj and two Umrahs.'
Hammad's statement is used as a proof (qawl sahabi/tabi'i) in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Al-Hakam disagreed with Hammad and required three Umrahs instead of two. The Hanafi school follows Hammad.
The difference is based on whether the qiran counts as one act or two.
5
Apply the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (one Hajj and two Umrahs) is the mufta bihi. The reasoning: the qarin's ihram includes both Hajj and Umrah; when prevented, each must be compensated. The one Hajj compensates for the Hajj part, and two Umrahs: one for the Umrah part of qiran and one for the missed Umrah (if the intention was qiran for Hajj and Umrah separately).
Some later scholars explain that the two Umrahs are because the qarin essentially intended two Umrahs (one for qiran and one separate) or because the qiran itself is considered as two units.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَلَى الْمُحْصَرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ الْقَضَاءُ وَعَلَى الْقَارِنِ حَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَتَانِ. عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم فِي حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ... أَرْسَلَنِي النَّبِيُّ صلى الله عليه وسلم مَعَ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبِي بَكْرٍ إِلَى التَّنْعِيمِ فَاعْتَمَرْتُ، فَقَالَ: هَذِهِ مَكَانَ عُمْرَتِكِ. (بخاري، باب كيف تحل الحائض، نمبر: 1556) عَنْ حَمَّادٍ، فِي رَجُلٍ أَهَلَّ بِعُمْرَةٍ وَحَجَّةٍ، فَأُحْصِرَ قَالَ: يَبْعَثُ بِالْهَدْيِ، فَإِذَا بَلَغَ الْهَدْيُ فَحِلَّهُ أَحَلَّ، وَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَتَانِ. وَقَالَ الْحَكَمُ: عَلَيْهِ حَجَّةٌ وَثَلَاثُ عُمَرَ. (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة، نمبر: 12797)
And upon the one prevented from Umrah is qada (making it up), and upon the qarin (combining Hajj and Umrah) is (qada of) one Hajj and two Umrahs. From Aisha: She said: We went out with the Prophet in the Farewell Hajj... the Prophet sent me with Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr to Tan'im and I performed Umrah, and he said: 'This is in place of your Umrah.' (Bukhari) From Hammad regarding a man who entered ihram for Umrah and Hajj and was prevented: He said: He sends the sacrificial animal, and when the animal reaches its place he becomes halal, and upon him is (qada of) one Hajj and two Umrahs. And al-Hakam said: Upon him is one Hajj and three Umrahs. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah)
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage provides two rulings. First, a person prevented from Umrah (muhsar bi'l-umrah) must make it up (qada) later. The evidence is the hadith of Aisha where the Prophet substituted an Umrah for her. Second, a qarin (one who combined Hajj and Umrah) who is prevented must make up one Hajj and two Umrahs: one Umrah for the qiran and one for the missed Umrah, plus the Hajj. The evidence from Hammad (a Tabi'i) explicitly states this, though there is a slight ikhtilaf with al-Hakam requiring three Umrahs. The Hanafi position adopts one Hajj and two Umrahs. The Urdu usul note (from the text) states: 'The principle: For the qarin, one Hajj and two Umrahs become obligatory.' This is based on the fact that the qarin had a single ihram for both, but when prevented, he must complete both by separate acts.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada): Making up an incomplete or missed pilgrimage act.
قارن (qarin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram (qiran).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
How many Umrahs must a qarin (one who combined Hajj and Umrah) make up if prevented?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
A qarin prevented from completing pilgrimage must make up one Hajj and two Umrahs, based on the statement of Hammad and the hadith of Aisha.

Ruling on Tahlal When Ihsar is Removed
Ruling with proof: three scenarios for tahlal after ihsar removal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three scenarios for tahlal when ihsar is removed after sending a hadi, and apply the Hanafi ruling of istihsan for the third scenario.

Core Idea
When ihsar lifts, tahlal depends on ability to catch hadi and Hajj; if only Hajj remains, istihsan permits tahlal.

In this lesson, we examine the detailed ruling of al-Quduri on the situation where a muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj) has sent a sacrificial animal (hadi) to be slaughtered on a specific day, and then the prevention is removed. The ruling distinguishes three outcomes based on whether the muhsar can still catch the hadi and/or the Hajj. The Hanafi school uses istihsan to allow tahlal when the Hajj is still possible but the hadi is lost, deviating from strict analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial act and condition
The muhsar has sent a hadi and appointed a day for its slaughter; then the prevention (ihsar) is removed. This sets up the scenarios.
2
Analyze the first scenario — both hadi and Hajj reachable
If the muhsar can catch up with both the hadi (not yet slaughtered) and the Hajj (time still available), he must remain in ihram and proceed with Hajj. Tahlal is not permissible.
This is the straightforward case: both original and substitute are achievable, so the original obligation remains.
3
Analyze the second scenario — only hadi reachable
If the muhsar can catch the hadi but cannot catch the Hajj (Hajj time has passed), he may perform tahlal. The original Hajj is no longer possible, so the substitute (hadi) fulfills the purpose.
Here, tahlal is allowed without need for istihsan.
4
Analyze the third scenario — only Hajj reachable but not hadi
If the hadi has already been slaughtered or cannot be caught, but the Hajj can still be performed, the Hanafi ruling allows tahlal by istihsan (juristic preference). Strict qiyas would require continuing in ihram because the original act (Hajj) is still possible.
Istihsan overrides qiyas because the hadi’s purpose (sacrifice) is fulfilled, removing the need for further ihram.
5
Understand the evidence and ikhtilaf
The Hanafi position is supported by a narration from Ibn Abbas distinguishing between one who breaks Hajj for pleasure (requires compensation) and one who is detained. Malik and others hold a different view, allowing tahlal anywhere without qada, based on the Hudaybiyyah incident.
This shows that the ruling is mukhtalaf fih; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا بَعَثَ الْمُحْصَرُ هَدْيًا وَوَاعَدَهُمْ أَنْ يَذْبَحُوهُ فِي يَوْمٍ بِعَيْنِهِ ثُمَّ زَالَ الْإِحْصَارُ فَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى إِدْرَاكِ الْهَدْيِ وَالْحَجِّ لَمْ يَجُزْ لَهُ التَّحَلُّلُ وَلَزِمَهُ الْمُضِيُّ وَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى إِدْرَاكِ الْهَدْيِ دُونَ الْحَجِّ تَحَلَّلَ وَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى إِدْرَاكِ الْحَجِّ دُونَ الْهَدْيِ جَازَ لَهُ التَّحَلُّلُ اسْتِحْسَانًا. عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: إِنَّ الْبَدَلَ عَلَى مَنْ نَقَضَ حَجَّهُ بِالتَّلَذُّذِ، فَأَمَّا مَنْ حَبَسَهُ عُذْرٌ أَوْ غَيْرُ ذَلِكَ، فَإِنَّهُ يَحِلُّ وَلَا يَرْجِعُ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَهُ هَدْيَ وَهُوَ مُحْصَرٌ نَحَرَهُ، إِنْ كَانَ لَا يَسْتَطِيعُ أَنْ يَبْعَثَ بِهِ، وَإِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ أَنْ يَبْعَثَ بِهِ لَمْ يَحِلَّ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الْهَدْيُ فَحِلَّهُ. وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ وَغَيْرُهُ: يَنْحَرُ هَدْيَهُ وَيَحْلِقُ فِي أَيِّ مَوْضِعٍ كَانَ، وَلَا قَضَاءَ عَلَيْهِ، لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَأَصْحَابَهُ بِالْحُدَيْبِيَةِ تَحَلَّلُوا وَحَلَقُوا وَحَلُّوا مِنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَبْلَ الطَّوَافِ، وَقَبْلَ أَنْ يَصِلَ الْهَدْيُ إِلَى الْبَيْتِ، ثُمَّ لَمْ يُذْكَرْ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَمَرَ أَحَدًا أَنْ يَقْضُوا شَيْئًا، وَلَا يَعُودُوا لَهُ وَالْحُدَيْبِيَةُ خَارِجٌ مِنَ الْحَرَمِ. (بخاري، باب من قال ليس على المحصر بدل، نمبر: 1813)
And when the muhsar sends a hadi (sacrificial animal) and agrees with them (the people at the Haram) to slaughter it on a specific day, then the prevention is removed: if he is able to catch up with the hadi and the Hajj, it is not permissible for him to perform tahlal, and he must continue (with ihram). If he is able to catch up with the hadi but not the Hajj, he may perform tahlal. If he is able to catch up with the Hajj but not the hadi, it is permissible for him to perform tahlal by istihsan. From Ibn Abbas: Indeed the compensation is upon one who breaks his Hajj by seeking pleasure, but one who is detained by an excuse or other than that, he may become halal and does not return (i.e., no qada? Actually the context is different). And if he has a hadi and is muhsar, he slaughters it, if he cannot send it; if he can send it, he does not become halal until the hadi reaches its place. And Malik and others said: He slaughters his hadi and shaves in whatever place he is, and there is no qada upon him, because the Prophet and his companions at Hudaybiyyah performed tahlal and shaved and became halal from everything before tawaf, and before the hadi reached the House, and it is not mentioned that the Prophet commanded anyone to make up anything, nor to return to it. And Hudaybiyyah is outside the Haram. (Bukhari)
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed ruling on the situation where a muhsar has sent a sacrificial animal (hadi) and appointed a day for its slaughter, but then the preventive condition is removed. The ruling distinguishes three scenarios: (1) If he can still catch both the hadi and the Hajj (i.e., the time of Hajj), he must continue in ihram and cannot perform tahlal. (2) If he can catch the hadi (it hasn't been slaughtered yet) but cannot catch the Hajj (the time has passed), he may perform tahlal. (3) If he can catch the Hajj but the hadi has already been slaughtered (or he cannot catch it), then it is permissible for him to perform tahlal by istihsan (juristic preference). The reason for istihsan in the third scenario is that the purpose of the hadi was to enable tahlal, and since the animal has been sacrificed, the tahlal is effectively complete even if he continues to the Hajj. The evidence from Ibn Abbas and Malik's opinion (though not Hanafi) is cited to show different views. The Hanafi position is that tahlal is valid in the third scenario by istihsan, contrary to strict qiyas which would require staying in ihram until able to personally reach the Haram. The Urdu usul note (from the text) adds: 'Principle: When one is able to perform the original (asl), it is not permissible to act upon the substitute (far'). Therefore, when ihsar is removed and both Hajj and hadi are attainable, one must return to the original (continue ihram).'

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference, a method of deriving rulings that deviates from strict analogy for the sake of convenience or necessity.
هدي (hadi): A sacrificial animal sent to the Haram for rituals; here specifically the dam al-ihsar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhsar can catch up with the Hajj but not with the hadi (because it was already slaughtered), what is the ruling on tahlal?
A) He must stay in ihram and cannot tahlal
B) He may perform tahlal by istihsan
C) He must wait until next year
D) He must send another hadi

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of tahlal after removal of ihsar depends on whether the muhsar can still catch the hadi and/or the Hajj; if only the Hajj is possible, istihsan permits tahlal.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Ruling on Ihsaar for Umrah and Qaarin
Ruling on being prevented from completing Hajj/Umrah with evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ihsaar for Umrah and Qaarin, identify the proofs (Aisha hadith, Ibn Abbas qawl, Hammad qawl), and explain the scenario of re-emerging prevention.

Core Idea
A prevented Umrah pilgrim must make it up; a Qaarin owes one Hajj and two Umrahs.

The Hanafi school holds that being prevented (ihsaar) from completing Hajj or Umrah due to enemy, illness, or other valid excuse does not absolve one from the obligation of completing the rituals. The prevented pilgrim must send a sacrificial animal (hady) to the Haram and, after slaughter, may exit ihram. However, the obligation to perform the missed rituals (qada) remains – a unique ruling supported by multiple proofs. This lesson examines the rulings on ihsaar for Umrah and the Qaarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together), the conditions for exiting ihram when prevention ends, and the evidence from the Qur'an, Sunnah, and sayings of the Companions and Tabi'un.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states two obligations: (1) the one prevented from Umrah must make it up (qada), and (2) the Qaarin (combining Hajj and Umrah) when prevented owes one Hajj and two Umrahs as qada.
These are wajib obligations, not merely recommended.
2
Locate the dalil for the Umrah qada
The hadith of Aisha (Bukhari 1556) is cited: the Prophet told her that the Umrah she performed from Tan'eem was 'in place of your Umrah', indicating that a missed Umrah due to valid excuse must be compensated.
This hadith is the primary proof for the obligation of qada for a prevented Umrah.
3
Locate the dalil for the Qaarin's obligation
The saying of Hammad (Tabi'i) in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba states that a Qaarin who is prevented owes one Hajj and two Umrahs. Al-Hakam said three Umrahs, but the Hanafi reliance is on Hammad.
The Hanafi school follows the view of Hammad, not al-Hakam.
4
Analyze the scenario of re-emerging prevention
If the prevention ends but the hady has been sent, the pilgrim's duty depends on what he can catch. If he can catch both the hady and the congregation (Hajj), he must continue. If only the hady, he may exit ihram. If only the Hajj, he may exit by istihsan.
Istihsan is used here because strict analogy would require him to complete, but the loss of the animal makes completion extremely difficult.
5
Note the ikhtilaf with Malik
Malik and others hold that the prevented person may slaughter the hady anywhere and owes no qada, citing the Hudaybiyyah incident. The Hanafis respond that Hudaybiyyah was a special case (the treaty prevented the hady from reaching), and the general principle requires qada.
This disagreement is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi position is supported by strong textual evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْإِحْصَارِ
وَعَلَى الْمُحْصَرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ الْقَضَاءُ وَعَلَى الْقَارِنِ حَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَتَانِ وَإِذَا بَعَثَ الْمُحْصَرُ هَدْيًا وَوَاعَدَهُمْ أَنْ يَذْبَحُوهُ فِي يَوْمٍ بِعَيْنِهِ ثُمَّ زَالَ الْإِحْصَارُ فَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى إِدْرَاكِ الْهَدْيِ وَالْجَ لَمْ يَجْزَ لَهُ التَّحَلُّلُ وَلَزِمَهُ الْمُضِيُّ وَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى إِدْرَاكِ الْهَدْيِ دُونَ الْجَ تَخَلَّلَ وَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى إِدْرَاكِ الْحَجَ دُونَ الْهَدْيِ جَازَ لَهُ التَّحَلُّلُ اسْتِحْسَانًا
وجه (۳) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَالْمُحْصَرُ بِالْجَ إِذَا تَحَلَّلَ فَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَةٌ \ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: «إِنَّا البَدَلُ عَلَى مَنْ نَقَضَ حَجَّهُ بِالتَّلَذُّذِ، فَأَمَّامَنْ حَبَسَهُ عُذْرٌ أَوْ غَيْرُ ذَلِكَ، فَإِنَّهُ يَحِلُّ وَلَا يَرْجِعُ، وَإِنْ كَانَ مَعَهُ هَدْيَ وَهُوَ مُحْصَرٌ تَخَرَهُ، إِنْ كَانَ لاَ يَسْتَطِيعُ أَنْ يَبْعَثَ بِهِ، وَإِنِ اسْتَطَاعَ أَنْ يَبْعَثَ بِهِ لَمْ يَحِلَّ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ الهَدْيُ فَحِلَّهُ» وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ وَغَيْرُهُ: يَنْحَرُ هَدْيَهُ وَيَحْلِقُ فِي أَيِّ مَوْضِعِ كَانَ، وَلَا قَضَاءَ عَلَيْهِ، لِأَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأَصْحَابَهُ بِالْحُدَيْبِيَةِ تَحَرُوا وَحَلَقُوا وَحَلُّوا مِنْ كُلِّ شَيْءٍ قَبْلَ الطَّوَافِ، وَقَبْلَ أَنْ يَصِلَ الهَدْيُ إِلَى البَيْتِ، ثُمَّ لَمْ يُذْكَرْ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَمَرَ أَحَدًا أَنْ يَقْضُوا شَيْئًا، وَلاَ يَعُودُوا لَهُ وَالحَدَيْبِيَةُ خَارِجٌ مِنَ الحَرَمِ (بخاري: بَابُ مَنْ قَالَ: لَيْسَ عَلَى المُحْصَر بَدَل نمبر: 1813)
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَعَلَى الْمُحْصَرِ بِالْعُمْرَةِ الْقَضَاءُ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، زَوْجِ
النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، قَالَتْ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ. أَرْسَلَنِي النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مَعَ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ أَبي بَكْرٍ إِلَى التَّنْعِيمِ فَاعْتَمَرْتُ، فَقَالَ: هَذِهِ مَكَانَ عُمْرَتِكِ» (بخاري بَابٌ : كَيْفَ تُهِلُ الحَائِضُ وَالنُّفَسَاءُ، نمبر: 1556)
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَعَلَى الْقَارِنِ حَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَتَانِ \ عَنْ حَمَّادٍ، فِي رَجُلٍ أَهَلَّ بِعُمْرَةٍ وَحَجَّةٍ، فَأَحْصِرَ قَالَ: «يَبْعَثُ بِالهَدْيِ، فَإِذَا بَلَغَ الْهَدْيُ فَحِلَّهُ أَحَلَّ، وَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةٌ وَعُمْرَتَانِ وَقَالَ الْحَكَمُ: «عَلَيْهِ حَجَّةٌ وَثَلَاثُ عُمَرَ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة في الرَّجُلِ يَجْمَعُ بَيْنَ الْحَجَ وَالْعُمْرَةِ، فَيَحْصُرُ مَا عَلَيْهِ فِي قَابِل؟، نمبر: 12797)
اصول: اصل پر قدرت ہونے کے باوجود فرع پر عمل کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، لہذا ایسے موقع پر احصار ختم ہوا کہ حج اور ہری دونوں کا ملنا ممکن ہے تو حج اصل ہے، اسلئے فورا اصل کی طرف کی رجوع کرنا چاہیئے۔
اصول: احناف: عمرہ پر بھی احصار کی گنجائش ہے، لہذ ا عمرہ کا محصر دم دیگر حلال ہو جائے اور قضاء کرے۔ اصول قارن پر ایک حج اور دو عمرے لازم ہونگے۔
Chapter of Ihsaar (Prevention). And upon the one prevented from completing Umrah is making it up (qada). And upon the Qaarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) is one Hajj and two Umrahs. And when the prevented person sends a sacrificial animal and appoints them to slaughter it on a specific day, then the prevention ceases, then if he is able to catch the animal and the congregation, it is not permissible for him to exit ihram and he must continue. If he is able to catch the animal but not the congregation, he may exit ihram. If he is able to catch the Hajj but not the animal, it is permissible for him to exit ihram by istihsan. Proof (3): Saying of a Companion to establish: 'And the one prevented from Hajj, when he exits ihram, he owes one Hajj and one Umrah.' From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them): 'Indeed the substitute is upon one who broke his Hajj by enjoyment. As for one whom an excuse or other than that detained, he exits ihram and does not return. And if he has an animal with him and he is prevented, he slaughters it. If he cannot send it, he does not exit until the animal reaches its destination.' Malik and others said: He slaughters his animal and shaves wherever he is, and there is no qada upon him, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) and his companions at Hudaybiyyah exited ihram and shaved and became halal from everything before tawaf and before the animal reached the House. Then it is not mentioned that the Prophet ordered anyone to make up anything or return. And Hudaybiyyah is outside the Haram. (Bukhari: Chapter: He who said there is no compensation for the prevented, no. 1813) Proof (1): Hadith to establish: 'And upon the one prevented from Umrah is qada.' From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her), wife of the Prophet (peace be upon him), she said: We went out with the Prophet in the Farewell Hajj. The Prophet sent me with Abdur-Rahman bin Abi Bakr to Tan'eem, and I performed Umrah. He said: 'This is in place of your Umrah.' (Bukhari: Chapter: How a menstruating woman and a postpartum woman enter ihram, no. 1556) Proof (1): Saying of a Tabi'i to establish: 'And upon the Qaarin is one Hajj and two Umrahs.' From Hammad concerning a man who entered ihram for Umrah and Hajj and was prevented. He said: 'He sends the animal, and when the animal reaches its destination, he exits ihram, and he owes one Hajj and two Umrahs.' Al-Hakam said: 'He owes one Hajj and three Umrahs.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba: On a man who combines Hajj and Umrah and is prevented, what does he owe the following year?, no. 12797) Usul: It is not permissible to act upon the branch while having power over the origin. Therefore, in a situation where the prevention ends such that it is possible to catch both Hajj and the animal, the Hajj is the origin, so one should immediately return to the origin. Usul: According to the Hanafis, prevention applies also to Umrah. Therefore, the one prevented from Umrah slaughters the animal and becomes halal and performs qada. Usul: Upon the Qaarin, one Hajj and two Umrahs become obligatory.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the chapter of Ihsaar (prevention from completing Hajj or Umrah). It begins by stating the basic rule: a person prevented from completing Umrah must make it up (qada), and a Qaarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram) owes one Hajj and two Umrahs. Then it details a scenario: if the prevented person had sent a sacrificial animal (hady) with a promise to slaughter on a specific day, and then the prevention is removed, the ruling depends on what he can still catch. If he can catch both the animal and the congregational Hajj, he must continue and cannot exit ihram. If he can catch the animal but not the congregation, he may exit ihram. If he can catch the Hajj but not the animal, he may exit by istihsan (juristic preference).

The proofs follow. The first proof (labeled as 'وجه (۳)') is the statement of the Companion Ibn Abbas, which differentiates between one who breaks his Hajj by sexual intercourse and one who is prevented by an excuse. For the latter, he may exit ihram without returning to complete the Hajj, but if he has an animal he must send it; if unable, he can slaughter. The text then reports Malik's view: he slaughters anywhere and no qada is required, citing the incident of Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet and his companions exited ihram before the animal reached the Kaaba. The Hanafi response, implied by the inclusion of this view, is that the Hudaybiyyah case was a special situation (the animal was stopped by the treaty), and the general rule is that qada is required. The second proof (from Aisha) directly supports the ruling that a person prevented from Umrah must make it up. The third proof (from Hammad and al-Hakam) establishes that a Qaarin when prevented owes one Hajj and two Umrahs, with al-Hakam saying three Umrahs. The usul notes in Urdu at the end explain Hanafi principles: when able to catch the origin (Hajj), one must prefer it over the branch; Umrah also has ihsaar; and the Qaarin owes one Hajj and two Umrahs.

Key Terms
الإحصار (al-ihsaar): The state of being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to enemy, illness, or other valid excuse after entering ihram.
المحصر (al-muhsar): The person who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah.
القارن (al-qaarin): A person who performs Hajj and Umrah together in a single ihram.
القضاء (al-qada'): Making up a missed or invalidated act of worship at a later time. Here it refers to performing a new Hajj or Umrah in a future year.
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram by a pilgrim who is prevented, to be slaughtered as a prerequisite to exiting ihram.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; a Hanafi method of departing from strict analogy (qiyas) for a more equitable ruling. Here, it allows tahallul when the animal cannot be caught but the Hajj can.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what does a Qaarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) owe if he is prevented (muhsar) from completing both?
A) One Hajj only
B) One Hajj and one Umrah
C) One Hajj and two Umrahs
D) One Hajj and three Umrahs

Key Takeaway
A prevented Umrah pilgrim must make it up; a Qaarin owes one Hajj and two Umrahs; the use of istihsan allows flexibility when catching the hady is impossible.

Ruling on Ihsaar within Makkah
Ruling on ihsaar with proof and usul clarification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ihsaar for a person in Makkah and apply it to cases where only one of the two arkan is missed.

Core Idea
Ihsaar in Makkah occurs only when prevented from both wuqoof and tawaf, not just one.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario: a person who enters ihram for Hajj from within Makkah but is then prevented from performing the two essential pillars—standing at Arafat (wuqoof) and the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ziyarah). The passage establishes when such a person is considered muhsar and when he is not, citing a proof from Imam Malik and then clarifying the Hanafi position through usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and ruling
Read the Arabic text and note the key condition: prevention (man') from both wuqoof and tawaf. If prevented from both, he is muhsar; if able to do one, he is not muhsar.
The term 'muhsar' means one who is prevented and must exit ihram with a sacrifice.
2
Examine the proof (dalil)
The author cites a statement from Imam Malik (a Tabi'i) in the Muwatta. Malik was asked about various excuses (fracture, illness, childbirth) and said such a person is muhsar like those from distant lands.
This proof is a qawl of a Tabi'i, which is a source used by Hanafis but with lower authority than Quran and Sunnah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi usul distinction
The usul notes explain that wuqoof is the foundation of Hajj. If one performs wuqoof and is later prevented from tawaf, it is not ihsaar; the Hajj is valid but a dam is due for delaying tawaf. Only prevention from both makes one muhsar.
This distinction is based on the principle that the rukn (pillar) of Hajj is primarily wuqoof, and tawaf is also a rukn but its omission can be compensated in certain cases.
4
Note the cross-madhhab element
Imam Malik's statement (as cited) seems to treat all excuses equally, equating them to ihsaar. The Hanafis restrict ihsaar to prevention from both arkan, showing a more nuanced definition.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is that on the Maliki view, missing any ritual due to an excuse makes one muhsar; on the Hanafi view, only missing both arkan qualifies.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a person who does wuqoof but then breaks his leg and cannot perform tawaf. According to the Hanafi ruling, he is not muhsar; his Hajj is valid but he must pay dam for delaying tawaf. If he missed both, he is muhsar and must repeat Hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْإِحْصَارِ وَمَنْ أَحْصِرَ بِمَكَّةَ وَهُوَ ثَمُنُوعٌ مِنْ الْوُقُوفِ وَالطَّوَافِ كَانَ مُحْصَرًا فَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى أَحَدِهِمَا فَلَيْسَ مخصر
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ أَحْصِرَ بِمَكَّةَ وَهُوَ تَمَنُوعٌ مِنْ الْوُقُوفِ \ سُئِلَ مَالِكٌ عَمَّنْ أَهَلَّ مِنْ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ بِالْحَجَ. ثُمَّ أَصَابَهُ كَسْرٌ، أَوْ بَطْنٌ مُتَحَرَقٌ، أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ تُطْلَقُ قَالَ: «مَنْ أَصَابَهُ هَذَا مِنْهُمْ فَهُوَ مُحْصَرٌ يَكُونُ عَلَيْهِ مِثْلُ مَا عَلَى أَهْلِ الْآفَاقِ، إِذَا هُمْ أَحْصِرُوا» (المؤطا لإمام مالك: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ أَحْصِرَ بِغَيْرِ عَدُةٍ، نمبر: 103) اصول: حج میں وقوف عرفہ اصل ہے لہذا اگر وقوف عرفہ کے بعد محصر ہوا تو یہ احصار شمار نہ ہو گا بلکہ حج ادا سمجھا جائے گا، یہ الگ بات ہے کہ طواف زیارت کو بار ہویں ذی الحجہ سے موخر کرنے سے دم لازم ہوتا ہے۔ اصول: اگر کسی کو ارکان حج یعنی وقوف عرفہ اور طواف زیارت دونوں سے روک دیا گیا تو وہ شخص مکہ میں رہتے ہوئے حل میں محصر کی طر شمار ہو گا۔
Chapter of Ihsaar. And whoever is prevented while in Makkah and is prevented from standing (at Arafat) and tawaf, he is a muhsar. But if he is able to do one of them, he is not a muhsar. Proof (1): Saying of a Tabi'i to establish: 'And whoever is prevented while in Makkah and is prevented from standing.' Malik was asked about one who entered ihram from the people of Makkah for Hajj, then suffered a fracture, or severe abdominal pain, or a woman giving birth. He said: 'Whoever among them is afflicted by this is a muhsar, and upon him is the same as upon the people of distant regions when they are prevented.' (Muwatta Imam Malik: Chapter on what has come concerning one prevented without an enemy, no. 103) Usul: In Hajj, standing at Arafat is the foundation. Therefore, if one is prevented after standing at Arafat, this is not considered ihsaar; rather, the Hajj is considered performed. This is separate from the fact that delaying the tawaf al-ziyarah beyond the 12th of Dhul-Hijjah necessitates a dam. Usul: If someone is prevented from both pillars of Hajj, i.e., standing at Arafat and tawaf al-ziyarah, then that person, while residing in Makkah, is considered a muhsar in terms of exiting ihram.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific scenario: a person who has entered ihram for Hajj from within Makkah but is then prevented from performing the two essential rituals—standing at Arafat (wuqoof) and the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ziyarah). The ruling states that if he is prevented from both, he is considered a muhsar (prevented person) and may exit ihram with the corresponding rules. However, if he is able to perform one of them, he is not a muhsar and must continue. The proof cited is from Imam Malik, who was asked about various excuses (fracture, severe illness, childbirth) and he said such a person is a muhsar and has the same obligation as a muhsar from distant lands. Though this is a Maliki view, the Hanafi usul notes at the end clarify the Hanafi position: the foundation of Hajj is wuqoof at Arafah; if one performs wuqoof and is later prevented from tawaf, it is not ihsaar but rather the Hajj is valid and only a dam is due for delaying tawaf. However, if prevented from both wuqoof and tawaf, then he is indeed a muhsar and may exit ihram. This lesson is a good example of how Hanafis define ihsaar: it applies only when one is prevented from the essential pillars (arkan), not from other obligations.

Key Terms
الوقوف (al-wuqoof): Standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah, a rukn (pillar) of Hajj.
الطواف (al-tawaf): Tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory circumambulation of the Kaaba) after coming from Arafat, a rukn of Hajj.
ركن (rukn): Pillar; an essential part of an act of worship without which the act is invalid. In Hajj, wuqoof and tawaf are arkan.
محصر (muhsar): A person who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah after entering ihram, often due to an enemy, illness, or other obstacle. The Hanafi definition in this passage specifies prevention from both arkan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul in this passage, if a person in Makkah is prevented from tawaf al-ziyarah but has already performed wuqoof at Arafat, is he considered a muhsar (prevented one)?
A) Yes, because he is prevented from a pillar
B) No, because wuqoof is the foundation and the Hajj is valid
C) Yes, because any prevention in Makkah is ihsaar
D) No, because he is not from the people of afaaq

Key Takeaway
Ihsaar in Makkah applies only when a pilgrim is prevented from both the standing at Arafat and the obligatory tawaf; prevention from one does not make one muhsar.

The Hanafi Definition of Ihsar: Prevention from Both Wuquf and Tawaf
Defining when a person in Makkah is considered muhsar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for a person in Makkah to be considered muhsar and explain why prevention from both wuquf and tawaf is required.

Core Idea
A muhsar is one prevented from both wuquf and tawaf; ability to perform one nullifies the status.

In this passage from al-Quduri, we learn the precise Hanafi definition of ihsar for a pilgrim already in Makkah. The matn lays down a clear condition: a person is only considered muhsar if he is prevented from both essential pillars: the standing at Arafah and the circumambulation of the Kaaba. The proof is drawn from a report of Imam Malik, which confirms this understanding through examples of illness and childbirth. We will unpack the ruling, the proof, and the underlying usul principles that distinguish ihsar from fawat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal act and its ruling
The act is being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah while in the state of ihram in Makkah. The ruling: if prevented from both wuquf (standing at Arafah) and tawaf (circumambulation), the person is classified as muhsar.
Note that ihsar is a specific legal status with defined consequences.
2
Locate the condition (shart) for ihsar
The matn states: 'وَمَنْ أُحْصِرَ بِمَكَّةَ وَهُوَ مَمْنُوعٌ مِنَ الْوُقُوفِ وَالطَّوَافِ كَانَ مُحْصَرًا فَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى أَحَدِهِمَا فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَرٍ'. The condition is prevention from both wuquf and tawaf. If the pilgrim is able to perform either one, he is not muhsar.
This distinguishes the Hanafi position from some other views.
3
Analyze the dalil (proof)
The proof is a narration from the Muwatta of Imam Malik. Malik was asked about specific hindrances (fracture, severe stomach illness, childbirth) and he ruled that such a person is muhsar, equating them to people from distant lands who are prevented.
The dalil is ahad (solitary) in transmission, so its certainty is zanni.
4
Derive the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
The examples in the narration involve prevention from completing both acts (wuquf and tawaf) – e.g., a woman giving birth on Arafah would be unable to stand and also unable to perform tawaf later. Thus, the narration supports the condition that both must be prevented.
The Urdu commentary clarifies that if one is prevented after wuquf, the Hajj is valid, and only tawaf delay may require a dam.
5
Note the Hanafi usul principles
The commentary states two principles: (1) wuquf is the primary pillar of Hajj; if prevented after wuquf, ihsar does not apply. (2) If prevented from both wuquf and tawaf, the person is muhsar even if remaining in Makkah.
These principles help distinguish ihsar from fawat (missing the time entirely).

Source Text

بَابُ الْإِحْصَارِ وَمَنْ أُحْصِرَ بِمَكَّةَ وَهُوَ مَمْنُوعٌ مِنَ الْوُقُوفِ وَالطَّوَافِ كَانَ مُحْصَرًا فَإِنْ قَدَرَ عَلَى أَحَدِهِمَا فَلَيْسَ بِمُحْصَرٍ. وَجْهُ: (1) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ: وَمَنْ أُحْصِرَ بِمَكَّةَ وَهُوَ مَمْنُوعٌ مِنَ الْوُقُوفِ. سُئِلَ مَالِكٌ عَمَّنْ أَهَلَّ مِنْ أَهْلِ مَكَّةَ بِالْحَجِّ ثُمَّ أَصَابَهُ كَسْرٌ أَوْ بَطْنٌ مُتَحَرَّقٌ أَوِ امْرَأَةٌ تُطْلَقُ قَالَ: «مَنْ أَصَابَهُ هَذَا مِنْهُمْ فَهُوَ مُحْصَرٌ يَكُونُ عَلَيْهِ مِثْلُ مَا عَلَى أَهْلِ الْآفَاقِ إِذَا هُمْ أُحْصِرُوا» (الموطأ لإمام مالك: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِيمَنْ أُحْصِرَ بِغَيْرِ عَدُوٍّ، رقم: 103) أصول: حج میں وقوف عرفہ اصل ہے لہذا اگر وقوف عرفہ کے بعد محصر ہوا تو یہ احصار شمار نہ ہو گا بلکہ حج ادا سمجھا جائے گا، یہ الگ بات ہے کہ طواف زیارت کو بار ہوں ذی الحجہ سے مؤخر کرنے سے دم لازم ہوتا ہے۔ أصول: اگر کسی کو ارکان حج یعنی وقوف عرفہ اور طواف زیارت دونوں سے روک دیا گیا تو وہ شخص مکہ میں رہتے ہوئے حل میں محصر کی طرح شمار ہو گا۔
Chapter of being prevented. And whoever is prevented in Makkah while he is prevented from the standing (at Arafah) and the circumambulation, he is muhsar. If he is able to do one of them, then he is not muhsar. Proof (1): The statement of the tabi'i for confirmation: 'And whoever is prevented in Makkah while he is prevented from standing.' Malik was asked about someone who assumed ihram from the people of Makkah for Hajj, then he suffered a fracture, or a burning in the stomach, or a woman who gives birth. He said: 'Whoever is afflicted with this from them, he is muhsar, and he must do like what the people of distant lands do when they are prevented.' (Muwatta of Imam Malik: Chapter of what came regarding one who is prevented without an enemy, no. 103) Principles: In Hajj, the standing at Arafah is the primary pillar. Therefore, if someone is prevented after the standing at Arafah, this is not considered ihsar; rather, his Hajj is considered performed. However, if the tawaf al-ziyarah is delayed beyond the 11th of Dhul Hijjah, a dam (sacrifice) becomes obligatory. Principles: If someone is prevented from both pillars of Hajj, i.e., the standing at Arafah and the tawaf al-ziyarah, then that person, while staying in Makkah, is considered like a muhsar in the state of ihram.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri defines the chapter of ihsar (being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah). The matn states that a person is muhsar (one who is prevented) only if he is prevented from both wuquf (standing at Arafah) and tawaf (circumambulation of the Kaaba). If he is able to perform either one, he is not considered muhsar. The proof provided is a statement attributed to a tabi'i and a narration from Imam Malik in the Muwatta. Malik was asked about various scenarios (fracture, severe stomach illness, childbirth) and ruled that such people are muhsar and must do as those from distant lands do when prevented. The Urdu commentary clarifies two usul (principles): First, since wuquf is the essential pillar of Hajj, if one is prevented only after performing wuquf, his Hajj is still valid, though delaying tawaf al-ziyarah requires a dam. Second, if one is prevented from both wuquf and tawaf, while in Makkah (in the state of ihram), he is treated as a muhsar.

Key Terms
إحصار (ihsar): Being prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to illness, enemy, or other obstacles.
محصر (muhsar): The person who is prevented from completing his Hajj or Umrah by circumstances beyond his control.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in al-Quduri, when is a person considered muhsar (prevented) in Makkah?
A) When he is prevented from the standing at Arafah only.
B) When he is prevented from both the standing at Arafah and the circumambulation (tawaf).
C) When he is prevented from any one pillar of Hajj.
D) When he is prevented from the circumambulation only.

Key Takeaway
A person in Makkah is only considered muhsar if prevented from both wuquf at Arafah and tawaf al-ziyarah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
