Ruling on Missing the Stand at Arafah (Fawat)
Ruling on fawat (missing Hajj) with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fawat (missing wuquf at Arafah) and identify the required remedy, citing the primary proofs from the matn.

Core Idea
Missing wuquf at Arafah by dawn of 10th Dhul Hijjah invalidates Hajj; remedy: exit ihram with Umrah and make up Hajj next year, no dam.

This lesson explains the chapter of fawat from Al-Quduri's matn, which addresses the situation where a pilgrim in ihram for Hajj misses the essential standing at Arafah before dawn of the Day of Sacrifice. The passage provides the ruling, the required actions, and the proofs from Quran, Hadith, and Companions' statements.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering ihram for Hajj and then missing the wuquf at Arafah until dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The ruling is that the Hajj is fata (missed) and invalid.
The ruling is explicit: 'faqad fatahu al-hajj'.
2
Locate the remedies prescribed
The matn lists four required actions: perform tawaf, sa'i, remove ihram (tahallul), and make up the missed Hajj the following year. No dam is required.
These actions constitute the exit from the invalidated Hajj and the compensation.
3
Analyze the primary proofs
The hadith of Ibn Umar states: 'Whoever stands at Arafat by night has caught Hajj; whoever misses Arafat by night has missed Hajj, so let him exit ihram with Umrah and perform Hajj the following year.' This directly supports the ruling.
Also the verse (2:199) and hadith of Urwah ibn Mudarris are cited as supporting evidence.
4
Note the rule for Umrah
Umrah is never 'missed' in the sense of fawat; it is permissible throughout the year except for five (or four) days when it is disliked: Day of Arafah and the days of Tashriq.
The hadith of Aisha specifies the prohibition on these days.
5
Consider the epistemological weight
The ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah, the authoritative transmitted position. The hadiths are ahad (zanni al-thubut), but the ruling is firmly established in the school.
No intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is recorded on this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْفَوَاتِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - وَمَنْ أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ فَفَاتَهُ الْوُقُوفُ بِعَرَفَةَ حَتَّى طَلَعَ الْفَجْرُ مِنْ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ وَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطُوفَ وَيَسْعَى وَيَتَحَلَّلَ وَيَقْضِيَ الْحَجَّ مِنْ قَابِلٍ وَلَا دَمَ عَلَيْهِ وَالْعُمْرَةُ لَا تَفُوتُ وَهِيَ جَائِزَةٌ فِي جَمِيعِ السَّنَةِ إِلَّا خَمْسَةَ أَيَّامٍ يُكْرَهُ فِعْلُهَا فِيهَا يَوْمَ عَرَفَةَ. وَجْهُ: (1) الْآيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ: ... ثُمَّ أَفِيضُوا مِنْ حَيْثُ أَفَاضَ النَّاسُ وَاسْتَغْفِرُوا اللَّهَ (سورة البقرة، 199) وَجْهُ: (2) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ: عَنْ عُرْوَةَ بْنِ مُضَرِّسٍ ... قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ شَهِدَ صَلَاتَنَا هَذِهِ وَوَقَفَ مَعَنَا حَتَّى نَدْفَعَ وَقَدْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ لَيْلًا أَوْ نَهَارًا فَقَدْ أَتَمَّ حَجَّهُ» (الترمذي: باب ما جاء فيمن أدرك الإمام بجمع فقد أدرك الحج، رقم 891) (أبو داود: باب من لم يدرك عرفة، رقم 1949) وَجْهُ: (1) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ وَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطُوفَ: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَاتٍ بِلَيْلٍ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الْحَجَّ وَمَنْ فَاتَهُ عَرَفَاتٌ بِلَيْلٍ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ فَلْيَحِلَّ بِعُمْرَةٍ وَعَلَيْهِ الْحَجُّ مِنْ قَابِلٍ» (سنن الدارقطني: كتاب الحج، رقم 2518) وَجْهُ: (2) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ وَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطُوفَ: مَنْ أَدْرَكَ عَرَفَةَ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَقَدْ تَمَّ حَجُّهُ (سنن الدارقطني: كتاب الحج، رقم 2516 / سنن البيهقي: باب إدراك الحج بإدراك عرفة قبل طلوع الفجر من يوم النحر، رقم 9812) وَجْهُ: (1) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيَّةِ لِثُبُوتِ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ وَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطُوفَ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: «حُلَّتِ الْعُمْرَةُ فِي السَّنَةِ كُلِّهَا إِلَّا فِي أَرْبَعَةِ أَيَّامٍ: يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ وَيَوْمُ النَّحْرِ وَيَوْمَانِ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ» (سنن البيهقي: باب العمرة في أشهر الحج، رقم 8741 / مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في العمرة من قال: في كل شهر، ومن قال: متى ما شئت، رقم 12723) أصول: احرام باندھ کر دس ذی الحجہ کی صبح تک وقوف عرفہ نہ کر سکا، اس سے حج فوت ہو گیا.
Chapter of missing (Hajj). He (al-Quduri) said - may Allah have mercy on him - And whoever enters ihram for Hajj and misses the standing at Arafah until dawn of the Day of Sacrifice, then his Hajj is missed, and he must perform tawaf, sa'i, remove his ihram, and perform the missed Hajj the following year, and no dam is upon him. And Umrah is not missed, and it is permissible throughout the year except for five days in which performing it is disliked: the Day of Arafah. Proof (1): The verse for confirmation: ... 'Then depart from where the people depart and seek forgiveness of Allah' (Surah al-Baqarah, 199). Proof (2): The hadith for confirmation: from Urwah ibn Mudarris ... the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever witnesses this prayer of ours and stands with us until we depart, and had stood at Arafah before that by night or day, then his Hajj is complete' (Tirmidhi: Chapter on whoever catches the Imam at Muzdalifah has caught Hajj, no. 891; Abu Dawud: Chapter on whoever does not catch Arafah, no. 1949). Proof (1) for the statement 'his Hajj is missed and he must perform tawaf': from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever stands at Arafat by night has caught Hajj, and whoever misses Arafat by night has missed Hajj, so let him exit ihram with an Umrah and he must perform Hajj the following year' (Sunan al-Daraqutni: Book of Hajj, no. 2518). Proof (2): Saying of a Companion for confirmation: 'Whoever catches Arafah before dawn on the Day of Sacrifice, his Hajj is complete' (Sunan al-Daraqutni: Book of Hajj, no. 2516 / Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter on catching Hajj by catching Arafah before dawn of the Day of Sacrifice, no. 9812). Proof (1): Saying of a female Companion for confirmation: from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: 'Umrah is permitted throughout the year except for four days: the Day of Arafah, the Day of Sacrifice, and two days after that' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi: Chapter on Umrah in the months of Hajj, no. 8741 / Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah: regarding Umrah, those who say every month and those who say whenever you wish, no. 12723). Principle: One who enters ihram and cannot perform the standing at Arafah by the morning of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah has missed Hajj.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage from al-Quduri is the chapter of fawat (missing Hajj). The matn states that if a person enters ihram for Hajj but misses the wuquf at Arafah before dawn of the Day of Sacrifice (10th Dhul Hijjah), then his Hajj is invalid. He must still perform tawaf al-umrah, sa'i, and exit ihram, and then make up the missed Hajj the following year. No dam (penalty sacrifice) is required. The matn also notes that Umrah is never 'missed' in this sense; it is permissible throughout the year except for five days when it is disliked: the Day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah) as mentioned, though the hadith from Aisha says four days. The proofs include the Quranic verse commanding departure from Arafah, the hadith of Urwah ibn Mudarris on catching Hajj by joining the imam at Muzdalifah after having stood at Arafah, and the hadith of Ibn Umar explicitly stating that missing Arafah at night means missing Hajj, with the remedy of performing Umrah and redoing Hajj. The Urdu usul summary restates: one who cannot stand at Arafah by dawn of 10th Dhul Hijjah has missed Hajj.

Key Terms
فوات (fawat): The state of having missed the time for a required act, specifically the standing at Arafah in Hajj.
وقوف عرفة (wuquf Arafah): The obligatory standing at Arafah on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah; the essential pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Quduri, what is the ruling for someone who enters ihram for Hajj but misses the standing at Arafah until dawn of the Day of Sacrifice?
A) His Hajj is still valid; he just needs to sacrifice an animal.
B) His Hajj is missed; he must perform tawaf, sa'i, exit ihram, and redo Hajj next year without paying a dam.
C) His Hajj is missed; he must perform tawaf and sa'i but does not need to redo Hajj.
D) His Hajj is valid if he completes the other rites; no compensation needed.

Key Takeaway
Missing wuquf at Arafah by dawn invalidates Hajj; the Hanafi remedy is to exit ihram with Umrah and make up Hajj the following year without dam.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Missing Hajj (Fawat al-Hajj)
Ruling on missing wuquf at Arafah and its consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when wuquf at Arafah is missed and identify the required actions and exemption from dam.

Core Idea
Missing wuquf at Arafah invalidates Hajj, but no dam is due — only qada.

Hajj is a pillar of Islam with specific rites. The most critical rite is standing at Arafah. But what if a pilgrim misses it? The Hanafi school has a clear ruling that not only defines the consequences but also exempts the person from a blood sacrifice. In this lesson, we will examine the matn of Al-Quduri and the proofs that establish this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon: missing wuquf at Arafah. The ruling is fawat (invalid) of the Hajj. Note the precise time threshold: before dawn of Yawm al-Nahr.
The act is not a commission but an omission.
2
List the required actions after fawat
The matn specifies that the person must perform tawaf, sa'y, and tahallul to exit ihram, and then make up the Hajj (qada) the following year. Importantly, no dam is required.
3
Locate the primary proof
The main dalil is the hadith of Ibn Umar from Darqutni: 'Whoever misses Arafat by night has missed the Hajj, so let him exit ihram for Umrah and perform Hajj the following year.' This directly supports the ruling.
The hadith is ahad, so thubut is zanni, but it is accepted in the Hanafi school.
4
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly negates any mention of dam. In Hanafi usul, the absence of a mention in a legal context indicates the absence of the obligation. Thus, no dam is inferred.
This is a case of mafhum al-mukhalafah? Actually it's a direct statement.
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) argue that the hadith does not explicitly negate dam and analogize to other invalidations requiring dam. The Hanafi response is that the silence of the text is sufficient to establish no dam.
The mufta bihi in Hanafi is the position of no dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْفَوَاتِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - وَمَنْ أَحْرَمَ بِالْحَجِّ فَفَاتَهُ الْوُقُوفُ بِعَرَفَةَ حَتَّى طَلَعَ الْفَجْرُ مِنْ يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ وَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطُوفَ وَيَسْعَى وَيَتَحَلَّلَ وَيَقْضِيَ الْحَجَّ مِنْ قَابِلٍ وَلَا دَمَ عَلَيْهِ
وَجْهُ الْآيَةِ: لِثُبُوتِ الْحُكْمِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {ثُمَّ أَفِيضُوا مِنْ حَيْثُ أَفَاضَ النَّاسُ وَاسْتَغْفِرُوا اللَّهَ} [البقرة: 199]
وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنْ عُرْوَةَ بْنِ مُضَرِّسٍ... فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ شَهِدَ صَلَاتَنَا هَذِهِ، وَوَقَفَ مَعَنَا حَتَّى نَدْفَعَ وَقَدْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ لَيْلًا، أَوْ نَهَارًا، فَقَدْ أَتَمَّ حَجَّهُ» (الترمذي: باب ما جاء فيمن أدرك الإمام بجمع فقد أدرك الحج، رقم 891) (أبو داؤد: باب من لم يدرك عرفة، رقم 1949)
وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَاتٍ بِلَيْلٍ فَقَدْ أَدْرَكَ الْحَجَّ وَمَنْ فَاتَهُ عَرَفَاتٌ بِلَيْلٍ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ فَلْيَحِلَّ بِعُمْرَةٍ وَعَلَيْهِ الْحَجُّ مِنْ قَابِلٍ» (سنن الدار قطني: كتاب الحج، رقم 2518)
وَجْهُ قَوْلِ الصَّحَابِيِّ: مَنْ أَدْرَكَ عَرَفَةَ قَبْلَ طُلُوعِ الْفَجْرِ فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ فَقَدْ تَمَّ حَجُّهُ (سنن الدار قطني: كتاب الحج، رقم 2516 / سنن البيهقي: باب إدراك الحج بإدراك عرفة قبل طلوع الفجر من يوم النحر، رقم 9812)
وَجْهُ قَوْلِ الصَّحَابِيَّةِ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: حَلَّتِ الْعُمْرَةُ فِي السَّنَةِ كُلَّهَا إِلَّا فِي أَرْبَعَةِ أَيَّامٍ: يَوْمُ عَرَفَةَ وَيَوْمُ النَّحْرِ وَيَوْمَانِ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ (سنن البيهقي: باب العمرة في أشهر الحج، رقم 8741 / مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في العمرة من قال في كل شهر ومتى ما شئت، رقم 12723)
اصول: احرام باندھ کر دس ذی الحجہ کی صبح تک وقوف عرفہ نہ کر سکا، اس سے حج فوت ہو گیا۔
Chapter of Missed (Hajj). He (Quduri) said - may Allah have mercy on him - : Whoever enters ihram for Hajj and misses the standing at Arafah until dawn of the Day of Nahr, then his Hajj is missed, and he must perform tawaf, sa'y, remove his ihram, and make up the Hajj the following year, and there is no blood sacrifice upon him. The evidence from the verse: to establish the ruling, His statement: 'Then depart from wherever the people depart and ask forgiveness of Allah' [al-Baqarah 199]. The evidence from the hadith: from Urwah ibn Mudarris... the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever attends this prayer of ours and stands with us until we depart, having stood at Arafah before that by night or day, has completed his Hajj.' (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud). The evidence from the hadith: from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever stands at Arafat by night has caught the Hajj, and whoever misses Arafat by night has missed the Hajj, so let him exit ihram for Umrah and must perform Hajj the following year.' (Darqutni). The evidence from the saying of a Companion: 'Whoever catches Arafah before dawn on the Day of Nahr has completed his Hajj.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi). The evidence from the saying of a Female Companion: from Aishah (may Allah be pleased with her) she said: 'Umrah is permissible throughout the entire year except for four days: the Day of Arafah, the Day of Nahr, and two days after that.' (Bayhaqi, Ibn Abi Shaybah). Principle: Whoever bound ihram and could not perform wuquf at Arafah by the morning of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, his Hajj is missed.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs on the legal consequences of missing the wuquf at Arafah in Hajj. The matn from Al-Quduri states: anyone who enters ihram for Hajj but fails to stand at Arafah before dawn of the 10th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Nahr) has missed Hajj. Such a person must perform tawaf around the Ka'bah (seven circuits) and sa'y between Safa and Marwah, then remove their ihram by shaving or trimming hair (tahallul). They are obligated to make up the missed Hajj the following year, and importantly, no blood sacrifice (dam) is required for the missed Hajj. The text then provides several proofs: first, a Quranic verse (2:199) which, though general, is cited as supporting the timing of departure from Arafah. Second, a hadith from Urwah ibn Mudharris indicating that standing at Arafah before dawn of Yawm al-Nahr constitutes catching Hajj. Third, a hadith from Ibn Umar explicitly stating that missing Arafat by night means missing Hajj, with the instruction to exit ihram by performing Umrah and repeating Hajj next year. Fourth, a saying of a Companion (Ibn Umar or similar) affirming that catching Arafah before dawn on the Day of Nahr completes Hajj. Fifth, a saying of Aishah restricting the permissibility of Umrah to exclude four days, which indirectly supports the timing. The Urdu summary reinforces that missing wuquf by dawn of the 10th results in a missed Hajj. Note: The hadith from Aishah regarding Umrah is cited here as part of the proofs for the fawat ruling, but it actually relates to the following topic on Umrah; this may be a scribal insertion. The Hanafi position is clear: no dam is required for the missed Hajj; only qada (makeup) is necessary.

Key Terms
فوات (fawat): The legal concept of missing a key ritual act in Hajj (wuquf at Arafah) such that the Hajj is no longer valid.
قضاء (qada): Making up a missed or invalid Hajj in a subsequent year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a person do if they miss wuquf at Arafah before dawn of Yawm al-Nahr?
A) They must offer a dam and continue with the remaining rituals.
B) They must perform tawaf, sa'y, remove ihram, and make up the Hajj next year without a dam.
C) They must sacrifice a camel and perform Hajj the next year.
D) They are free from any obligation and do not need to repeat Hajj.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, missing wuquf at Arafah before dawn of Yawm al-Nahr invalidates Hajj, requiring the pilgrim to perform tawaf, sa'y, and tahallul, and to make up Hajj next year without any dam.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Time and Legal Status of 'Umrah in the Hanafi School
Rulings on 'Umrah: it is not missed, permissible all year except five days, and it is sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the permissibility of 'Umrah throughout the year, identify the five days when it is disliked, and explain why the Hanafi school classifies 'Umrah as sunnah rather than wajib.

Core Idea
Umrah is an emphasized sunnah, never missed, and may be performed any day except the five days of Hajj sacrifice and tashreeq.

This lesson examines the legal framework for 'Umrah (the lesser pilgrimage) according to the Hanafi school. We learn that unlike Hajj, 'Umrah does not have a fixed time and is never considered 'missed'. However, performing it on five specific days of Dhul Hijjah is disliked. The central debate in this passage revolves around whether 'Umrah is obligatory or merely a sunnah; the Hanafi school, relying on explicit prophetic words and other evidences, holds it to be an emphasized sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Extract the three explicit rulings from the matn
Read the first part of the matn: 'And 'Umrah is not missed, and it is permissible throughout the entire year except for five days... and 'Umrah is a sunnah.' Identify these three rulings.
The matn is concise; these are the foundational statements.
2
Identify the disliked days and their proof
The matn lists five days: Day of Arafah, Day of Nahr, and the three Days of Tashreeq. The proof cited is a saying of a Tabi'i that after Tashreeq one may perform 'Umrah at any time, implying that before that is disliked.
This shows the time restriction is based on practice of the early generation.
3
Analyze the hadith of Jabir as evidence for sunnah
The hadith quotes the Prophet explicitly answering 'No' when asked if 'Umrah is obligatory, adding that performing it is better. This is the primary Hanafi proof that 'Umrah is not fard.
The word 'la' is explicit negation of obligation; 'afdal' indicates recommendation.
4
Consider the counter-evidence for obligation
The passage also cites the hadith of Zayd ibn Thabit calling Hajj and 'Umrah 'fariqatan' and the saying of Ibn Abbas declaring 'Umrah obligatory. These are presented as the opposing view.
The Hanafi school responds by interpreting 'fariqatan' as 'legally prescribed acts' not equally obligatory, and prioritizes the explicit hadith of Jabir.
5
Summarize the pillars of 'Umrah
The Urdu note at the end lists three pillars: ihram, tawaf of the Kaaba, and sa'y between Safa and Marwah. These are the essential acts; omission of any invalidates the 'Umrah.
No mention of halq/taqsir as a pillar here, but in other texts it is a wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالْعُمْرَةُ لَا تَفُوتُ وَهِيَ جَائِزَةٌ فِي جَمِيعِ السَّنَةِ إِلَّا خَمْسَةَ أَيَّامٍ يُكْرَهُ فِعْلُهَا فِيهَا: يَوْمَ عَرَفَةَ وَيَوْمَ النَّحْرِ وَأَيَّامَ التَّشْرِيقِ. وَالْعُمْرَةُ سُنَّةٌ
وَجْهُ قَوْلِ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنِ الْعُمْرَةِ فَقَالَ: إِذَا مَضَتْ أَيَّامُ التَّشْرِيقِ فَاعْتَمِرْ مَتَى شِئْتَ إِلَى قَابِلٍ (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: في العمرة من قال في كل شهر ومتى ما شئت، رقم 12724)
وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنْ جَابِرٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ سُئِلَ عَنِ الْعُمْرَةِ أَوَاجِبَةٌ هِيَ؟ قَالَ: «لَا، وَأَنْ تَعْتَمِرُوا هُوَ أَفْضَلُ» (الترمذي: باب ما جاء في العمرة أواجبة هي أم لا؟ رقم 931 / سنن البيهقي: باب من قال العمرة تطوع، رقم 8750)
وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِنَّ الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ فَرِيضَتَانِ لَا يَضُرُّكَ بِأَيِّهِمَا بَدَأْتَ» (سنن الدار قطني: كتاب الحج، رقم 2718 / سنن البيهقي: باب من قال بوجوب العمرة استدلالاً بقول الله تعالى {وأتموا الحج والعمرة لله} [البقرة: 196]، رقم 8760)
وَجْهُ قَوْلِ الصَّحَابِيِّ: أَنَّ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: الْعُمْرَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ كَوُجُوبِ الْحَجِّ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا (سنن الدار قطني: كتاب الحج، رقم 2720)
وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا زَوْجِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَتْ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ... قَالَتْ: فَطَافَ الَّذِينَ كَانُوا أَهَلُّوا بِالْعُمْرَةِ بِالْبَيْتِ وَبَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ ثُمَّ حَلُّوا (بخاري: باب كيف تهل الحائض والنفساء، رقم 1556)
وَجْهُ الْحَدِيثِ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو نُعَيْمٍ... فَقَالَ لَهُمْ: «أَحِلُّوا مِنْ إِحْرَامِكُمْ بِطَوَافِ الْبَيْتِ وَبَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ وَقَصِّرُوا ثُمَّ أَقِيمُوا حَلَالًا» (بخاري: باب التمتع والإقران والإفراد بالحج، رقم 1568)
اصول: عمرہ کے ارکان تین ہیں: احرام باندھنا، طواف بیت اللہ سات شوط، سعی بین الصفاء والمروة، بس یہی عمرہ کے اعمال ہیں۔
And 'Umrah is not missed, and it is permissible throughout the entire year except for five days in which performing it is disliked: the Day of Arafah, the Day of Nahr, and the Days of Tashreeq. And 'Umrah is a sunnah. The evidence of the saying of a Tabi'i: regarding 'Umrah, he said: 'When the Days of Tashreeq have passed, perform 'Umrah whenever you wish next year.' (Ibn Abi Shaybah). The evidence of the hadith: from Jabir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was asked whether 'Umrah is obligatory. He said: 'No, and that you perform 'Umrah is better.' (Tirmidhi, Bayhaqi). The evidence of the hadith: from Zayd ibn Thabit, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, Hajj and 'Umrah are two obligations; it does not harm you with which you begin.' (Darqutni, Bayhaqi). The evidence of the saying of the Companion: that Ibn Abbas said: ''Umrah is obligatory like the obligation of Hajj for whoever has the means to do it.' (Darqutni). The evidence of the hadith: from Aishah (may Allah be pleased with her), the wife of the Prophet (peace be upon him), she said: We went out with the Prophet (peace be upon him) during the Farewell Hajj... she said: Those who had entered ihram for 'Umrah performed tawaf of the House and between Safa and Marwah, then they removed their ihram. (Bukhari). The evidence of the hadith: Abu Nu'aym narrated... He (the Prophet) said to them: 'Exit from your ihram with tawaf of the House and between Safa and Marwah, and shorten (your hair), then remain in a state of being permissible.' (Bukhari). Principle: The pillars of 'Umrah are three: binding ihram, tawaf of the House seven circuits, sa'y between Safa and Marwah; these are the only actions of 'Umrah.
Source pages p. 291

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs concerning 'Umrah. The matn states three rulings: (1) 'Umrah is not subject to fawat (i.e., it does not become 'missed' like Hajj). (2) It is permissible to perform 'Umrah any time of the year except for five days: the Day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah), the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), and the three Days of Tashreeq (11th-13th Dhul Hijjah). On these days, performing 'Umrah is makruh (disliked). (3) 'Umrah is a sunnah (commendable, not obligatory). The text then provides proofs. The Hanafi position is that 'Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), not fard. The proofs cited include: a hadith from Jabir where the Prophet explicitly says 'Umrah is not obligatory, and that performing it is better (afdal). A hadith from Zayd ibn Thabit that says Hajj and 'Umrah are 'fariqatan' (obligations), but the Hanafis interpret this as meaning they are both acts of worship with legal status, not necessarily equal in obligation. The saying of Ibn Abbas that 'Umrah is obligatory like Hajj is also cited, but the author of the sharh presents both sides and then the matn settles on sunnah. The hadith of Aishah and the narrated instruction from Abu Nu'aym show that the Prophet allowed those in ihram for Hajj to exit by performing 'Umrah, which indicates that 'Umrah is not an independent obligation but a voluntary act that can be performed separately. The Urdu summary concludes by listing the pillars of 'Umrah: ihram, tawaf, and sa'y. Note: The presence of both wajib and sunnah narrations indicates a difference of opinion; the Hanafi madhhab (as per the matn) takes the position that it is sunnah, not fard.

Key Terms
عمرة (umrah): The lesser pilgrimage to Makkah, consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa'y, and halq or taqsir.
سنة (sunnah): An act that is recommended and rewarded, but not obligatory; omission is not sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On which days is it disliked (makruh) to perform 'Umrah according to the Hanafi school?
A) The Day of Arafah and the Day of Nahr only.
B) The Day of Arafah, the Day of Nahr, and the Days of Tashreeq.
C) Only the three Days of Tashreeq.
D) Any day in the month of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Takeaway
According to the Hanafi school, 'Umrah is a recommended sunnah, permissible all year except for five days in Dhul Hijjah, and it is never considered missed.

The Hanafi Ruling on Umrah: Sunnah Mu'akkadah and Its Pillars
Ruling on Umrah being sunnah with its pillars and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on Umrah, identify its three pillars, and explain the primary proof from the hadith of Jabir, reconciling it with conflicting evidence.

Core Idea
Umrah is a sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib; its pillars are ihram, tawaf, and sa‘i.

This lesson delves into the Hanafi position on Umrah, which is considered a highly recommended sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) rather than an obligation. The matn of al-Quduri explicitly states 'Umrah is sunnah' and enumerates its components. We will examine the primary proof from the hadith of Jabir, address the conflicting hadith that appear to suggest obligation, and understand the Hanafi method of reconciliation (tawfiq).

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The matn states 'Wal-‘umratu sunnatun'. Identify the hukm level and what it means in the Hanafi school.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is a highly recommended act, omission disliked but not sinful.
2
List the Pillars (Arkan)
From the matn and the Urdu summary, list the actions that are considered pillars of Umrah. Distinguish between arkan (pillars) and wajibat (obligations) if mentioned.
The matn includes halq but later Hanafi scholars consider halq/tagsir as wajib, not rukn.
3
Analyze the Primary Proof
Examine the hadith of Jabir. Notice the Prophet's direct answer 'No' to the question of obligation. Determine the wajh al-dalalah (how it proves the ruling).
This hadith is a clear negation of wujub.
4
Address Conflicting Hadith
Consider the hadith of Zaid bin Thabit and Ibn Abbas that suggest obligation. Understand how the Hanafi school reconciles these by giving precedence to the explicit negation and interpreting the other texts as statements of emphasis or completion of an already-initiated act.
The verse 'wa atimmu al-hajja wal-umrata lillah' is interpreted as commanding completion, not initial obligation.
5
Understand the Tarjih (Preference)
The Hanafi school prefers the explicit and specific hadith of Jabir over the general or ambiguous statements. This is a standard usul principle: a specific text is given precedence over a general one when there is apparent conflict.
This tarjih results in the mufta bihi position that Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah.

بَابُ الْفَوَاتِ وَالْعُمْرَةُ سُنَّةٌ وَهِيَ الإِحْرَامُ وَالطَّوَافُ وَالسَّعَى وَالْحَلْقُ فَقَدْ فَاتَهُ الْحَجُّ وَعَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَطُوفَ عَنِ الْعُمْرَةِ، فَقَالَ: «إِذَا مَضَتْ أَيَّامُ التَّشْرِيقِ، فَاعْتَمِرْ مَتَى شِئْتَ إِلَى قَابِلِ» (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة: فِي الْعُمْرَةِ مَنْ قَالَ: فِي كُلِّ شَهْرٍ، وَمَنْ قَالَ: مَتَى مَا شِئْتَ، نمبر: 12724) وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ، أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ سُئِلَ عَنِ العُمْرَةِ أَوَاجِبَةٌ هِيَ؟ قَالَ: «لَا، وَأَنْ تَعْتَمِرُوا هُوَ أَفْضَلُ» (الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ العُمْرَةِ أَوَاجِبَةٌ هِيَ أَمْ لا؟ نمبر 931) وَعَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «إِنَّ الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ فَرِيضَتَانِ لَا يَضُرُّكُ بِأَيْهِمَا بَدَأْتَ» (سنن الدار قطني : كِتَابُ الحَجّ، نمبر : 2718) وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «الْعُمْرَةُ وَاجِبَةٌ كَوُجُوبِ الْحَجِّ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا» (سنن الدار قطني : كِتَابُ الحَجِّ، نمبر : 2720) وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا، زَوْجِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، قَالَتْ: خَرَجْنَا مَعَ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي حَجَّةِ الْوَدَاعِ، قَالَتْ: فَطَافَ الَّذِينَ كَانُوا أَهَلُّوا بِالعُمْرَةِ بِالْبَيْتِ، وَبَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ، ثُمَّ حَلُّوا، (بخاري بَابٌ : كَيْفَ تُهِلُ الحَائِضُ وَالنُّفَسَاءُ، نمبر: 1556) أَتَى أَبُو نُعَيْمٍ فَقَالَ لَهُمْ: «أَحِلُّوا مِنْ إِحْرَامِكُمْ بِطَوَافِ البَيْتِ، وَبَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ، وَقَصِرُوا، ثُمَّ أَقِيمُوا حَلالًا» (بخاري بَابُ التَّمَتُّعِ وَالإِقْرَانِ وَالإِفْرَادِ بِالحَجَ، نمبر: 1568) اصُول : عُمْرَةٍ كَارْكَانٍ تِينْ هَيْں ا احرام باندھنا، ۲ طواف بیت اللہ سات شوط،۳ سعی بین الصفاء والمروه، بس یہی عمرہ کے اعمال ہیں.
Chapter of Missing the Hajj. And Umrah is a sunnah, and it is ihram, tawaf, sa'i, and shaving. Then he has missed the Hajj, and upon him is to perform tawaf for Umrah. He said: 'When the days of Tashreeq have passed, then perform Umrah whenever you wish until next year.' (Ibn Abi Shaybah) And from Jabir that the Prophet was asked about Umrah, is it obligatory? He said: 'No, and that you perform Umrah is better.' (Tirmidhi) And from Zaid bin Thabit: 'Indeed Hajj and Umrah are two obligations; it does not harm you with which you begin.' (Darqutni) And from Ibn Abbas: 'Umrah is obligatory like the obligation of Hajj for one who can find a way.' (Darqutni) And from Aisha: 'We went out with the Prophet in the Farewell Hajj...' (Bukhari) And Abu Nu'aim came and said to them: 'Become free from your ihram by tawaf of the House and between Safa and Marwah, and shorten, then remain in a state of halal.' (Bukhari) Principles: Umrah has three pillars: 1. entering ihram, 2. tawaf of the House seven circuits, 3. sa'i between Safa and Marwah. These are the actions of Umrah.
Source pages p. 292

Commentary
This passage from the chapter of Fawat (missing Hajj) presents the ruling on Umrah according to the Hanafi school. The matn states that Umrah is sunnah (recommended, not obligatory) and its pillars are ihram, tawaf of the Kaaba, sa'i between Safa and Marwah, and shaving or cutting the hair. The text then provides several hadith proofs to support the ruling. The first hadith from Jabir explicitly states that Umrah is not obligatory, and performing it is better. This is the foundation of the Hanafi position that Umrah is not fard but a highly recommended sunnah. However, another hadith from Zaid bin Thabit calls both Hajj and Umrah 'fariḍatān' (two obligations), and Ibn Abbas also considered Umrah obligatory. The Hanafi school reconciles these by considering the hadith of Jabir as specific and stronger, interpreting 'fariḍatān' as meaning they are both important acts of worship, but the obligation of Umrah is not at the same level as Hajj. The Hanafi ruling is that Umrah is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah) once in a lifetime, not wajib. The passage concludes with an Urdu summary reiterating the three pillars of Umrah.

Key Terms
الْعُمْرَةُ (al-‘umrah): A pilgrimage to the Kaaba consisting of ihram, tawaf, sa‘i, and halq/tagsir, performed at any time of the year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, what is the ruling of Umrah?
A) Wajib
B) Fard
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Umrah is a sunnah mu'akkadah once in a lifetime, with pillars of ihram, tawaf, and sa‘i; the Hanafi school relies on the explicit hadith of Jabir to establish its non-obligatory status.

Minimum Acceptable Hadi and Disqualifying Defects
Ruling on minimum hadi and disqualifying defects with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum species and age requirements for a valid hadi (sacrificial animal) according to the Hanafi school and identify which defects invalidate it, with reference to the Quran and Sunnah proofs.

Core Idea
The hadi must be at least a sheep (or a thaniyy camel/cow); it must be free from seven specified defects.

This lesson covers the essential requirements for a hadi, the animal sacrificed during Hajj by those performing tamattu' or qiran. You will learn the minimum acceptable species and age, and the defects that render it invalid. The rulings are grounded in the Quran and authentic hadith, demonstrating how the Hanafi school derives detailed conditions from general and specific texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognize that 'hadi' is an animal sent to the Haram for sacrifice, wajib for tamattu' and qiran. The passage specifies the minimum and conditions for validity.
The ruling is wajib based on Quran 2:196.
2
Determine the minimum species and age
The minimum is a sheep. For camels and cows, the animal must be thaniyy (entering second year) or older. For sheep, jadha' (one-year-old) suffices.
Thaniyy is defined as at least 2 years for cows/goats, 5 years for camels; jadha' is a sheep about 12 months old.
3
Identify the disqualifying defects
The text lists: cut ear (or most of it), cut tail, cut limb (hand or foot), blind eye, emaciated, lame. These are based on the hadith of al-Bara' with additions by qiyas.
The defects must be obvious; minor defects are overlooked.
4
Locate the proofs
The passage cites Quran 2:196 for the general principle, the hadith of Ibn Abbas (share in blood) for permissibility of sheep, the hadith of Jabir for jadha' age, and the hadith of al-Bara' for defects.
The hadith of Jabir allows jadha' when older animals are hard to find, but Hanafis accept it generally for sheep.
5
Derive the ruling
These rules are conditions for the validity of the hadi. Violation makes the animal invalid (la yujzi'). The mufta bihi position prefers jadha' only from sheep, not goats.
Intra-Hanafi difference: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allowed jadha' from goats, but the matn restricts to sheep.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْهَدْيِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - الْهَدْيُ أَدْنَاهُ شَاةٌ وَهُوَ مِنْ ثَلَاثَةِ أَنْوَاعِ الْإِبِلِ وَالْبَقَرِ وَالْغَنَمِ لَا يُجْزِئُ فِي ذَلِكَ كُلِهِ الثَّنِيُّ فَصَاعِدًا إِلَّا الضَّانَ فَإِنَّ الْجَدَعَ مِنْهُ يُجْزِئُ وَلَا يُجْزِئُ فِي الْهَدْيِ مَقْطُوعُ الْأُذُنِ وَلَا أَكْثَرِهَا وَلَا مَقْطُوعَةُ الذَّنَبِ وَلَا الْيَدِ وَلَا الرّجُل وَلَا النَّاهِبَةُ الْعَيْنِ وَلَا الْعَجْفَاءُ وَلَا الْعَرْجَاءُ وَالدَّلِيلُ عَلَى أَدْنَى الْهَدْيِ قَوْلُهُ تَعَالَى: {فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيِ} [البقرة: 196] وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: «فِيهَا جَزُورٌ أَوْ بَقَرَةً أَوْ شَاةٌ أَوْ شِرْكَ فِي دَمٍ» (رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ) وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا تَذْبَحُوا إِلَّا مُسِنَّةً إِلَّا أَنْ يَعْسُرَ عَلَيْكُمْ فَتَذْبَحُوا جَدَعَةً مِنَ الضَّأْنِ» (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ) وَعَنِ الْبَرَاءِ بْنِ عَازِبٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «أَرْبَعٌ لَا تَجُوزُ فِي الْأَضَاحِيِّ: الْعَوْرَاءُ بَيِّنٌ عَوَرُهَا، وَالْمَرِيضَةُ بَيِّنٌ مَرَضُهَا، وَالْعَرْجَاءُ بَيِّنٌ ظَلَعُهَا، وَالْكَسِيرُ الَّتِي لَا تَنْقَى» (رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَالتِّرْمِذِيُّ)
Chapter of the Hadi. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him - The hadi, its minimum is a sheep, and it is from three types: camel, cow, and sheep. Nothing suffices from all that except the thaniyy (two-year-old) and above, except for sheep, for the jadha' (one-year-old) from it suffices. And nothing suffices in the hadi: an animal with a cut ear, nor the majority of the ear, nor a cut tail, nor a cut hand or foot, nor a blind eye, nor emaciated, nor lame. And the proof for the minimum of the hadi is the saying of Allah: 'Then whatever is available of the hadi' (al-Baqarah 196). And from Ibn Abbas: 'In it (the hadi) is a camel, or a cow, or a sheep, or a share in blood.' (Narrated by Bukhari). And from Jabir: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Do not slaughter except a musinnah (older animal) unless it is difficult for you, then slaughter a jadha'ah from sheep.' (Narrated by Abu Dawud). And from al-Bara' bin 'Azib: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Four (animals) are not permissible in the sacrificial animals: the one-eyed on its blindness is clear, the sick on its sickness is clear, the lame on its lameness is clear, and the broken that has no marrow.' (Narrated by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi).
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from the Chapter of Hadi (the sacrificial animal brought to the Haram) presents the Hanafi ruling on the minimum acceptable animal and required age. The matn states that the hadi must be a sheep (the minimum), but it can also be a camel or a cow. The age requirement: for camels and cows, the animal must be thaniyy (second year, i.e., at least two years old) or older. For sheep, the jadha' (one-year-old) is acceptable. This is based on the general verse 'fama istaysara minal hadyi' (whatever is easy of the hadi) and the hadith from Jabir allowing jadha' from sheep if older animals are hard to find. The passage then lists disqualifying defects: a cut ear (or most of it), cut tail, cut limb, blind eye, emaciated, and lame. These are from the hadith of al-Bara' which mentions four defects: blind, sick, lame, and broken. The Hanafi school adds others by qiyas. The Urdu note explains that 'hadi' is an animal sent to the Haram for sacrifice. The passage emphasizes that the hadi must be free from obvious defects.

Key Terms
الْهَدْي (al-hadyu): An animal sent to the Haram (Mecca) to be sacrificed as an offering for hajj, obligatory for tamattu' and qiran.
الثَّنِيُّ (ath-thaniyyu): An animal that has entered its second year; for camels, at least 5 years; for cows and goats, at least 2 years.
الْجَدَعَ (al-jada'a): A sheep that is one year old (around 12 months) and has started to replace its baby teeth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum age for a sheep to be valid as a hadi according to this passage?
A) Two years (thaniy)
B) One year (jadha')
C) Six months
D) Three years

Key Takeaway
The hadi must be a sheep (minimum) or thaniyy camel/cow, and free from specific defects; the proofs are from Quran and authentic hadith.

Basic Conditions of Hady: Minimum, Types, Age, and Defects
Ruling with proof: conditions of Hady animal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum animal for Hady, list the three permissible types, determine the required age (thani) and the exception for sheep, and identify the defects that render a Hady animal invalid.

Core Idea
Hady minimum is a sheep; only thani and above except jada' sheep; seven defects invalidate.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational rulings of Hady (the sacrificial animal sent to the Haram). The matn of Al-Quduri establishes the minimum a sheep, the three types, the age requirement of thani (with an exception for sheep), and a list of defects that disqualify the animal. Understanding these conditions is crucial for the validity of Hajj Tamattu' and Qiran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the minimum and types
Locate the statement that the minimum Hady is a sheep (shāh) and that it comes from three types: camel, cow, and sheep/goat. This is the basic definition.
Sheep includes goats in Hanafi terminology.
2
Determine the required age
Find the rule that only a thani (animal that has entered its second year) or older is valid for Hady. Then note the exception: a jada' (around six months to one year) from sheep is acceptable due to hardship.
Thani differs by species: camel 5 years, cow 2 years, goat 1 year.
3
List the invalidating defects
Read the list of defects: cut ear (or most of it), cut tail, missing limb (hand or foot), blindness (obvious), emaciation, lameness. Each defect invalidates the Hady.
The Hadith from al-Barā' adds broken horn and sick as well, but the matn focuses on these.
4
Review the Hadith proofs
Observe that the author cites specific Hadith for each ruling: the age exception from Jābir (Abu Dawud), and the defects from al-Barā' and others. This shows the proof structure.
The Hadith are all ahad (non-mutawatir) but accepted in this context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْهَدْي
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - الْهَدْيُ أَدْنَاهُ شَاةٌ وَهُوَ مِنْ ثَلَاثَةِ أَنْوَاعِ الْإِبِلِ وَالْبَقَرِ وَالْغَنَمِ لَا يُجْزِئُ فِي ذَلِكَ كُلِهِ الثَّنِيُّ فَصَاعِدًا إِلَّا الضَّأْنَ فَإِنَّ الْجَدَعَ مِنْهُ يُجْزِئُ وَلَا يُجْزِئُ فِي الْهَدْيِ مَقْطُوعُ الْأُذُنِ وَلَا أَكْثَرِهَا وَلَا مَقْطُوعَةُ الذَّنَبِ وَلَا الْيَدِ وَلَا الرِّجْلِ وَلَا الْعَوْرَاءُ وَلَا الْعَجْفَاءُ وَلَا الْعَرْجَاءُ
لوجه:(1) الآية لثبوت الْهَدْيُ أَدْنَاهُ شَاةٌ وَهُوَ مِنْ ثَلَاثَةِ أَنْوَاعِ الْفَإِذَا أَمِنتُمْ فَمَن تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَج فَمَا أَسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيِ فَمَن لَّمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجَ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ تِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ (سورة البقرة، 2 آلاية نمبر: 195)
وجه:(۲) تفسير ابن عباس لثبوت الْهَدْيُ أَدْنَاهُ شَاةٌ وَهُوَ مِنْ ثَلَاثَةِ أَنْوَاعِ احَدَّثَنَا أَبُو جَمْرَةَ، قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، عَنِ المُتْعَةِ، فَأَمَرَنِي بِمَا، وَسَأَلْتُهُ عَنِ الهَدْيِ، فَقَالَ: «فِيهَا جَزُورٌ أَوْ بَقَرَةً أَوْ شَاةٌ أَوْ شِرْكَ فِي دَمٍ» (بخاري بَابُ فَمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الحَجَ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الهَدْيِ، نمبر: 1688)
ل وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت يُجْزِئُ فِي ذَلِكَ كُلِهِ التَّنِيُّ فَصَاعِدًا إِلَّا الضَّأْنَ اعَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لا تَذْبَحُوا إِلَّا مُسِنَّةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَعْسُرَ عَلَيْكُمْ فَتَذْبَحُوا جَدَعَةٌ مِنَ الضَّأْنِ» (أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ السِّنَ فِي الصَّحَايَا، نمبر: 2797)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُجْزِئُ فِي الْهَدْيِ مَقْطُوعُ الْأُذُنِ ا سَأَلْتُ الْبَرَاءَ بْنَ عَازِبٍ مَا لَا يَجُوزُ فِي الْأَصَاحِيِّ. فَقَالَ: قَامَ فِينَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأَصَابِعِي أَقْصَرُ مِنْ أَصَابِعِهِ، وَأَنَامِلِي أَقْصَرُ مِنْ أَنَامِلِهِ فَقَالَ: " أَرْبَعٌ لا تَجُورُ فِي الْأَصَاحِيّ - فَقَالَ : الْعَوْرَاءُ بَيِّنٌ عَوَرُهَا، وَالْمَرِيضَةُ بَيّنْ مَرَضُهَا ، وَالْعَرْجَاءُ بَيّنْ طَلْعُهَا، وَالْكَسِيرُ الَّتِي لَا تَنْقَى ". (أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الصَّحَايَا، نمبر: 2802/ الترمذي : بَابُ مَا لَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ الْأَصَاحِي، نمبر 1497)
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يُجْزِئُ فِي الْهَدْيِ مَقْطُوعُ الْأُذُنِ \ قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ عُتْبَةَ بْنَ عَبْدِ السُّلَمِيَّ فَقُلْتُ: يَا أَبَا الْوَلِيدِ إِنّى خَرَجْتُ أَلْتَمِسُ الصَّحَايَا فَلَمْ أَجِدُ شَيْئًا يُعْجِبُنِي غَيْرَ ثَرْمَاءَ فَكَرِهْتُهَا فَمَا تَقُولُ؟ قَالَ: أَفَلَا جِئْتَنِي بِهَا. قُلْتُ : سُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ تَجُوزُ عَنْكَ وَلَا تَجُوزُ عَنِي. قَالَ: نَعَمْ، إِنَّكَ تَشُكُ وَلا أَشُكُ، إنما " نَهَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَن المُصْفَرَّةِ، وَالْمُسْتَأْصَلَةِ، وَالْبَحْقَاءِ وَالْمُشَيَّعَةِ، وَكِسَرَا، وَالْمُصْفَرَّةُ: الَّتِي تُسْتَأْصَلُ أُذُنُهَا حَتَّى يَبْدُوَ سَمَاخُهَا " وَالْمُسْتَأْصَلَةُ: الَّتِي اسْتُؤْصِلَ قَرْنُهَا مِنْ أَصْلِهِ وَالْبَخْقَاءُ: الَّتي تُبْخَقُ عَيْنَهَا، وَالْمُشَيَّعَةُ: الَّتِي لَا تَتْبَعُ الْغَنَمَ عَجَفًا وَضَعْفًا، وَالْكَسْرَاءُ: الْكَسِيرَةُ " (أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الصَّحَايَا، نمبر: 2803)
وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُجْزِئُ فِي الْهَدْيِ مَقْطُوعُ الْأُذُنِ عَنْ عَلِقٍ، قَالَ: «أَمَرَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنْ نَسْتَشْرِفَ الْعَيْنَ وَالْأُذُنَيْنِ، وَلا تُضَحِي بِعَوْراءَ، وَلَا مُقَابَلَةٍ، وَلَا مُدَابَرَةٍ، وَلَا خَرْقَاءَ، وَلا شَرْقَاءَ قَالَ زُهَيْرٌ: فَقُلْتُ لِأَبِي إِسْحَاقَ : أَذَكَرَ عَصْبَاءَ؟ قَالَ: «لا» . قُلْتُ: فَمَا الْمُقَابَلَةُ؟ قَالَ: «يُقْطَعُ طَرَفُ الْأُذُنِ» . قُلْتُ : فَمَا الْمُدَابَرَةُ؟، قَالَ: «يُقْطَعُ مِنْ مُؤَخَّرِ الْأُذُنِ» قُلْتُ: فَمَا الشَّرْقَاءُ؟ قَالَ: «تُشَقُّ الْأُذُنُ» . قُلْتُ: فَمَا الْخَرْقَاءُ؟ قَالَ: «تُخْرَقُ أُذُنُهَا لِلسِّمَةِ» (أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الصَّحَايَا، نمبر: 2804)
اصول : جو جانور ذبح اور قربت کے لئے حرم بھیجا جائے اسے ہدی کہتے ہیں، تین ہیں اونٹ ۲ گائے ۳ بکری۔
وَالشَّاةُ جَائِزَةٌ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي مَوْضِعَيْنِ مَنْ طَافَ لِلزَّيَارَةِ جُنُبًا وَمَنْ جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةَ وَالْبَدَنَةُ وَالْبَقَرَةُ يُجْزِئُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ إِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الشُرَكَاءِ يُرِيدُ الْقُرْبَةَ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمْ يُرِيدُ بِنَصِيبِهِ اللَّحْمَ لَمْ يَجُزْ لِلْبَاقِينَ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالشَّاةُ جَائِزَةٌ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي مَوْضِعَيْنِ \ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، التي صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الطَّوَافُ حَوْلَ البَيْتِ مِثْلُ الصَّلاةِ، إِلَّا أَنَّكُمْ تَتَكَلَّمُونَ فِيهِ، فَمَنْ تَكَلَّمَ فِيهِ فَلَا يَتَكَلَّمَنَّ إِلَّا بِخَيْرٍ» (سنن الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الكَلَامِ فِي الطَّوَافِ نمبر: 960)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالشَّاةُ جَائِزَةٌ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي مَوْضِعَيْنِ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: قَدِمْتُ مَكَّةَ وَأَنَا حَائِضٌ وَلَمْ أَطُفْ بِالْبَيْتِ وَلا بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ قَالَتْ: فَشَكَوْتُ ذَلِكَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، قَالَ: «افْعَلِي كَمَا يَفْعَلُ الْحَاجُ غَيْرَ أَنْ لَا تَطُوفِي بِالْبَيْتِ حَتَّى تَطْهُرِي» (بخاري: بَابٌ : تَقْضِي الحَائِضُ المَنَاسِكَ كُلَّهَا إِلَّا الطَّوَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ: 1650)
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالْبَدَنَةُ وَالْبَقَرَةُ يُجْزِئُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ بْن عَبْدِ اللهِ. قَالَ: نَحَرْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَامَ الْخَدَيْنِيَةِ الْبَدَنَةَ عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ. وَالْبَقَرَةَ عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ (مسلم: بَاب الاشْتِرَاكِ فِي الْهَدْيِ، وَإِجْزَاءِ الْبَقَرَةِ وَالْبَدَنَةِ كُلّ مِنْهُمَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ، غبر: 1318)
Chapter of Hady. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him - Hady: its minimum is a sheep, and it is of three types: camels, cows, and sheep/goats. In all of that, only the thani and above is valid except for sheep, for the jadha' from it is valid. And it is not valid in Hady: one with cut ear, nor most of them (i.e., of the ear), nor one with cut tail, nor hand, nor foot, nor blind in one eye, nor emaciated, nor lame. ... And the sheep is valid in everything except in two cases: one who performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub, and one who has intercourse after standing at Arafat. And the camel and the cow, each one of them suffices for seven persons, when each of the partners intends worship; but if one of them intends meat with his share, it does not suffice for the remaining.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, expanded with Hadith proofs and Urdu commentary, covers the essential rulings of Hady (the sacrificial animal sent to the Haram for Hajj). The passage begins by stating the minimum Hady is a sheep, and it can be from three types: camel, cow, or sheep/goat. The age requirement: only animals that have reached the thani stage (i.e., second year for camels, second year for cows, first year for goats, but for sheep the jadha' – around six months to one year – is also acceptable due to ease). Then it lists defects that render the animal invalid: a cut ear or more than half of it, a cut tail, a missing limb, blindness, emaciation, or lameness. These defects are supported by multiple Hadith, including the famous narration from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib listing four defective animals. The text then adds two special rulings: a sheep is valid for all expiations and offerings except in two situations: (1) if someone performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of janabah (major impurity), and (2) if someone had intercourse after the Wuquf at Arafah. In these two cases, a sheep is not sufficient; a larger animal is needed. Then, a camel or cow can be shared among seven persons if all intend worship (qurbah); but if one partner intends only to obtain meat, the others' shares are invalid. This is based on the practice at Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet ﷺ allowed one camel for seven men. The Urdu commentary clarifies that 'hady' is an animal sent to the Haram for slaughter, and it has three types.

Key Terms
الهَدْي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal that is sent to the Haram (Mecca) to be slaughtered as an offering for Hajj or Umrah, whether wajib or tatawwu'.
الثَّنِيُّ (al-thani): An animal that has entered its second year (for camels, it is when the second year begins; for cows and goats, similar). The minimum age for a valid Hady except for sheep.
الجَدَعُ (al-jada'): A sheep that is about six months to one year old; it is acceptable for Hady even though it has not reached the thani stage, due to hardship in finding older sheep.
العَوْرَاءُ (al-'awra'): An animal blind in one eye; such an animal is invalid for Hady.
الشَّاةُ (al-shatu): A sheep (or goat) that meets the conditions; it is valid for all Hady except the two specific cases mentioned in the next lesson.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following animals is valid for Hady?
A) A three-year-old camel with a broken ear.
B) A one-year-old goat (thani) with a cut tail.
C) A six-month-old sheep (jada') with healthy ears and eyes.
D) A two-year-old cow that is blind in one eye.

Key Takeaway
A valid Hady must meet the minimum of a sheep, be from the three types, be thani (except jada' sheep), and be free from the listed defects.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Special Rulings: Sheep in Two Cases and Sharing of Camel/Cow
Ruling with proof: special exceptions and sharing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two cases where a sheep is not sufficient for Hady, and explain the conditions for sharing a camel or cow among seven persons.

Core Idea
Sheep valid for all Hady except after janabah Tawaf or intercourse at Arafat; camel/cow shared among seven with common intention.

This lesson covers two exceptional rulings from the Hady section. First, while a sheep is generally sufficient, there are two specific situations where it is not. Second, the permissibility of sharing a camel or cow among up to seven people, provided all intend worship. These rulings are essential for pilgrims who may face these circumstances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exceptions where sheep is insufficient
Find the text: 'Wal-shatu jā'izatun fī kulli shay'in illā fī mawdi'ayn: man ṭāfa lil-ziyārati junuban, wa man jāma'a ba'da al-wuqūfi bi-Arafah.' These are the only two cases where a sheep is not accepted for Hady.
In these cases, a larger animal like a camel or cow is required.
2
Understand the rationale for the exceptions
Both cases involve a major violation during Hajj: performing Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of janabah (requires a sacrifice of a camel or cow), and intercourse after Wuquf at Arafah (also requires a similar expiation). The sheep is considered too slight for these serious violations.
The exact ruling for janabah Tawaf: the Hady becomes wajib as a penalty (dam).
3
State the sharing rule for camel and cow
Read: 'Wal-badanatu wal-baqaratu yujzi'u kullu wāḥidin minhumā 'an sab'atin idhā kāna kullu wāḥidin min al-shurakā'i yurīdu al-qurbah.' This means one camel or cow suffices for seven persons, provided each partner intends qurbah (worship).
The hadith from Jabir at Hudaybiyyah confirms this practice.
4
Analyze the condition of intention
If one of the partners intends only meat (not worship), then the Hady is invalid for all. This shows that the intention of qurbah is essential for the validity of the collective sacrifice.
This is based on the principle that acts are judged by intentions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْهَدْي
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - الْهَدْيُ أَدْنَاهُ شَاةٌ وَهُوَ مِنْ ثَلَاثَةِ أَنْوَاعِ الْإِبِلِ وَالْبَقَرِ وَالْغَنَمِ لَا يُجْزِئُ فِي ذَلِكَ كُلِهِ الثَّنِيُّ فَصَاعِدًا إِلَّا الضَّأْنَ فَإِنَّ الْجَدَعَ مِنْهُ يُجْزِئُ وَلَا يُجْزِئُ فِي الْهَدْيِ مَقْطُوعُ الْأُذُنِ وَلَا أَكْثَرِهَا وَلَا مَقْطُوعَةُ الذَّنَبِ وَلَا الْيَدِ وَلَا الرِّجْلِ وَلَا الْعَوْرَاءُ وَلَا الْعَجْفَاءُ وَلَا الْعَرْجَاءُ
لوجه:(1) الآية لثبوت الْهَدْيُ أَدْنَاهُ شَاةٌ وَهُوَ مِنْ ثَلَاثَةِ أَنْوَاعِ الْفَإِذَا أَمِنتُمْ فَمَن تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَج فَمَا أَسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْيِ فَمَن لَّمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجَ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ تِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ (سورة البقرة، 2 آلاية نمبر: 195)
وجه:(۲) تفسير ابن عباس لثبوت الْهَدْيُ أَدْنَاهُ شَاةٌ وَهُوَ مِنْ ثَلَاثَةِ أَنْوَاعِ احَدَّثَنَا أَبُو جَمْرَةَ، قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، عَنِ المُتْعَةِ، فَأَمَرَنِي بِمَا، وَسَأَلْتُهُ عَنِ الهَدْيِ، فَقَالَ: «فِيهَا جَزُورٌ أَوْ بَقَرَةً أَوْ شَاةٌ أَوْ شِرْكَ فِي دَمٍ» (بخاري بَابُ فَمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الحَجَ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الهَدْيِ، نمبر: 1688)
ل وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت يُجْزِئُ فِي ذَلِكَ كُلِهِ التَّنِيُّ فَصَاعِدًا إِلَّا الضَّأْنَ اعَنْ جَابِرٍ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لا تَذْبَحُوا إِلَّا مُسِنَّةَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَعْسُرَ عَلَيْكُمْ فَتَذْبَحُوا جَدَعَةٌ مِنَ الضَّأْنِ» (أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ السِّنَ فِي الصَّحَايَا، نمبر: 2797)
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُجْزِئُ فِي الْهَدْيِ مَقْطُوعُ الْأُذُنِ ا سَأَلْتُ الْبَرَاءَ بْنَ عَازِبٍ مَا لَا يَجُوزُ فِي الْأَصَاحِيِّ. فَقَالَ: قَامَ فِينَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَأَصَابِعِي أَقْصَرُ مِنْ أَصَابِعِهِ، وَأَنَامِلِي أَقْصَرُ مِنْ أَنَامِلِهِ فَقَالَ: " أَرْبَعٌ لا تَجُورُ فِي الْأَصَاحِيّ - فَقَالَ : الْعَوْرَاءُ بَيِّنٌ عَوَرُهَا، وَالْمَرِيضَةُ بَيّنْ مَرَضُهَا ، وَالْعَرْجَاءُ بَيّنْ طَلْعُهَا، وَالْكَسِيرُ الَّتِي لَا تَنْقَى ". (أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الصَّحَايَا، نمبر: 2802/ الترمذي : بَابُ مَا لَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ الْأَصَاحِي، نمبر 1497)
وجه : (٢) الحديث لثبوت وَلا يُجْزِئُ فِي الْهَدْيِ مَقْطُوعُ الْأُذُنِ \ قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ عُتْبَةَ بْنَ عَبْدِ السُّلَمِيَّ فَقُلْتُ: يَا أَبَا الْوَلِيدِ إِنّى خَرَجْتُ أَلْتَمِسُ الصَّحَايَا فَلَمْ أَجِدُ شَيْئًا يُعْجِبُنِي غَيْرَ ثَرْمَاءَ فَكَرِهْتُهَا فَمَا تَقُولُ؟ قَالَ: أَفَلَا جِئْتَنِي بِهَا. قُلْتُ : سُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ تَجُوزُ عَنْكَ وَلَا تَجُوزُ عَنِي. قَالَ: نَعَمْ، إِنَّكَ تَشُكُ وَلا أَشُكُ، إنما " نَهَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَن المُصْفَرَّةِ، وَالْمُسْتَأْصَلَةِ، وَالْبَحْقَاءِ وَالْمُشَيَّعَةِ، وَكِسَرَا، وَالْمُصْفَرَّةُ: الَّتِي تُسْتَأْصَلُ أُذُنُهَا حَتَّى يَبْدُوَ سَمَاخُهَا " وَالْمُسْتَأْصَلَةُ: الَّتِي اسْتُؤْصِلَ قَرْنُهَا مِنْ أَصْلِهِ وَالْبَخْقَاءُ: الَّتي تُبْخَقُ عَيْنَهَا، وَالْمُشَيَّعَةُ: الَّتِي لَا تَتْبَعُ الْغَنَمَ عَجَفًا وَضَعْفًا، وَالْكَسْرَاءُ: الْكَسِيرَةُ " (أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الصَّحَايَا، نمبر: 2803)
وجه:(۳) الحديث لثبوت وَلَا يُجْزِئُ فِي الْهَدْيِ مَقْطُوعُ الْأُذُنِ عَنْ عَلِقٍ، قَالَ: «أَمَرَنَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنْ نَسْتَشْرِفَ الْعَيْنَ وَالْأُذُنَيْنِ، وَلا تُضَحِي بِعَوْراءَ، وَلَا مُقَابَلَةٍ، وَلَا مُدَابَرَةٍ، وَلَا خَرْقَاءَ، وَلا شَرْقَاءَ قَالَ زُهَيْرٌ: فَقُلْتُ لِأَبِي إِسْحَاقَ : أَذَكَرَ عَصْبَاءَ؟ قَالَ: «لا» . قُلْتُ: فَمَا الْمُقَابَلَةُ؟ قَالَ: «يُقْطَعُ طَرَفُ الْأُذُنِ» . قُلْتُ : فَمَا الْمُدَابَرَةُ؟، قَالَ: «يُقْطَعُ مِنْ مُؤَخَّرِ الْأُذُنِ» قُلْتُ: فَمَا الشَّرْقَاءُ؟ قَالَ: «تُشَقُّ الْأُذُنُ» . قُلْتُ: فَمَا الْخَرْقَاءُ؟ قَالَ: «تُخْرَقُ أُذُنُهَا لِلسِّمَةِ» (أبو داؤد: بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الصَّحَايَا، نمبر: 2804)
اصول : جو جانور ذبح اور قربت کے لئے حرم بھیجا جائے اسے ہدی کہتے ہیں، تین ہیں اونٹ ۲ گائے ۳ بکری۔
وَالشَّاةُ جَائِزَةٌ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي مَوْضِعَيْنِ مَنْ طَافَ لِلزَّيَارَةِ جُنُبًا وَمَنْ جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةَ وَالْبَدَنَةُ وَالْبَقَرَةُ يُجْزِئُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ إِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الشُرَكَاءِ يُرِيدُ الْقُرْبَةَ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمْ يُرِيدُ بِنَصِيبِهِ اللَّحْمَ لَمْ يَجُزْ لِلْبَاقِينَ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالشَّاةُ جَائِزَةٌ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي مَوْضِعَيْنِ \ عَنْ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، التي صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الطَّوَافُ حَوْلَ البَيْتِ مِثْلُ الصَّلاةِ، إِلَّا أَنَّكُمْ تَتَكَلَّمُونَ فِيهِ، فَمَنْ تَكَلَّمَ فِيهِ فَلَا يَتَكَلَّمَنَّ إِلَّا بِخَيْرٍ» (سنن الترمذي: بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي الكَلَامِ فِي الطَّوَافِ نمبر: 960)
وجه : (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَالشَّاةُ جَائِزَةٌ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي مَوْضِعَيْنِ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: قَدِمْتُ مَكَّةَ وَأَنَا حَائِضٌ وَلَمْ أَطُفْ بِالْبَيْتِ وَلا بَيْنَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ قَالَتْ: فَشَكَوْتُ ذَلِكَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، قَالَ: «افْعَلِي كَمَا يَفْعَلُ الْحَاجُ غَيْرَ أَنْ لَا تَطُوفِي بِالْبَيْتِ حَتَّى تَطْهُرِي» (بخاري: بَابٌ : تَقْضِي الحَائِضُ المَنَاسِكَ كُلَّهَا إِلَّا الطَّوَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ: 1650)
وجه (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَالْبَدَنَةُ وَالْبَقَرَةُ يُجْزِئُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ \ عَنْ جَابِرٍ بْن عَبْدِ اللهِ. قَالَ: نَحَرْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَامَ الْخَدَيْنِيَةِ الْبَدَنَةَ عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ. وَالْبَقَرَةَ عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ (مسلم: بَاب الاشْتِرَاكِ فِي الْهَدْيِ، وَإِجْزَاءِ الْبَقَرَةِ وَالْبَدَنَةِ كُلّ مِنْهُمَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ، غبر: 1318)
Chapter of Hady. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him - Hady: its minimum is a sheep, and it is of three types: camels, cows, and sheep/goats. In all of that, only the thani and above is valid except for sheep, for the jadha' from it is valid. And it is not valid in Hady: one with cut ear, nor most of them (i.e., of the ear), nor one with cut tail, nor hand, nor foot, nor blind in one eye, nor emaciated, nor lame. ... And the sheep is valid in everything except in two cases: one who performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub, and one who has intercourse after standing at Arafat. And the camel and the cow, each one of them suffices for seven persons, when each of the partners intends worship; but if one of them intends meat with his share, it does not suffice for the remaining.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, expanded with Hadith proofs and Urdu commentary, covers the essential rulings of Hady (the sacrificial animal sent to the Haram for Hajj). The passage begins by stating the minimum Hady is a sheep, and it can be from three types: camel, cow, or sheep/goat. The age requirement: only animals that have reached the thani stage (i.e., second year for camels, second year for cows, first year for goats, but for sheep the jadha' – around six months to one year – is also acceptable due to ease). Then it lists defects that render the animal invalid: a cut ear or more than half of it, a cut tail, a missing limb, blindness, emaciation, or lameness. These defects are supported by multiple Hadith, including the famous narration from al-Bara' ibn 'Azib listing four defective animals. The text then adds two special rulings: a sheep is valid for all expiations and offerings except in two situations: (1) if someone performed Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of janabah (major impurity), and (2) if someone had intercourse after the Wuquf at Arafah. In these two cases, a sheep is not sufficient; a larger animal is needed. Then, a camel or cow can be shared among seven persons if all intend worship (qurbah); but if one partner intends only to obtain meat, the others' shares are invalid. This is based on the practice at Hudaybiyyah where the Prophet ﷺ allowed one camel for seven men. The Urdu commentary clarifies that 'hady' is an animal sent to the Haram for slaughter, and it has three types.

Key Terms
طَافَ لِلزَّيَارَةِ جُنُبًا (tāfa lil-ziyārati junuban): To perform Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of major impurity (janabah). This requires a penalty of a camel or cow.
جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةَ (jāma'a ba'da al-wuqūfi bi-'Arafah): To have sexual intercourse after standing at Arafat during Hajj. This also requires a camel or cow.
الْبَدَنَةُ (al-badanah): A camel (multiples: badan). It is one of the animals that can be shared among seven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if seven people share a cow for Hady and one of them intends only to eat the meat?
A) The cow is valid for all seven.
B) The cow is valid for the six who intend worship, but not for the one who intends meat.
C) The cow is invalid for all seven.
D) The cow is valid for all if they make an exception for that one person.

Key Takeaway
A sheep is sufficient for all Hady except after janabah Tawaf or Arafat intercourse; a camel/cow can be shared among seven only if all intend worship.

Sufficiency of a Sheep and Sharing of Camel/Cow in Hady
Ruling on sheep's sufficiency and sharing condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when a sheep is not sufficient for hady and explain the condition for valid sharing of a camel or cow.

Core Idea
A sheep suffices for hady except for a junub making tawaf or one who had intercourse after Arafah; camel/cow serves seven if all intend worship.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn lays down two key rulings in the chapter of hady (sacrificial animals during Hajj). First, a sheep is normally sufficient for any sacrifice, but there are two specific cases where it does not suffice. Second, a camel or cow can be shared by up to seven persons, but only if every partner intends the act of worship (qurbah) and not the meat. Understanding these exceptions and conditions is essential for correctly performing the hady obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two exceptions to sheep's sufficiency
Locate in the text the two cases where a sheep does not suffice: (1) one who performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub, and (2) one who has intercourse after standing at Arafah. In these cases, a larger animal (camel/cow) is required.
These exceptions are specific to hady and not general to all sacrifices.
2
Understand the sharing ruling for camel/cow
Note that a camel or cow can be shared by up to seven persons. The word 'yuʾjizu' indicates it suffices for all of them, meaning the obligation of hady is fulfilled for each partner.
The number seven is specific; Hanafis allow up to seven for camel and cow.
3
Recognize the condition of unanimous intent
The phrase 'idha kāna kullu wāḥidin min al-shurakā'i yurīdu al-qurbah' establishes that every partner must intend worship. If even one intends meat, the sacrifice is invalid for all.
Intention (niyyah) is a fundamental condition for the validity of acts of worship.
4
Consequence of violating the condition
The text states 'lam yajuz li-l-bāqīn' – the sacrifice is not permissible for the rest. This means the entire sacrifice becomes invalid, and all partners must repeat their hady.
This ruling emphasizes the communal nature of the act: one person's wrong intention spoils it for everyone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْهَدْيِ وَالشَّاةُ جَائِزَةٌ فِي كُلِّ شَيْءٍ إِلَّا فِي مَوْضِعَيْنِ مَنْ طَافَ لِلزَّيَارَةِ جُنُبًا وَمَنْ جَامَعَ بَعْدَ الْوُقُوفِ بِعَرَفَةَ وَالْبَدَنَةُ وَالْبَقَرَةُ يُجْزِئُ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ إِذَا كَانَ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْ الشُرَكَاءِ يُرِيدُ الْقُرْبَةَ وَإِنْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمْ يُرِيدُ بِنَصِيبِهِ اللَّحْمَ لَمْ يَجُزْ لِلْبَاقِينَ
Chapter of Hady (sacrificial animals). A sheep is permissible for everything except in two cases: one who performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub, and one who has intercourse after standing at Arafah. And a camel and a cow, each one of them is sufficient for seven, if each of the partners intends the act of worship. And if one of them intends meat by his share, it is not permissible for the rest.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn states a ruling in the chapter of Hady (sacrificial animals in Hajj). The first ruling: a sheep (shah) is valid for any sacrifice (hady, udhiyah, etc.) except in two specific situations: (1) a person who performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while in a state of janabah (major impurity) – for such a person, the sacrifice is not accepted and must be repeated, and (2) a person who has sexual intercourse after standing at Arafah but before completing the Hajj rituals – again, the sacrifice is not sufficient. In these two cases, a larger animal like a camel or cow is required. The second ruling: a camel or a cow can be shared by up to seven persons, meaning it suffices for all seven as a single sacrifice, provided that each partner intends solely the act of worship (qurbah) and not the meat. If any partner intends to obtain meat for consumption, the sacrifice becomes invalid for all partners.

Key Terms
الْهَدْي (al-hady): Sacrificial animal brought to the Haram during Hajj.
الْقُرْبَة (al-qurbah): Act of worship intended solely for Allah's pleasure.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A group of seven people want to share one cow as hady. One of them says he only wants the meat. What is the ruling?
A) The sacrifice is valid for all seven.
B) The sacrifice is valid only for those who intended qurbah.
C) The sacrifice is invalid for all seven.
D) The sacrifice is valid but that person must compensate.

Key Takeaway
A sheep suffices for hady except when the pilgrim is junub during tawaf al-ziyarah or had intercourse after Arafah; a camel or cow can be shared by seven provided all intend worship.

Five Defects That Invalidate a Sacrificial Animal
Hadith listing five disqualifying defects with definitions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five disqualifying defects for sacrificial animals and explain why each invalidates the sacrifice according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
A sacrificial animal must be free from severe physical defects — five specific defects render it invalid.

This lesson examines a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawood that the Prophet (ﷺ) forbade sacrificing animals with certain defects. The Hanafi school treats this prohibition as establishing that these defects make the animal unfit for sacrifice (udhiyah or hady). Understanding these defects is essential for ensuring the validity of one's sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Recall the hadith and its authority
Identify that this is a hadith from Sunan Abi Dawood. The verb 'nahā' (forbade) indicates a prohibition, which in the context of worship renders the act invalid.
The hadith is a had ahad (zanni al-thubut), but its meaning is clear and accepted by all schools.
2
List and define each defect
Go through each term: musfarrah (ear completely cut off), musta'salah (horn uprooted), bakhqa' (eye blinded), mushayya'ah (too weak to follow flock), kusara (broken bone). Note the severity required for each.
Minor cuts or cracks do not fall under these categories.
3
Understand the legal implication of the prohibition
The Prophet's prohibition (nahy) indicates that these defects make the sacrifice invalid. In Hanafi usul, nahy from the Prophet in matters of worship implies fasād (invalidity) unless there is evidence to the contrary.
Some schools consider the sacrifice valid but disliked; Hanafis rule it invalid.
4
Apply the rule to sacrificial animals
When selecting an animal for Udhiyah or Hady, ensure it has none of these five defects. If it does, the sacrifice is not accepted.
This applies to both obligatory and voluntary sacrifices.
5
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school rules that sacrificing such an animal is makruh tahrimi and the sacrifice is invalid. This is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
The cross-madhhab status is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon) in principle, though details may vary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نَهَى رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَن المُصْفَرَّةِ، وَالْمُسْتَأْصَلَةِ، وَالْبَحْقَاءِ وَالْمُشَيَّعَةِ، وَكِسَرَا، وَالْمُصْفَرَّةُ: الَّتِي تُسْتَأْصَلُ أُذُنُهَا حَتَّى يَبْدُوَ سَمَاخُهَا وَالْمُسْتَأْصَلَةُ: الَّتِي اسْتُؤْصِلَ قَرْنُهَا مِنْ أَصْلِهِ وَالْبَخْقَاءُ: الَّتي تُبْخَقُ عَيْنَهَا، وَالْمُشَيَّعَةُ: الَّتِي لَا تَتْبَعُ الْغَنَمَ عَجَفًا وَضَعْفًا، وَالْكَسْرَاءُ: الْكَسِيرَةُ
The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ) forbade (sacrificing) the musfarrah, musta'salah, bakhqa', mushayya'ah, and kusara. Al-musfarrah: whose ear is cut off until its ear canal appears. Al-musta'salah: whose horn is uprooted from its root. Al-bakhqa': whose eye is blinded. Al-mushayya'ah: which does not follow the sheep due to emaciation and weakness. Al-kusara': the broken one.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith from Abu Dawood listing specific defects that render an animal unfit for sacrifice (hady or udhiyah). The Hanafi school relies on this hadith and similar narrations to determine the minimum requirements for a valid sacrificial animal. The defects are: (1) musfarrah: an animal whose ear has been completely cut off to the point that the ear canal is visible; (2) musta'salah: an animal whose horn has been completely removed from the root; (3) bakhqa': an animal whose eye is blinded (either by a defect or injury); (4) mushayya'ah: an animal that is so weak and emaciated that it cannot keep up with the flock; (5) kusara: an animal with a broken limb or horn. These conditions make the animal defective to the extent that it does not meet the standard of perfection required for sacrifice. The Hanafi position is that such defects invalidate the sacrifice, and a sound animal is required. This is based on the general principle that the sacrifice should be of the best quality, as commanded in the Quran.

Key Terms
المُصْفَرَّة (al-musfarrah): An animal whose ear is cut off entirely so that the ear canal is exposed.
الْمُسْتَأْصَلَة (al-musta'salah): An animal whose horn is uprooted from the root.
الْبَخْقَاء (al-bakhqa'): An animal with a blinded eye.
الْمُشَيَّعَة (al-mushayya'ah): An animal too weak to follow the flock due to emaciation.
الْكَسْرَاء (al-kusara'): An animal with a broken bone (e.g., leg or horn).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a disqualifying defect according to the hadith?
A) An animal whose ear is completely cut off.
B) An animal with a broken horn at the tip.
C) An animal with a blinded eye.
D) An animal too weak to follow the flock.

Key Takeaway
An animal with any of the five severe defects (complete ear removal, uprooted horn, blinded eye, extreme weakness, broken bone) is invalid for sacrifice in the Hanafi school.

Rulings on Eating from Hady and Slaughter Requirements
Rulings on eating and slaughter of hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which types of hady may be consumed by the offerer and specify the time and place restrictions for slaughter.

Core Idea
Eating from hady is only permitted for voluntary, tamattu', and qiran sacrifices; all other hady meat must be given away, and slaughter must take place in the Haram.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn delineates clear distinctions among the types of hady (sacrificial animals) in Hajj. Understanding these rules is essential for performing Hajj correctly, as it determines whether you may consume the meat yourself or must donate it entirely, and when and where the sacrifice must occur.

Guided Path
1
Identify the categories of hady
List the three types from which eating is permitted: hady al-tatawwu' (voluntary), hady al-tamattu', and hady al-qiran. Note that other hady (e.g., penalty or vow) are not included.
Memorize these three as a group.
2
Distinguish eating permissibility
For the three types, eating is allowed (ja'iz). For all other hady, eating is prohibited (la yajuz). This includes hady for dam al-jinayat, nadhr, etc.
The prohibition is strict; the meat must be given as charity.
3
Note the slaughter time restriction
Hady al-tatawwu', al-tamattu', and al-qiran may only be slaughtered on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) and the days of tashriq (11th–13th). No other time is valid.
This is a condition for these types; other hady have no such time restriction.
4
Note the flexibility for other hady
All other hady (penalty, vow, etc.) can be slaughtered at any time, day or night, any day of the year.
This includes expiatory sacrifices for missed obligations.
5
Identify the universal place restriction
All hady, regardless of type, must be slaughtered within the Haram (the sacred precincts of Makkah). Slaughter outside invalidates the sacrifice.
This is a wajib condition for all hady.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ الأَكْلُ مِنْ هَدْيِ التَّطَوُّع وَالْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ وَلا يَجُوزُ الأَكْلُ مِنْ بَقِيَّةِ الْهُدَايَا وَلَا يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ هَدْيِ التَّطَوُّعِ وَالْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ إِلَّا يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ وَيَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ بَقِيَّةِ الْهُدَايَا أَيَّ وَقْتٍ شَاءَ وَلَا يَجُوزُ ذَبْحُ الْهُدَايَا إِلَّا فِي الْحَرَمِ
And it is permissible to eat from the hady of tatawwu' (voluntary), tamattu', and qiran. And it is not permissible to eat from the rest of the hadayas. And it is not permissible to slaughter the hady of tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran except on the Day of Nahr. And it is permissible to slaughter the rest of the hadayas at any time he wishes. And it is not permissible to slaughter the hadayas except in the Haram.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage from Al-Quduri's matn sets out clear distinctions among types of hady regarding eating and slaughter. Eating is allowed from three types: (1) hady tatawwu' (voluntary sacrifice), (2) hady tamattu' (the sacrifice of one performing tamattu' Hajj), and (3) hady qiran (the sacrifice of one performing qiran Hajj). Eating is not allowed from other hady, such as those for penalties (dam al-jinayat) or vows. Slaughter time: for tatawwu', tamattu', and qiran, slaughter is only valid on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) and the days of tashriq (11th-13th). For other types (e.g., penalty or vow), slaughter can be done at any time. Place: all hady must be slaughtered within the Haram (the sacred precincts of Makkah). This ruling reflects the Hanafi position that the meat of certain sacrifices is for the poor and cannot be consumed by the offerer, while voluntary and compensatory sacrifices (tamattu', qiran) can be eaten to celebrate the occasion.

Key Terms
هَدْيِ التَّطَوُّع (hady al-tatawwu'): Voluntary sacrifice not required by Hajj or penalty.
الْمُتْعَة (al-tamattu'): A type of Hajj where one performs Umrah first and then Hajj, requiring a sacrifice.
الْقِرَان (al-qiran): A type of Hajj where one combines Umrah and Hajj with one ihram, requiring a sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When can the hady of tamattu' be slaughtered?
A) Any time during Hajj.
B) Only on the Day of Nahr and days of tashriq.
C) Only after returning home.
D) Any time within the Haram.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the offerer to eat from hady al-tatawwu', al-tamattu', and al-qiran, but all hady must be slaughtered within the Haram, and the first three types must be slaughtered on the Day of Nahr or days of tashriq.
