6 min
Ruling on Eating from the Hady
States ruling on permissibility of eating from different types of hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on eating from different types of hady and identify the hadith proof that supports the distinction.

Core Idea
Eating from voluntary and tamattu'/qiran hady is permissible; obligatory hady is not.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on whether the pilgrim may eat from the meat of the sacrificial animals (hady) offered during Hajj. The matn of Al-Quduri makes a clear distinction based on the type of hady, and the author provides a hadith as proof. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling categories
Read the matn: 'It is permissible to eat from the hady of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran, and it is not permissible to eat from the rest of the hadaya.' Note the two categories: permissible and prohibited.
The 'rest of the hadaya' refers to obligatory hady such as those due for vows, penalties, or expiations.
2
Locate the hadith proof
The author cites a hadith from Abu Dawud where the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent a companion with eighteen sacrificial camels and instructed him not to eat from them. This shows that the prohibition to eat is specific to certain types, implying permission for others.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but sufficient for a ruling of permissibility.
3
Understand the istidlal
The wajh al-dalalah: The Prophet's instruction 'do not eat from them' was directed at a specific group of hady (the eighteen camels). The absence of a general prohibition for all hady indicates that the default is permissibility, and the prohibition is limited to obligatory hady.
This is a dalil al-khitab (implied meaning) that the ruling varies by type.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that eating from voluntary (tatawwu'), tamattu', and qiran hady is permissible (mubah). Eating from obligatory hady (vows, kaffarah, dam) is not permissible (haram). This is the mufta bihi position.
Other schools may differ; some allow eating from obligatory hady as well.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْهَدْيِ
وَيَجُوزُ الأَكْلُ مِنْ هَدْيِ التَّطَوُّعِ وَالْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ، وَلا يَجُوزُ الأَكْلُ مِنْ بَقِيَّةِ الْهُدَايَا.
وجه: (1) الحديث لثبوت وَيَجُوزُ الْأَكْلُ مِنْ هَدْيِ التَّطَوُّعِ وَالْمُتْعَةِ وَالْقِرَانِ
عَنْ مُوسَى بْنِ سَلَمَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، قَالَ: بَعَثَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم فَلَانَا الْأَسْلَمِيُّ، وَبَعَثَ مَعَهُ بِثَمَانِ عَشْرَةَ بَدَنَةً، فَقَالَ: أَرَأَيْتَ إِنْ أُزْحِفَ عَلَيَّ مِنْهَا شَيْءٌ قَالَ: «تَنْحَرُهَا، ثُمَّ تَصْبُغُ نَعْلَهَا فِي دَمِهَا، ثُمَّ اضْرِبُهَا عَلَى صَفْحَتِهَا، وَلَا تَأْكُلْ مِنْهَا أَنْتَ وَلَا أَحَدٌ مِنْ أَصْحَابِكَ - أَوْ قَالَ – مِنْ أَهْلِ رُفْقَتِكَ» (أبو داؤد: بَابٌ فِي الْهَدْيِ إِذَا عَطِبَ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَبْلُغَ، نمبر : 1763)
اصول : وہ ہری جو جنایت یا کسی دم کی وجہ سے ہو وہ کفارات ہیں اور انکا خو دیا احباب کو کھلانا درست نہیں۔
Chapter of Hady. It is permissible to eat from the hady of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran, and it is not permissible to eat from the rest of the hadaya. Proof (1) The hadith for establishing that it is permissible to eat from the hady of voluntary, tamattu', and qiran: From Musa bin Salamah, from Ibn Abbas, he said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) sent so-and-so al-Aslami, and sent with him eighteen sacrificial camels. He said: What do you think if some of them become incapacitated? He said: Slaughter them, then dye their sandals in their blood, then strike them on their humps, and do not eat from them yourself nor anyone from your companions or from the people of your company. (Abu Dawud) Principle: The hady that is due to a crime or any blood money are expiations, and it is not correct to feed their meat to friends.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the matn of Al-Quduri on the permissibility of eating from the meat of sacrificial animals (hady) offered during Hajj. The ruling distinguishes between types: one may eat from a voluntary (tatawwu') hady, or from the hady of tamattu' and qiran, but not from the rest of the hadaya, which include obligatory ones such as those due for vows, penalties, or violations (kaffarat). The proof cited is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) sent a companion with eighteen sacrificial camels and instructed him not to eat from them if they became incapacitated. This indicates that the prohibition to eat is limited to certain types, implying permission for others. The Urdu principle adds that hady due for jinayat or dam (kaffarat) are not to be eaten by the offerer or his friends. Thus, the ruling is that eating from voluntary and tamattu'/qiran hady is permissible (jaiz), while eating from obligatory hady is not permissible.

Key Terms
هدي التطوع (hady al-tatawwu'): A sacrificial animal offered voluntarily in Hajj, not due to a vow or obligation.
هدي المتعة (hady al-mut'ah): The sacrificial animal offered by a pilgrim performing tamattu' (combining Umrah and Hajj with a break).
هدي القران (hady al-qiran): The sacrificial animal offered by a pilgrim performing qiran (combining Umrah and Hajj without a break).
بقية الهدايا (baqiyyat al-hadaya): The rest of the sacrificial animals, i.e., obligatory ones like nadhr, dam, kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
From which type of hady is eating permissible in the Hanafi school?
A) Hady due to a vow (nadhr)
B) Hady of tamattu'
C) Hady of kaffarah for hunting
D) Hady for a missed obligation

Key Takeaway
Eating from voluntary, tamattu', and qiran hady is permissible; eating from obligatory hady is not.
